$\;m_T = 3\;$
$\;m_N = -\dfrac{1}{m_T} = -\dfrac{1}{3}\;$
26qperpendicularity condition
Apply the product rule (with chain rule on composite factors) to differentiate uv
$\;y = x(x+1)^3\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = (x+1)^3 + x \cdot 3(x+1)^2 = (x+1)^2(4x+1)\;$
17qproduct rule selection
Differentiate implicitly to obtain dy/dx without isolating y
$\;x^2 + xy + y^2 = 7\;$
$\;2x + y + x\dfrac{dy}{dx} + 2y\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{-(2x+y)}{x+2y}\;$
14qimplicit differentiation
Collect and factor the unknown to isolate it from a linear equation
$\;3u - a = 5 + u\;$
$\;u(3 - 1) = 5 + a \Rightarrow u = \dfrac{5 + a}{2}\;$
13qlinear isolation
Differentiate implicitly when y cannot be cleanly isolated
$\;x^2 + xy + y^2 = 7\;$
$\;2x + y + x\dfrac{dy}{dx} + 2y\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{-(2x+y)}{x+2y}\;$

12qline equation construction
Row-reduce (A − λI) to extract eigenvectors from the null space
$\;A - 3I = \begin{pmatrix} -1 & 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 1 & -1 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\xrightarrow{R_3} \begin{pmatrix} -1 & 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 1 & -1 \\ 0 & 0 & 0 \end{pmatrix},\ z=t:\, y=t,\, x=t \Rightarrow \mathbf{e} = \begin{pmatrix}1\\1\\1\end{pmatrix}\;$
11qnull space extraction
Rewrite roots, reciprocals, and surds as fractional/negative index powers before differentiating
$\;y = \sqrt{x} + \dfrac{1}{x}\;$
$\;y = x^{1/2} + x^{-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \tfrac{1}{2}x^{-1/2} - x^{-2}\;$
10qindex law rewrite
Substitute to bridge a disguised quadratic into standard form
$\;4^x - 3 \cdot 2^x + 2 = 0\;$
$\;u = 2^x:\quad u^2 - 3u + 2 = 0 \Rightarrow (u-1)(u-2) = 0\;$
9qsubstitution bridge
Factorise non-monic quadratic by the ac-method (split middle term and group)
$\;2x^2 + 5x + 3\;$
$\;2x^2 + 2x + 3x + 3 = 2x(x+1) + 3(x+1) = (2x+3)(x+1)\;$
9qstrategic factorisation
Cross two in-plane (or direction) vectors to obtain a perpendicular normal
$\;\mathbf{u} = \begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\2\end{pmatrix},\quad \mathbf{v} = \begin{pmatrix}0\\1\\1\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\mathbf{n} = \mathbf{u} \times \mathbf{v} = \begin{vmatrix}\mathbf{i}&\mathbf{j}&\mathbf{k}\\1&0&2\\0&1&1\end{vmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix}-2\\-1\\1\end{pmatrix}\;$
9qcross product normal
Factor out the leading coefficient from x² and x terms to enable completing the square
$\;3x^2 + 12x + 5\;$
$\;3(x^2 + 4x) + 5 = 3(x+2)^2 - 12 + 5 = 3(x+2)^2 - 7\;$
8qcompleting the square
Multiply by the conjugate surd to rationalise a binomial denominator
$\;\dfrac{1}{2+\sqrt{3}}\;$
$\;\dfrac{1}{2+\sqrt{3}}\cdot\dfrac{2-\sqrt{3}}{2-\sqrt{3}} = \dfrac{2-\sqrt{3}}{4-3} = 2-\sqrt{3}\;$
8qrationalisation
Multiply through by the LCD to clear denominators and form a polynomial equation
$\;\dfrac{3}{x} + 5 = 2x\;$
$\;3 + 5x = 2x^2 \Rightarrow 2x^2 - 5x - 3 = 0\;$
8qclearing fractions
Apply Pythagorean identity cos²x = 1 − sin²x to create self-referencing reduction recurrence
$\;I_n = (n-1)\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-2}x\,\cos^2 x\,dx\;$
$\;I_n = (n-1)\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-2}x\,(1-\sin^2 x)\,dx = (n-1)\,I_{n-2} - (n-1)\,I_n \Rightarrow I_n = \dfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2}\;$

8qconjugate deflation
Collect, factor, and divide to isolate dy/dx as a linear unknown

7qlinear isolation

7qquadratic formula
Collect the self-referencing integral on one side and solve linearly to close the reduction formula

$\;2^5\!\left(1 + \tfrac{x}{2}\right)^{\!5} = 32\!\left(1 + \tfrac{x}{2}\right)^{\!5}\;$
4qtemplate matching
Translate |y|<1 convergence condition into validity range for x
$\;(1+3x)^{-2}\;$
$\;|3x|<1 \Rightarrow |x|<\tfrac{1}{3}\;$
4qconvergence condition
Equate expansion's base to target value to find substitution x
$\;(1+2x)^4 \approx 1 + 8x + 24x^2 + 32x^3,\quad \text{find } 1.02^4\;$
$\;1+2x=1.02 \Rightarrow x=0.01;\quad 1+8(0.01)+24(0.0001)+32(0.000001)=1.08243\;$

4qvalidity verification
Differentiate x with respect to y then reciprocate to obtain dy/dx
$\;x = \sin y\;$
$\;\dfrac{dx}{dy} = \cos y \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{1}{\cos y} = \sec y\;$
4qreciprocal derivative
Expand product of polynomial factors before applying the power rule term-by-term
$\;y = (x-1)(x+2)^2\;$
$\;y = x^3 + 3x^2 - 4 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 + 6x\;$
4qexpand then differentiate
Apply Newton-Raphson iteration via x_{n+1} = x_n − f(x_n)/f'(x_n) to refine a root estimate
$\;f(x) = x^2 - 3,\quad f'(x) = 2x,\quad x_0 = 2\;$
$\;x_1 = 2 - \dfrac{2^2 - 3}{2(2)} = 2 - \dfrac{1}{4} = 1.75\;$
4qnewton raphson iteration
Rewrite into sum-of-simple-terms form before differentiating
$\;y = \dfrac{x^2 + 1}{x}\;$
$\;y = x + x^{-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 1 - x^{-2}\;$
4qpre differentiation simplification

4qreciprocal derivative conversion
Choose u as the polynomial factor in IBP to reduce its degree
$\;\int x\,e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;u=x,\ dv=e^{x}dx \Rightarrow x\,e^{x} - \int e^{x}\,dx = (x-1)\,e^{x}+C\;$
4qintegration by parts
Select the correct arc length or surface area integral formula to frame the problem
$\;y = x^{3/2},\quad 0 \le x \le 1\;$
$\;L = \int_0^1 \sqrt{1 + \left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2}\,dx = \int_0^1 \sqrt{1 + \tfrac{9}{4}x}\,dx\;$
4qformula selection
Apply trapezium rule to tabulated ordinates to estimate a definite integral
$\;\int_{0}^{2} f(x)\,dx,\quad h=1,\quad y_0=1,\; y_1=3,\; y_2=5\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{2}\bigl[(1+5)+2(3)\bigr] = \tfrac{1}{2}(12) = 6\;$
4qnumerical integration
Integrate upper-minus-lower between intersection limits to find enclosed area
$\;y = 4 - x^2,\quad y = x^2,\quad x \in [-1,\,1]\;$
$\;A = \int_{-1}^{1}\bigl[(4-x^2)-x^2\bigr]\,dx = \int_{-1}^{1}(4-2x^2)\,dx = \left[4x-\tfrac{2x^3}{3}\right]_{-1}^{1} = \dfrac{20}{3}\;$
4qarea between curves
Convert integration limits to the new variable to avoid back-substitution
$\;\int_0^1 2x(x^2+1)^2\,dx,\quad u=x^2+1\;$
$\;x=0\Rightarrow u=1,\; x=1\Rightarrow u=2:\quad \int_1^2 u^2\,du = \left[\tfrac{u^3}{3}\right]_1^2 = \tfrac{7}{3}\;$
4qlimit conversion
Apply power-reduction or Pythagorean identity to linearise squared trig/hyperbolic terms
$\;\int \cos^2 x\, dx\;$
$\;\int \tfrac{1}{2}(1+\cos 2x)\, dx = \tfrac{x}{2} + \tfrac{\sin 2x}{4} + C\;$
4qidentity selection
Cascade reduction formula down to a known base case to extract a numerical value
$\;I_n = nI_{n-1} - e^{-1},\quad I_0 = 1 - e^{-1}\;$
$\;I_1 = 1 - 2e^{-1},\quad I_2 = 2(1-2e^{-1}) - e^{-1} = 2 - 5e^{-1}\;$
4qrecursive descent
Split a trig power as f^(n-1)·f (or f^(n-2)·f²) to set up a clean reduction-formula IBP
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\,dx\;$
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-1}x \cdot \sin x\,dx,\quad u = \sin^{n-1}x,\ dv = \sin x\,dx \Rightarrow I_n = (n-1)\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-2}x\,\cos^2 x\,dx\;$

4qboundary exact evaluation
Convert complex number to modulus-argument polar form to enable de Moivre or geometric reasoning
$\;z = 1 + i\;$
$\;|z| = \sqrt{2},\quad \theta = \dfrac{\pi}{4} \Rightarrow z = \sqrt{2}\, e^{i\pi/4}\;$
4qpolar conversion
Convert to polar form and apply de Moivre's theorem with +2kπ offsets to enumerate all n distinct nth roots
$\;z^3 = 8\;$

4qde moivre root extraction
Apply point-gradient form then rearrange to required line-equation format

$\;y - 2 = 3(x - 1) \Rightarrow y = 3x - 1\;$
4qline equation construction
Eliminate the parameter to obtain a Cartesian equation
$\;x = t^2,\quad y = 2t\;$
$\;t = \dfrac{y}{2} \Rightarrow x = \left(\dfrac{y}{2}\right)^2 = \dfrac{y^2}{4}\;$
4qparametric elimination
Substitute coordinates of a known point into a curve/line equation to solve for the unknown parameter
$\;y = 3x + c,\quad (1,\,5) \text{ on the line}\;$
$\;5 = 3(1) + c \Rightarrow c = 2\;$
4qpoint on line substitution
Substitute zero for one coordinate to find an axis intersection
$\;y = 2x + 6\;$
$\;y = 0 \Rightarrow 2x + 6 = 0 \Rightarrow x = -3,\quad (-3,\,0)\;$
4qaxis intersection
Decompose composite circular region into sectors and triangles to compute area
$\;\text{Sector } OAB:\ r=4,\ \angle AOB=\tfrac{\pi}{3};\ \triangle OBC:\ OB=4,\ OC=5,\ \angle BOC=\tfrac{\pi}{6}\;$
$\;A = \tfrac{1}{2}(4^2)\!\left(\tfrac{\pi}{3}\right) + \tfrac{1}{2}(4)(5)\sin\tfrac{\pi}{6} = \dfrac{8\pi}{3} + 5\;$
4qarea decomposition
Set x=0 and y=0 in tangent/normal equation to extract axis intercepts
$\;\dfrac{x\cos\theta}{3} + \dfrac{y\sin\theta}{2} = 1\;$
$\;y=0 \Rightarrow x=3\sec\theta;\quad x=0 \Rightarrow y=2\csc\theta\;$

Decompose a composite figure into elementary sub-shapes to compute length or area
$\;\text{Vertices } (0,0),\,(3,0),\,(3,2),\,(0,4)\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{2}(3)(4+2) = 9 \quad\text{or}\quad \underbrace{3\times2}_{\text{rect}} + \underbrace{\tfrac{1}{2}\times3\times2}_{\triangle} = 9\;$
4qgeometric decomposition
 review

4qstandard conic normal derivation
Form characteristic equation det(A − λI) = 0 to find eigenvalues
$\;A = \begin{pmatrix} 3 & 1 \\ 0 & 2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\det(A - \lambda I) = (3-\lambda)(2-\lambda) = 0 \Rightarrow \lambda = 2,\,3\;$
4qcharacteristic equation
Construct integrating factor μ = e^{∫P dx} and multiply through to collapse LHS into d/dx[μy]
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} + \dfrac{2}{x}\,y = x\;$
$\;\mu = e^{\int 2/x\, dx} = x^{2},\quad \dfrac{d}{dx}\bigl[x^{2}\,y\bigr] = x^{3}\;$
4qintegrating factor method
Form auxiliary equation to convert constant-coefficient ODE into algebra
$\;y'' + 5y' + 6y = 0\;$
$\;m^2 + 5m + 6 = 0 \Rightarrow (m+2)(m+3)=0 \Rightarrow y = Ae^{-2x} + Be^{-3x}\;$
4qauxiliary equation method
Classify auxiliary equation roots to select the correct CF template

$\;\Delta = 16-52 = -36<0,\; m = 2\pm 3i \Rightarrow y = e^{2x}(A\cos 3x + B\sin 3x)\;$
4qroot classification
Substitute boundary condition into general solution to determine the constant of integration
$\;y = x^2 + C,\quad y(1) = 5\;$
$\;5 = 1 + C \Rightarrow C = 4 \Rightarrow y = x^2 + 4\;$
4qinitial condition substitution

4qparametric tangent condition

4qparameter elimination

4qidentity selection

4qidentity selection

4qsubstitution bridge
Resolve SSA ambiguous case by selecting 180°−arcsin when obtuse angle required
$\;\sin C = 0.6,\quad C \text{ obtuse}\;$
$\;\alpha = \arcsin(0.6) \approx 36.9^\circ \Rightarrow C = 180^\circ - 36.9^\circ = 143.1^\circ\;$
4qambiguous case resolution
Divide the two coefficient equations to isolate tan α and recover the auxiliary angle
$\;R\cos\alpha = 3,\quad R\sin\alpha = 4\;$
$\;\frac{R\sin\alpha}{R\cos\alpha} = \frac{4}{3} \Rightarrow \tan\alpha = \frac{4}{3} \Rightarrow \alpha = \arctan\!\tfrac{4}{3}\;$
4qratio elimination
Eliminate trig parameter using Pythagorean or double-angle identity bridge
$\;x = 2\sin^2\theta,\quad y = \cos 2\theta\;$
$\;\sin^2\theta = \tfrac{x}{2},\quad \cos 2\theta = 1 - 2\sin^2\theta \Rightarrow y = 1 - x\;$
4qparametric elimination
Equate parametric position vectors componentwise to test 3D line intersection
$\;l_1: \mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\0\end{pmatrix}+\lambda\begin{pmatrix}1\\2\\1\end{pmatrix},\quad l_2: \mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}0\\1\\1\end{pmatrix}+\mu\begin{pmatrix}2\\1\\0\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\text{(i)}\ 1+\lambda=2\mu,\quad \text{(ii)}\ 2\lambda=1+\mu \Rightarrow \lambda=1,\,\mu=1;\quad \text{(iii)}\ 0+1=1+0\ \checkmark \Rightarrow \text{intersection at } (2,2,1)\;$
4qparametric intersection test
Use sine formula directly to obtain the line-plane angle
$\;\mathbf{d} = (1,\,0,\,2),\quad \mathbf{n} = (0,\,0,\,1)\;$
$\;\sin\alpha = \dfrac{|\mathbf{d}\cdot\mathbf{n}|}{|\mathbf{d}|\,|\mathbf{n}|} = \dfrac{2}{\sqrt{5}} \Rightarrow \alpha = \arcsin\!\dfrac{2}{\sqrt{5}}\;$

3qrationalisation

3qfraction clearing
Verify candidate roots against original-equation domain to discard extraneous solutions
$\;\sqrt{x+3} = x-1 \Rightarrow x+3 = x^2 -2x+1 \Rightarrow x \in \{-1,\, 4\}\;$
$\;x=-1:\; x-1=-2<0\ (\text{reject});\quad x=4:\; x-1=3\ge0\ \Rightarrow x=4\;$
3qdomain validation
Impose discriminant strictly less than zero to enforce no real intersections
$\;x^2 - kx + 2 = 0\;$

3qdiscriminant condition
Set discriminant to zero to enforce tangency / single-intersection
$\;x^2 = 2x + c \Rightarrow x^2 - 2x - c = 0\;$
$\;(-2)^2 - 4(1)(-c) = 0 \Rightarrow 4 + 4c = 0 \Rightarrow c = -1\;$
3qdiscriminant condition
Rewrite symmetric functions of roots via elementary symmetric polynomials to use Vieta's outputs
$\;x^2 - 5x + 3 = 0,\quad \alpha+\beta=5,\; \alpha\beta=3\;$
$\;\alpha^2+\beta^2 = (\alpha+\beta)^2 - 2\alpha\beta = 25 - 6 = 19\;$
3qidentity selection

3qparameter determination

3qcoefficient comparison

3qknown root factorisation
Recognise 1 + (dy/dx)² as a perfect square to collapse the arc-length radical

3qperfect square recognition

3qproduct rule selection

3qparametric differentiation

Differentiate term-by-term using the power rule on a sum of ax^n terms
$\;y = 3x^4 - 5x^2 + 2x - 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 12x^3 - 10x + 2\;$
3qpower rule differentiation
Differentiate curve and substitute x-coordinate to obtain tangent gradient
$\;y = x^3 - 3x,\quad P(1,\,-2)\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 - 3,\quad m = 3(1)^2 - 3 = 0\;$
3qderivative as gradient
Discard the exponential factor since e^{f(x)} > 0 to reduce to an algebraic equation
$\;e^{2x}(3x - 6) = 0\;$
$\;e^{2x} > 0 \Rightarrow 3x - 6 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2\;$
3qexponential never zero
Equate derivative to given gradient to form solvable equation
$\;f(x) = x^2 + kx,\quad f'(2) = 7\;$
$\;f'(x) = 2x + k \Rightarrow 4 + k = 7 \Rightarrow k = 3\;$
3qgradient equation
Substitute the given point into dy/dx to obtain the tangent gradient
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{2x + y}{x - 2y},\quad P(1,1)\;$
$\;m = \dfrac{2(1) + 1}{1 - 2(1)} = \dfrac{3}{-1} = -3\;$
3qevaluate at point
Set numerator of dy/dx fraction to zero to locate stationary points
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{x^2 - 4}{x^2 + 1}\;$
$\;x^2 - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow x = \pm 2\;$
3qfraction zero condition
Decompose proper rational integrand via partial fractions to reduce to log/power integrals
$\;\int \dfrac{3}{x(x+1)}\,dx\;$
$\;\dfrac{3}{x(x+1)} = \dfrac{3}{x} - \dfrac{3}{x+1} \Rightarrow 3\ln|x| - 3\ln|x+1| + C\;$
3qpartial fractions then integrate
Recognise f'(x)/f(x) pattern to integrate as ln|f(x)|
$\;\int \dfrac{2x}{x^2+1}\,dx\;$
$\;f(x)=x^2+1,\; f'(x)=2x \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{f'(x)}{f(x)}\,dx = \ln|x^2+1|+C\;$
3qlogarithmic recognition
Split a rational fraction term-by-term into standard integrable pieces
$\;\int \frac{u-1}{u^2}\,du\;$
$\;\int \left(\frac{1}{u} - u^{-2}\right)du = \ln|u| + \frac{1}{u} + C\;$
3qalgebraic decomposition
Split integrand by linearity to reuse a known integral
$\;\int_{1}^{3}\!\frac{7}{x}\,dx,\quad\text{given }\int_{1}^{3}\!\frac{6}{x}\,dx\approx6.59\;$
$\;\int_{1}^{3}\!\frac{7}{x}\,dx = \int_{1}^{3}\!\frac{6}{x}\,dx + \int_{1}^{3}\!\frac{1}{x}\,dx = 6.59 + \ln 3\;$
3qlinearity decomposition
Substitute u = ax+b to linearise composite integrand
$\;\int (3x+1)^4\,dx\;$
$\;u=3x+1,\; dx=\tfrac{du}{3} \Rightarrow \tfrac{1}{3}\cdot\tfrac{u^5}{5}+C = \tfrac{(3x+1)^5}{15}+C\;$
3qlinear substitution
Simplify the integrand algebraically before integrating to reduce term count and complexity
$\;\int \dfrac{x^3 + x^2}{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\int (x^2 + x)\,dx = \dfrac{x^3}{3} + \dfrac{x^2}{2} + C\;$
3qpre integration simplification
Evaluate IBP boundary brackets at engineered limits to kill or simplify them
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\, dx \Rightarrow \bigl[-\sin^{n-1}x\,\cos x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2}\;$
$\;x=\tfrac{\pi}{2}:\cos\tfrac{\pi}{2}=0;\quad x=0:\sin^{n-1}0=0 \Rightarrow \bigl[-\sin^{n-1}x\,\cos x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2}=0\;$
3qboundary evaluation
Anchor the recursion by evaluating the lowest-index integral directly
$\;I_n = nI_{n-1},\quad I_0 = \int_0^1 e^{-x}\,dx\;$
$\;I_0 = \bigl[-e^{-x}\bigr]_0^1 = 1 - e^{-1} \Rightarrow I_2 = 2I_1 = 2(1\cdot I_0) = 2(1 - e^{-1})\;$
3qbase case evaluation
Collapse 1+(dy/dx)² into a perfect square to kill the arc-length radical
$\;y = \dfrac{x^2}{2} + \dfrac{1}{2x},\quad \dfrac{dy}{dx} = x - \dfrac{1}{2x^2}\;$
$\;1+\left(x - \tfrac{1}{2x^2}\right)^2 = 1 + x^2 - 1 + \tfrac{1}{4x^4} = x^2 + \tfrac{1}{4x^4} = \left(x + \tfrac{1}{2x^2}\right)^2\;$
3qarc length simplification
Substitute known point into antiderivative to determine constant of integration
$\;f(x) = x^2 + 3x + c,\quad f(1) = 7\;$
$\;1 + 3 + c = 7 \Rightarrow c = 3\;$
3qinitial condition substitution
Unroll reduction formula iteratively to a base case
$\;I_n = \dfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2},\quad I_0 = \dfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
$\;I_4 = \dfrac{3}{4}\,I_2 = \dfrac{3}{4}\cdot\dfrac{1}{2}\,I_0 = \dfrac{3}{4}\cdot\dfrac{1}{2}\cdot\dfrac{\pi}{2} = \dfrac{3\pi}{16}\;$
3qreduction descent
Match integrand to a formula-booklet standard form for direct antidifferentiation
$\;\int_0^1 \dfrac{1}{1+x^2}\,dx\;$
$\;\bigl[\arctan x\bigr]_0^1 = \arctan 1 - \arctan 0 = \dfrac{\pi}{4}\;$
3qstandard form recognition
Keep IBP role assignment consistent across repeated applications to close the loop
$\;I = \int e^{x}\sin x\,dx\;$
$\;I = e^{x}\sin x - e^{x}\cos x - I \Rightarrow I = \dfrac{e^{x}(\sin x - \cos x)}{2} + C\;$
3qibp assignment consistency
Apply power-reduction identities to linearise trig powers for integration
$\;\int \cos^2 x\,dx\;$
$\;\int \tfrac{1+\cos 2x}{2}\,dx = \tfrac{x}{2} + \tfrac{\sin 2x}{4} + C\;$
3qpower reduction linearisation

3qlog decomposition for reuse

3qparametric volume setup
Interpret nth roots of a complex number as vertices of a regular n-gon
$\;z^4 = 16\;$
$\;R = 16^{1/4} = 2,\quad \text{args } \tfrac{2k\pi}{4},\ k=0,\dots,3 \Rightarrow \text{square on } |z|=2,\quad A = \tfrac{4}{2}\cdot 4 \cdot \sin\tfrac{\pi}{2} = 8\;$
3qgeometric interpretation
Apply de Moivre's theorem with 2kπ offsets to extract all n distinct nth roots
$\;z^3 = 8i = 8\,\mathrm{cis}\!\left(\tfrac{\pi}{2} + 2k\pi\right)\;$
$\;z_k = 2\,\mathrm{cis}\!\left(\tfrac{\pi/2 + 2k\pi}{3}\right),\quad k=0,1,2 \Rightarrow \arg z = \tfrac{\pi}{6},\; \tfrac{5\pi}{6},\; -\tfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
3qde moivre root extraction
 review
Complete the square in w-plane coordinates to extract circle centre and radius from transformed locus equation
3qlocus identification
Classify standard complex locus equations as circle, perpendicular bisector, or half-line
$\;|z - 2i| = 3,\quad |z - 1| = |z - 3|,\quad \arg(z - 1) = \tfrac{\pi}{4}\;$
$\;\text{circle centre }(0,2)\ r=3;\quad \text{perp.\ bisector } x=2;\quad \text{half-line from }(1,0),\ \theta=\tfrac{\pi}{4}\;$
3qlocus recognition
Eliminate the parameter θ via the Pythagorean identity to obtain a Cartesian locus
$\;x = 3\cos\theta,\quad y = 2\sin\theta\;$
$\;\cos^2\theta + \sin^2\theta = 1 \Rightarrow \dfrac{x^2}{9} + \dfrac{y^2}{4} = 1\;$
3qparametric elimination
Translate a shaded bounded region into a system of inequalities from its boundary curves
$\;R\text{: above } y = x^2,\text{ below } y = x + 2,\text{ between intersections } x = -1,\; x = 2\;$
$\;R:\; y \geq x^2,\; y \leq x+2,\; -1 \leq x \leq 2\;$
3qregion inequality assignment
Translate region's position relative to each boundary into directed inequalities
$\;R \text{ bounded by } y = x,\; y = 0,\; x = 2;\; \text{test point } (1,\tfrac{1}{2})\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{2} \le 1,\; \tfrac{1}{2} \ge 0,\; 1 \le 2 \;\Rightarrow\; y \le x,\; y \ge 0,\; x \le 2\;$
3qregion inequality assignment
Equate y-expressions to reduce intersection to a single equation in x
$\;y = x^2,\quad y = 2x + 3\;$
$\;x^2 = 2x + 3 \Rightarrow x^2 - 2x - 3 = 0\;$
3qelimination by equating
Back-substitute into the simpler/parameter-free equation to find the missing coordinate
$\;y = 2x + 1,\quad x = 3\;$
$\;y = 2(3) + 1 = 7 \Rightarrow (3,\,7)\;$
3qback substitution choice
Parametrise point on conic to collapse two unknowns to one
$\;y^2 = 8x,\quad P\text{ on curve}\;$
$\;P = (2t^2,\,4t) \Rightarrow (4t)^2 = 16t^2 = 8(2t^2)\ \checkmark\;$
3qparametric representation
Apply tangent-radius perpendicularity via negative-reciprocal gradient
$\;C(0,0),\; P(3,4)\;$
$\;m_{CP} = \tfrac{4}{3} \Rightarrow m_T = -\tfrac{3}{4},\; y - 4 = -\tfrac{3}{4}(x - 3)\;$
3qperpendicular gradient
Clear fractions by multiplying through to reach required standard form
$\;y - 1 = -\tfrac{3}{2}(x - 4)\;$
$\;2y - 2 = -3x + 12 \Rightarrow 3x + 2y - 14 = 0\;$
3qform conversion
Translate geometric position conditions into algebraic equations by substitution
$\;y = x^2 - 4x + 3,\quad y = 0\;$
$\;x^2 - 4x + 3 = 0 \Rightarrow (x-1)(x-3) = 0\;$
3qgeometric to algebraic
Quote standard conic results directly to bypass derivation
$\;\frac{x^2}{9}+\frac{y^2}{4}=1,\quad P=(3\cos\theta,\,2\sin\theta)\;$
$\;\text{Tangent: } \frac{x\cos\theta}{3}+\frac{y\sin\theta}{2}=1\;$
3qstandard result recall

Eliminate parameter by expressing cosθ and sinθ from two locus coordinates then applying cos²+sin²=1
3qlocus elimination
Diagonalise A = PDP⁻¹ to reduce matrix powers to scalar powers
$\;A = PDP^{-1},\quad D = \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;A^n = P D^n P^{-1} = P \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 2^n \end{pmatrix} P^{-1}\;$
3qdiagonalisation
Apply the adjugate-over-determinant formula to invert a parametric 3×3 matrix
$\;M = \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & k & 1 \\ 0 & 2 & 3 \end{pmatrix},\quad \det M = 3k-2\;$
$\;M^{-1} = \dfrac{1}{3k-2}\begin{pmatrix} 3k-2 & 0 & 0 \\ 0 & 3 & -1 \\ 0 & -2 & k \end{pmatrix},\quad k \neq \tfrac{2}{3}\;$
3qadjugate inverse
Form integrating factor μ = e^{∫P(x)dx} to collapse LHS into exact derivative
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} + \dfrac{2}{x}\,y = x^3\;$
$\;\mu = e^{\int 2/x\,dx} = e^{2\ln x} = x^2\;$
3qintegrating factor method
Apply integrating factor e^{∫P(x)dx} to solve first-order linear ODE
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} + 3y = e^{-x}\;$
$\;\mu = e^{3x},\quad \dfrac{d}{dx}\!\left[e^{3x}y\right] = e^{2x} \Rightarrow e^{3x}y = \tfrac{1}{2}e^{2x} + C\;$
3qintegrating factor method
Divide through by the coefficient of dy/dx to reach standard linear form
$\;x\dfrac{dy}{dx} + 2y = x^3\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} + \dfrac{2}{x}\,y = x^2\;$
3qstandard form reduction
Decompose linear ODE solution as CF plus PI via superposition
$\;y'' + 3y' + 2y = e^{x}\;$
$\;y = \underbrace{Ae^{-x} + Be^{-2x}}_{y_{CF}} + \underbrace{\tfrac{1}{6}e^{x}}_{y_{PI}}\;$
3qsuperposition principle
Equate coefficients of linearly independent basis functions to solve for PI constants
$\;y'' + y' = 3x \quad \Rightarrow \quad y_p = ax + b,\; y_p' = a,\; y_p'' = 0\;$
$\;a = 3,\; b = 0 \quad \Leftarrow \quad (0) + (a) = 0\cdot x + 3x \Rightarrow a = 3,\; y_p = 3x\;$
3qcoefficient comparison
Reverse the substitution to express the solution in original variables
$\;v = 1 + Ce^{-x},\quad v = y^{-1}\;$
$\;y = \dfrac{1}{v} = \dfrac{1}{1 + Ce^{-x}}\;$
3qsubstitution reversal

3qrate balance formulation
Exploit reflection symmetry to halve the polar area integration range
$\;A = \tfrac{1}{2}\int_{0}^{2\pi} a^2(1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta,\quad r(-\theta)=r(\theta)\;$
$\;A = 2 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}\int_{0}^{\pi} a^2(1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta = a^2\int_{0}^{\pi}(1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta = \tfrac{3\pi a^2}{2}\;$
3qsymmetry exploitation
Exploit polar-curve symmetry to halve (or fraction) the integration range
$\;A = \tfrac{1}{2}\int_{0}^{2\pi} (1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta\;$
$\;r(-\theta)=r(\theta) \Rightarrow A = 2 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}\int_{0}^{\pi}(1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta\;$
3qsymmetry reduction

3qtangent analysis
Close induction with a complete formal conclusion to secure the final A-mark
$\;\text{Base case }(n=1)\checkmark,\quad \text{Inductive step }(n=k \Rightarrow n=k+1)\checkmark\;$
$\;\text{True for }n=1;\; n=k \Rightarrow n=k+1;\; \therefore \text{ true for all } n\in\mathbb{Z}^{+} \text{ by induction.}\;$
3qinduction conclusion
Extract the target divisor as an explicit factor to close a divisibility/parity proof
$\;6n + 4,\quad n \in \mathbb{Z}\;$
$\;6n + 4 = 2(3n + 2) = 2k,\quad k = 3n+2 \in \mathbb{Z} \Rightarrow 2 \mid (6n+4)\;$
3qfactor extraction
Choose AP sum formula matching the known triple of variables
$\;a = 3,\; l = 7,\; n = 5\;$
$\;S_5 = \dfrac{5}{2}(3 + 7) = 25\;$
3qformula selection
Multiply truncated standard series term-by-term to expand a product
$\;e^x \sin x \text{ to } x^3:\quad (1+x+\tfrac{x^2}{2}+\tfrac{x^3}{6})(x-\tfrac{x^3}{6})\;$
$\;0 + 1\cdot x + x\cdot x + \bigl(\tfrac{x^2}{2}\cdot x + 1\cdot(-\tfrac{x^3}{6})\bigr) = x + x^2 + \tfrac{x^3}{3}\;$
3qseries multiplication
Encode AP/GP conditions as simultaneous equations to extract a and d (or r)
$\;u_3 = 8,\quad u_7 = 20\;$
$\;(a+6d)-(a+2d)=20-8 \Rightarrow d=3,\; a=2\;$
3qparameter extraction
Select the expansion point (Taylor vs Maclaurin) to match the question
$\;e^x \text{ about } x=1,\text{ order 2}\;$
$\;e^x = e + e(x-1) + \dfrac{e}{2}(x-1)^2\;$
3qexpansion point selection
Verify |r| < 1 to validate or filter geometric sum-to-infinity solutions
$\;5r^2 - r - 6 = 0 \Rightarrow r = \tfrac{6}{5} \text{ or } r = -\tfrac{1}{5}\;$
$\;\left|\tfrac{6}{5}\right| > 1\ (\text{reject}),\quad \left|-\tfrac{1}{5}\right| < 1\ (\text{accept}) \Rightarrow r = -\tfrac{1}{5}\;$
3qvalidity check
Iterate recurrence with full precision (or set u_{n+1}=u_n=L) to find fixed-point limit
$\;u_{n+1} = \sqrt{2u_n + 3},\quad u_1 = 1\;$
$\;u_{n+1}=u_n=L:\quad L = \sqrt{2L+3} \Rightarrow L^2 - 2L - 3 = 0 \Rightarrow L = 3\;$
3qfixed point iteration

3qlinked AP GP reduction

3qidentity selection
Select a trig identity that bridges current form to target form
$\;6\sin x\cos x\;$
$\;6 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}\sin 2x = 3\sin 2x\;$
3qidentity selection
Substitute a parameter into part (a)'s proven identity to bridge to part (b)

3qsubstitution bridge

3qr formula
Reject trig roots outside [−1, 1] to filter valid quadratic solutions

3qdomain filtering
Use reference angle and CAST quadrants to enumerate all trig solutions

3qpythagorean reduction

3qperiod extraction

3qsolution counting

3qperpendicular foot via dot product
Substitute u = base^d to bridge fractional-power equation onto an already-solved polynomial
$\;x^3 - 5x^2 + 6x = 0 \text{ has roots } x=0,2,3.\quad\text{Solve } t^{3/2} - 5t + 6t^{1/2} = 0\;$

2qsubstitution bridge
Combine logs into a single logarithm and equate arguments
$\;\log_3 x + \log_3(x+2) = \log_3 8\;$
$\;\log_3[x(x+2)] = \log_3 8 \Rightarrow x^2+2x-8=0 \Rightarrow x=2\;$
2qlog law simplification
Condense a difference of logarithms into a single log of a quotient
$\;\ln(2x) - \ln(x+1) = 0\;$
$\;\ln\!\left(\dfrac{2x}{x+1}\right) = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{2x}{x+1} = 1 \Rightarrow x = 1\;$
2qlog law simplification

2qlog law simplification
Factor out the common exponential to enable zero-product analysis
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = e^{2x} + 4x\,e^{2x}\;$
$\;e^{2x}(1 + 4x) = 0 \Rightarrow 1 + 4x = 0 \Rightarrow x = -\tfrac{1}{4}\;$
2qstrategic factorisation
Factorise monic integer quadratic by systematic factor-pair search
$\;x^2 - 7x + 12 = 0\;$
$\;pq=12,\ p+q=7:\ 3\times4=12,\ 3+4=7 \Rightarrow (x-3)(x-4)=0\;$
2qstrategic factorisation
Factor out the lowest common power to leave a simple linear residual
$\;3(x+1)^2 e^{2x} + 6(x+1)^3 e^{2x}\;$
$\;3(x+1)^2 e^{2x}\bigl[1 + 2(x+1)\bigr] = 3(x+1)^2 e^{2x}(2x+3)\;$
2qstrategic factorisation
Apply domain-range duality to find domain or range of inverse
$\;f(x)=\dfrac{1}{x-3},\; x\neq 3,\;\text{range: } y\neq 0\;$
$\;\text{dom}(f^{-1})=\text{ran}(f):\; x\neq 0,\quad \text{ran}(f^{-1})=\text{dom}(f):\; y\neq 3\;$
2qinverse function application
Swap x and y then solve for y to find the inverse function
$\;y = \dfrac{3}{x+1}\;$
$\;x = \dfrac{3}{y+1} \Rightarrow x(y+1)=3 \Rightarrow y = \dfrac{3}{x}-1\;$
2qinverse function application
Decompose compound exponents to expose a shared base expression
$\;2^{2x+1} - 7 \cdot 2^x + 6 = 0\;$
$\;2^{2x+1} = 2 \cdot (2^x)^2 \Rightarrow 2(2^x)^2 - 7(2^x) + 6 = 0\;$
2qindex law decomposition
Split exponential of a linear expression into constant × base^(±t) form
$\;N = 10^{2 + 0.3t}\;$
$\;N = 10^{2} \cdot 10^{0.3t} = 100 \cdot (10^{0.3})^{t} = 100 \cdot 2^{t}\;$
2qindex law decomposition
Decompose compound exponent via index laws to expose substitution structure
$\;2^{2x+1} - 3 \cdot 2^x = 2\;$
$\;2^{2x} \cdot 2 - 3 \cdot 2^x = 2,\quad p=2^x \Rightarrow 2p^2 - 3p - 2 = 0\;$
2qindex law decomposition
Rewrite surds and reciprocal terms as fractional/negative indices to enable power-rule operations
$\;y = \dfrac{3}{\sqrt{x}} + \sqrt{x}\;$
$\;y = 3x^{-1/2} + x^{1/2}\;$
2qindex law decomposition
Multiply numerator and denominator by the lowest power to clear negative exponents
$\;\dfrac{3x^{1/2} - x^{-1/2}}{x^{1/2}}\;$
$\;\dfrac{x^{1/2}(3x^{1/2} - x^{-1/2})}{x^{1/2} \cdot x^{1/2}} = \dfrac{3x - 1}{x}\;$
2qrationalisation
Solve quadratic via formula and reject the non-physical root
$\;n^2 + n - 6 = 0,\quad n > 0\;$
$\;n = \dfrac{-1 \pm 5}{2} = 2 \text{ or } {-3} \Rightarrow n = 2\;$
2qroot selection
Cross-multiply to clear denominators and reduce to a polynomial equation
$\;\dfrac{x}{3} = \dfrac{2}{x-1}\;$
$\;x(x-1) = 6 \Rightarrow x^2 - x - 6 = 0\;$
2qfraction clearing
Multiply outer numerator and denominator by the inner denominator to clear a compound fraction
$\;\dfrac{2\cdot\dfrac{x+1}{x-1}+3}{\dfrac{x+1}{x-1}-1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{2(x+1)+3(x-1)}{(x+1)-(x-1)} = \dfrac{5x-1}{2}\;$
2qfraction clearing
Match linearised log-equation coefficients to graph gradient and intercept
$\;A = p\,q^t,\quad \log_{10}A = 0.5t + 2\;$
$\;\log_{10}q = 0.5,\; \log_{10}p = 2 \;\Rightarrow\; q = 10^{0.5} \approx 3.16,\; p = 10^{2} = 100\;$
2qcoefficient matching
Reject non-positive roots after exponential substitution to enforce range
$\;y = e^x,\quad y^2 - 2y - 3 = 0 \Rightarrow y = 3 \text{ or } y = -1\;$
$\;y = -1 \text{ rejected } (e^x > 0) \Rightarrow e^x = 3 \Rightarrow x = \ln 3\;$
2qdomain filtering
Filter candidate solutions through the substitution's hidden domain
$\;\text{Let } u = \sqrt{x},\quad u^2 - 5u + 6 = 0 \Rightarrow u = 2,\, 3\;$
$\;u = \sqrt{x} \geq 0:\; u=2\;\checkmark,\; u=3\;\checkmark \Rightarrow x = 4,\, 9\;$
2qdomain filtering
Solve quadratic inequality by finding roots and selecting interior interval
$\;x^2 - 5x + 4 < 0\;$
$\;(x-1)(x-4) < 0 \Rightarrow 1 < x < 4\;$
2qquadratic inequality
Back-substitute into the simplest already-isolated equation to recover the remaining unknown
$\;y = 5 - x,\quad x = 2\;$
$\;y = 5 - 2 = 3\;$
2qback substitution
Reject extraneous roots by enforcing logarithm domain on original equation
$\;\log_2(x) + \log_2(x-3) = 2 \Rightarrow x^2 - 3x - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 4,\; x = -1\;$
$\;x = -1 \text{ rejected: } \log_2(-1)\text{ undefined};\quad x = 4\;$
2qdomain validation
Factorise a quadratic by inspection to extract exact rational roots
$\;2x^2 - 5x + 3 = 0\;$
$\;(2x - 3)(x - 1) = 0 \Rightarrow x = \tfrac{3}{2} \text{ or } x = 1\;$
2qquadratic factorisation
Apply discriminant > 0 to enforce two distinct real roots
$\;x^2 + kx + 4 = 0\;$
$\;k^2 - 4(1)(4) > 0 \Rightarrow k^2 - 16 > 0\;$
2qdiscriminant condition
Apply square-of-sum identity to express α²+β² via Vieta's
$\;x^2 - 3x + 1 = 0,\quad \alpha+\beta = 3,\quad \alpha\beta = 1\;$
$\;\alpha^2+\beta^2 = (\alpha+\beta)^2 - 2\alpha\beta = 9 - 2 = 7\;$

2qnumerical approximation

2qcompound substitution tracking
Differentiate implicitly treating y as a function of x to extract dy/dx
$\;x^2 + y^2 = 25\;$
$\;2x + 2y\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = -\dfrac{x}{y}\;$
2qimplicit differentiation
Differentiate implicitly term-by-term using product and chain rules to obtain dy/dx
$\;x^2 + xy + y^2 = 7\;$

2qimplicit differentiation
Select the product rule to differentiate a product of two non-trivial functions

2qproduct rule selection
Apply the product rule to mixed x–y terms during implicit differentiation

2qchain rule

$\;y = x^2,\quad P = (1,1),\quad Q = (1+h,\,(1+h)^2)\;$

2qasymptotic analysis
Validate candidate values against the function's domain and range to reject extraneous cases

2qdomain validation
Differentiate and evaluate at the given point to obtain the tangent gradient

2qtangent via derivative
Bridge between variables using the defining equation or a shared parameter

$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2\sec x\tan x = \dfrac{y}{2}\,\sqrt{\dfrac{y^2}{4}-1} \cdot 2 = \dfrac{y\sqrt{y^2-4}}{4}\;$
2qsubstitution bridge
Differentiate repeatedly and evaluate at the expansion point to obtain Taylor/Maclaurin coefficients
$\;f(x) = e^{x^2},\quad \text{Maclaurin up to } x^4\;$
$\;f(0)=1,\ f'=2xe^{x^2}\!\Rightarrow f'(0)=0,\ f''=2e^{x^2}+4x^2e^{x^2}\!\Rightarrow f''(0)=2,\ f'''(0)=0,\ f^{(4)}(0)=12 \Rightarrow e^{x^2}=1+x^2+\tfrac{x^4}{2}\;$
2qsystematic differentiation
Match curve's derivative to required line gradient to locate tangent point
$\;y = x^2 + 3x,\quad \text{tangent parallel to } y = 5x\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x + 3 = 5 \Rightarrow x = 1,\; y = 4\;$
2qtangent gradient matching
Differentiate the inverse relation and reciprocate to obtain dy/dx
$\;y = \arcsin x \Rightarrow x = \sin y\;$
$\;\dfrac{dx}{dy} = \cos y \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{1}{\cos y} = \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{1-x^2}}\;$
2qinverse function differentiation
Apply the quotient rule to differentiate a ratio of two functions
$\;y = \dfrac{x^2}{x+1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{(x+1)(2x) - x^2(1)}{(x+1)^2} = \dfrac{x^2+2x}{(x+1)^2}\;$
2qquotient rule
Analyse sign of f'(x) to prove monotonicity or classify stationary points
$\;f(x)=\dfrac{2x+1}{x-1},\quad x>1\;$
$\;f'(x)=\dfrac{(x-1)(2)-(2x+1)(1)}{(x-1)^2}=\dfrac{-3}{(x-1)^2}<0 \Rightarrow f \text{ decreasing}\;$
2qsign of derivative
Sketch curve via end-behaviour and turning points to count solutions of f(x)=k
$\;f(x) = x^3 - 3x,\quad f'(x)=0 \Rightarrow x=-1\ (\text{max},\,2),\; x=1\ (\text{min},\,-2)\;$
$\;\lim_{x\to\pm\infty} f = \pm\infty,\; \text{rises to }2,\; \text{falls to }-2,\; \text{rises} \Rightarrow f(x)=k \text{ has } \begin{cases}3 \text{ roots} & -2<k<2\\1 \text{ root} & |k|>2\end{cases}\;$
2qcurve sketching for solutions
Translate tangent gradient conditions into algebraic equations on dy/dx
$\;y = x^3 - 3x,\quad \text{tangent slope } = 9\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 - 3 = 9 \Rightarrow 3x^2 = 12 \Rightarrow x = \pm 2\;$
2qgeometric to algebraic translation
Bridge known and target rates via the chain rule through a shared variable
$\;V = h^3,\quad \dfrac{dV}{dt} = 6,\quad h = 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{dh}{dt} = \dfrac{dV/dt}{dV/dh} = \dfrac{6}{3h^2}\bigg|_{h=1} = 2\;$
2qrelated rates chain rule bridge
Substitute u = inner function to collapse a composite power into an integrable form
$\;\int 2x(x^2+1)^3\,dx\;$
$\;u=x^2+1,\; du=2x\,dx \Rightarrow \int u^3\,du = \tfrac{u^4}{4}+C = \tfrac{(x^2+1)^4}{4}+C\;$
2qsubstitution bridge
Substitute u equal to the inner expression to absorb its derivative
$\;\int_0^2 \frac{x}{(x+1)^2}\,dx\;$
$\;u = x+1,\; x = u-1,\; \int_1^3 \frac{u-1}{u^2}\,du = \int_1^3 \left(\frac{1}{u} - \frac{1}{u^2}\right)du\;$
2qsubstitution bridge
Apply integration by parts when integrand is a product of unlike functions or a lone log/inverse-trig
$\;\int x\,e^x\,dx\;$
$\;u=x,\ dv=e^x dx \Rightarrow x\,e^x - \int e^x\,dx = x\,e^x - e^x + C\;$
2qintegration by parts
Apply LIATE priority to choose u in integration by parts
$\;\int x\,e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;u=x,\; dv=e^{x}dx \Rightarrow x\,e^{x} - \int e^{x}\,dx = (x-1)\,e^{x}+C\;$
2qintegration by parts
Split sin^n x = sin^(n-1) x · sin x to set up IBP reduction
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\, dx\;$
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-1} x \cdot \sin x\, dx,\quad u = \sin^{n-1} x,\; dv = \sin x\, dx\;$
2qreduction formula ibp
Apply integration by parts twice to close a polynomial-times-trig reduction formula
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} x^n \sin x\, dx\;$
$\;I_n = n\bigl[x^{n-1}\sin x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2} - n(n-1)\int_0^{\pi/2} x^{n-2}\sin x\, dx = n\!\left(\tfrac{\pi}{2}\right)^{n-1} - n(n-1)\,I_{n-2}\;$
2qreduction formula ibp
Set u = (polynomial factor) in IBP to drive a reduction formula
$\;I_n = \int_0^1 x^n e^{-x}\,dx\;$
$\;u = x^n,\ dv = e^{-x}dx \Rightarrow I_n = \bigl[-x^n e^{-x}\bigr]_0^1 + n\!\int_0^1 x^{n-1}e^{-x}\,dx = nI_{n-1} - e^{-1}\;$

$\;V = \pi\int_0^1 y^2\,dx = \pi\int_0^1 x^4\,dx\;$
2qformula selection
Integrate f'(x) term-by-term to recover f(x) with constant of integration
$\;f'(x) = 3x^2 - 2x + 1\;$
$\;f(x) = x^3 - x^2 + x + c\;$
2qantidifferentiation
Classify ordinates as endpoints vs interior to apply the trapezium rule
$\;n=4,\; h=0.25,\; y_0=1,\; y_1=2,\; y_2=3,\; y_3=4,\; y_4=5\;$
$\;\int_0^1 y\,dx \approx \dfrac{0.25}{2}\bigl[(1+5)+2(2+3+4)\bigr] = 0.125 \times 24 = 3\;$
2qtrapezium rule application
Flip integration limits to absorb a leading negative sign
$\;-\int_{4}^{0} u^{1/2}\,du\;$
$\;-\int_{4}^{0} u^{1/2}\,du = \int_{0}^{4} u^{1/2}\,du\;$
2qlimit reversal
Convert x-limits to u-limits to keep the definite integral in u-space
$\;\int_{0}^{1} 2x(x^2+1)^3\,dx,\quad u=x^2+1\;$
$\;x=0\Rightarrow u=1,\; x=1\Rightarrow u=2:\quad \int_{1}^{2} u^3\,du = \tfrac{15}{4}\;$
2qlimit transformation
Set up trapezium rule by reading h and labelling ordinates correctly
$\;x: 0,\,1,\,2,\,3;\quad y: 2,\,5,\,4,\,3;\quad n=3,\; h=1\;$
$\;\int_0^3 y\,dx \approx \tfrac{1}{2}\bigl[(2+3)+2(5+4)\bigr] = \tfrac{1}{2}(23) = 11.5\;$
2qtrapezium rule setup
Verify integrand sign on the interval to remove absolute values
$\;\int_0^2 |x-3|\, dx\;$
$\;x-3 < 0 \text{ on } [0,2] \Rightarrow \int_0^2 (3-x)\, dx\;$
2qsign analysis
Apply reverse power rule term-by-term to integrate non-integer powers
$\;\int \sqrt{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\int x^{1/2}\,dx = \dfrac{x^{3/2}}{3/2} = \tfrac{2}{3}x^{3/2} + C\;$
2qpower rule integration
Reuse an earlier part's integral result by matching structural form
$\;\text{(a)}\ \int x e^x\,dx = xe^x - e^x + C.\quad \text{(b)}\ \tfrac{1}{2}y^2 = \int t\,e^t\,dt\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{2}y^2 = te^t - e^t + C \Rightarrow y^2 = 2te^t - 2e^t + A\;$
2qcross part linkage
Algebraically pre-process the integrand into a sum of standard x^n or e^{kx} terms
$\;\int \dfrac{x^2 + 3}{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \left(x + 3x^{-1}\right)dx = \dfrac{x^2}{2} + 3\ln|x| + C\;$
2qalgebraic preparation
Append +C to indefinite integrals to capture the full antiderivative family
$\;\int 2x\,dx\;$
$\;x^2 + C\;$
2qintegration constant
Assign u to the algebraic factor via LIATE for integration by parts
$\;\int x\,e^{2x}\,dx\;$
$\;u=x,\ \tfrac{dv}{dx}=e^{2x} \Rightarrow \tfrac{x}{2}e^{2x}-\int \tfrac{1}{2}e^{2x}\,dx = \tfrac{x}{2}e^{2x}-\tfrac{1}{4}e^{2x}+C\;$
2qparts assignment
Spot f'(x)/f(x) or f'(x)·f(x)^n pattern to integrate by inspection
$\;\int \dfrac{2x}{x^2+1}\,dx\;$
$\;f=x^2+1,\; f'=2x \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{f'}{f}\,dx = \ln(x^2+1)+C\;$
2qreverse chain rule
Integrate both sides of d/dx[μy]=μQ to obtain the general solution
$\;\dfrac{d}{dx}[e^{2x} y] = e^{x}\;$
$\;e^{2x} y = \int e^{x}\,dx + C = e^{x} + C \Rightarrow y = e^{-x} + Ce^{-2x}\;$
2qdirect integration
Set up washer/disc volume by squaring y to eliminate surds
$\;V = \pi\int_{0}^{4}\left(3^2 - \left(\sqrt{x}\right)^2\right)dx\;$
$\;V = \pi\int_{0}^{4}\left(9 - x\right)dx\;$
2qvolume of revolution setup
Split integral by linearity to reuse a previous numerical estimate
$\;\int_0^{5} f(x)\,dx \approx 8.3,\quad g(x) = f(x) + 3\;$
$\;\int_0^{5} g(x)\,dx = \int_0^{5} f(x)\,dx + 3(5-0) = 8.3 + 15 = 23.3\;$
2qintegral linearity reuse
Deduce missing integration limit from curve-axis or curve-domain constraints
$\;y = \sqrt{x},\quad y\text{-axis},\quad x\text{-axis},\quad x = 4\;$
$\;y=0 \Rightarrow \sqrt{x}=0 \Rightarrow x=0;\quad \text{limits: } [0,\,4]\;$
2qboundary identification
Pull constant multiplier outside the integral to simplify or reuse a known result
$\;\int 5x^2\,dx\;$
$\;5\int x^2\,dx = 5 \cdot \dfrac{x^3}{3} = \dfrac{5x^3}{3} + C\;$
2qconstant factor extraction
Rewrite the integrand into power-rule-ready form before integrating
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x}}\,dx\;$
$\;\int x^{-1/2}\,dx = \dfrac{x^{1/2}}{1/2} + C = 2\sqrt{x} + C\;$
2qalgebraic rewrite before integration
Convert parametric area ∫y dx into ∫y(dx/dt)dt with sign-aware limits
$\;x = 2 - t,\quad y = t^2,\quad 0 \le x \le 2\;$
$\;A = \int_{t=2}^{0} t^2(-1)\,dt = \int_{0}^{2} t^2\,dt\;$
2qparametric area conversion
Use concavity and strip-width to judge and improve trapezium-rule accuracy
$\;y = \sqrt{x},\quad x \in [0,4],\quad \text{2 strips}\;$
$\;f''(x)<0 \Rightarrow \text{concave down} \Rightarrow \text{chords below curve} \Rightarrow A_{\text{trap}} < A_{\text{true}};\; \text{more strips} \Rightarrow \text{better}\;$
2qtrapezium rule error analysis
Repeat integration by parts n times to eliminate a degree-n polynomial factor
$\;\int x^2 e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;x^2 e^x - 2\!\int x e^x\,dx = x^2 e^x - 2\bigl(x e^x - e^x\bigr) + C = (x^2 - 2x + 2)e^x + C\;$

2qde moivre root extraction
Substitute to bridge a complex equation into a simpler solvable form
$\;z^4 + 5z^2 + 4 = 0\;$
$\;w = z^2:\quad w^2 + 5w + 4 = 0 \Rightarrow (w+1)(w+4) = 0 \Rightarrow z = \pm i,\;\pm 2i\;$
2qsubstitution bridge
Parametrise the source locus with one real parameter to substitute into the target equation
$\;\arg(z) = \tfrac{\pi}{4},\quad |z - 2| = \sqrt{2}\;$
$\;z = t(1+i),\; t>0:\quad (t-2)^2 + t^2 = 2 \Rightarrow t^2 - 2t + 1 = 0 \Rightarrow t=1,\; z=1+i\;$
2qparametric substitution
Invert the Möbius transformation to express z in terms of w
$\;w = \dfrac{z+1}{z-1},\quad |z|=1\;$
$\;z = \dfrac{w+1}{w-1} \Rightarrow \left|\dfrac{w+1}{w-1}\right| = 1 \Rightarrow |w+1| = |w-1|\;$
2qinverse substitution
Apply de Moivre's theorem to compute a power of a complex number
$\;z = \sqrt{2}\!\left(\cos\dfrac{\pi}{4} + i\sin\dfrac{\pi}{4}\right),\quad n=6\;$
$\;z^6 = (\sqrt{2})^6\!\left(\cos\dfrac{6\pi}{4} + i\sin\dfrac{6\pi}{4}\right) = 8\!\left(\cos\dfrac{3\pi}{2} + i\sin\dfrac{3\pi}{2}\right) = -8i\;$
2qde moivre power
Find principal argument via reference angle plus quadrant adjustment
$\;z = -1 + \sqrt{3}\,i\;$
$\;\alpha = \arctan\!\left(\dfrac{\sqrt{3}}{1}\right) = \dfrac{\pi}{3},\quad \text{Q2: } \arg z = \pi - \dfrac{\pi}{3} = \dfrac{2\pi}{3}\;$
2qquadrant adjusted argument
Convert Cartesian complex numbers to modulus-argument form with quadrant check
$\;w = -1 + i\;$
$\;r = \sqrt{1+1} = \sqrt{2},\quad \theta = \arctan\!\left(\tfrac{1}{-1}\right)+\pi = \tfrac{3\pi}{4} \Rightarrow w = \sqrt{2}\!\left(\cos\tfrac{3\pi}{4}+i\sin\tfrac{3\pi}{4}\right)\;$
2qmodulus argument conversion
Eliminate the real parameter to obtain a Cartesian equation in u and v
$\;u = \dfrac{t+1}{t-1},\quad v = \dfrac{-2}{t-1}\;$
$\;u = 1 + \dfrac{2}{t-1} = 1 - v \Rightarrow u + v - 1 = 0\;$

2qgeometric interpretation

$\;2 > 1,\; 2 < 4,\; 1 > 0 \Rightarrow x < y < 4,\; x > 0\;$

$\;BC = AC - AB = 10 - 7 = 3\;$
2qgeometric deduction
Multiply gradients of the two segments at the vertex to verify a right angle
$\;V(1,1),\; A(3,3),\; B(3,-1)\;$
$\;m_{VA} = \frac{3-1}{3-1} = 1,\quad m_{VB} = \frac{-1-1}{3-1} = -1,\quad m_{VA} \times m_{VB} = -1 \Rightarrow VA \perp VB\;$

2qpoint gradient form
Invoke converse of angle-in-semicircle theorem to identify a diameter
$\;P(0,0),\; Q(2,2),\; R(4,0) \text{ lie on a circle.}\; m_{QP}=\frac{2-0}{2-0}=1,\; m_{QR}=\frac{2-0}{2-4}=-1.\;$
$\;m_{QP}\cdot m_{QR}=1\times(-1)=-1 \;\Rightarrow\; \angle PQR=90^\circ \;\Rightarrow\; PR \text{ is a diameter (converse of angle in semicircle), centre }=\left(2,0\right),\; r=2\;$
2qcircle theorem invocation
Substitute the given point into dy/dx then apply point-gradient formula
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{x+y}{y-x},\quad (1,\,2)\;$
$\;m = \dfrac{1+2}{2-1} = 3 \Rightarrow y-2 = 3(x-1) \Rightarrow 3x - y - 1 = 0\;$
2qtangent from implicit derivative
Set discriminant to zero to enforce line-curve tangency
$\;y = x + c \text{ tangent to } x^2 + y^2 = 1\;$
$\;x^2 + (x+c)^2 = 1 \Rightarrow 2x^2 + 2cx + (c^2-1)=0,\quad \Delta = 4c^2 - 8(c^2-1)=0 \Rightarrow c = \pm\sqrt{2}\;$

2qconic focal distance
Assemble P from eigenvectors and D from eigenvalues to write A = PDP⁻¹
$\;\lambda_1=2,\;\mathbf{v}_1=\begin{pmatrix}1\\0\end{pmatrix},\quad \lambda_2=3,\;\mathbf{v}_2=\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;P=\begin{pmatrix}1&1\\0&1\end{pmatrix},\; D=\begin{pmatrix}2&0\\0&3\end{pmatrix},\; A=PDP^{-1}\;$
2qdiagonalisation
Assemble A = PDP⁻¹ with matched eigenvector–eigenvalue column ordering
$\;\lambda_1=1,\; \mathbf{e}_1=\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\end{pmatrix},\quad \lambda_2=3,\; \mathbf{e}_2=\begin{pmatrix}1\\-1\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;P=\begin{pmatrix}1&1\\1&-1\end{pmatrix},\; D=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&3\end{pmatrix} \Rightarrow A=PDP^{-1}=\begin{pmatrix}2&-1\\-1&2\end{pmatrix}\;$
2qdiagonalisation
Verify diagonalisation by checking AP = PD column-by-column
$\;A=\begin{pmatrix}2&1\\0&3\end{pmatrix},\ P=\begin{pmatrix}1&1\\0&1\end{pmatrix},\ D=\begin{pmatrix}2&0\\0&3\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;AP=\begin{pmatrix}2&3\\0&3\end{pmatrix},\ PD=\begin{pmatrix}2&3\\0&3\end{pmatrix} \Rightarrow AP=PD\ \checkmark\;$
2qverification strategy
Form det(A − λI) = 0 to extract eigenvalues
$\;A = \begin{pmatrix} 3 & 1 \\ 0 & 2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\det(A - \lambda I) = (3-\lambda)(2-\lambda) = 0 \Rightarrow \lambda = 2,\,3\;$
2qcharacteristic polynomial
Apply Cayley-Hamilton to reduce high matrix powers and polynomials
$\;A^2 - 4A + 3I = 0,\quad \text{find } A^3\;$
$\;A^3 = A \cdot A^2 = A(4A - 3I) = 4A^2 - 3A = 4(4A - 3I) - 3A = 13A - 12I\;$
2qcayley hamilton reduction
Apply A^n = PD^nP^(-1) to reduce matrix powers to scalar powers
$\;A = PDP^{-1},\quad D = \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;A^n = P \begin{pmatrix} 1^n & 0 \\ 0 & 2^n \end{pmatrix} P^{-1} = P \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 0 \\ 0 & 2^n \end{pmatrix} P^{-1}\;$
2qdiagonal power shortcut
Form the characteristic equation det(A − λI) = 0 to extract eigenvalues
$\;A = \begin{pmatrix} 3 & 1 \\ 0 & 2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\det(A - \lambda I) = (3-\lambda)(2-\lambda) - 0 = 0 \Rightarrow \lambda = 2,\,3\;$
2qeigenvalue extraction
Substitute trial PI into ODE and equate coefficients to determine constants
$\;y'' - 3y' + 2y = 4e^{5x},\quad y_{PI} = ae^{5x}\;$
$\;25a - 15a + 2a = 4 \Rightarrow 12a = 4 \Rightarrow a = \tfrac{1}{3}\;$
2qundetermined coefficients

2qpi trial selection

$\;4x\frac{d^2y}{dx^2} + 2\frac{dy}{dx} + y = 0,\quad x = t^2\;$
$\;\frac{dy}{dx}=\frac{1}{2t}\frac{dy}{dt},\ \frac{d^2y}{dx^2}=\frac{1}{4t^2}\frac{d^2y}{dt^2}-\frac{1}{4t^3}\frac{dy}{dt} \Rightarrow \frac{d^2y}{dt^2}+y=0\;$

2qpost substitution separation
Apply the polar area formula A = ½∫r² dθ with correct limits

$\;A = \tfrac{1}{2}\int_0^{\pi/2} \cos^2\theta\,d\theta = \tfrac{1}{2}\int_0^{\pi/2} \tfrac{1+\cos 2\theta}{2}\,d\theta = \dfrac{\pi}{8}\;$

2qcartesian polar bridge
Substitute the assumed closed form into the recurrence to bridge k to k+1
$\;u_{k+1} = 2u_k + 1,\quad u_k = 2^k - 1\;$

2qrecurrence induction bridge
Use sign analysis on the domain to fix square-root signs or disprove inequalities
$\;0 < y < \dfrac{\pi}{4},\quad \sin^2(2y) = \dfrac{x}{6}\;$
$\;0 < 2y < \dfrac{\pi}{2} \Rightarrow \sin(2y) > 0 \Rightarrow \sin(2y) = +\sqrt{\dfrac{x}{6}}\;$
2qsign analysis
Substitute rearranged inductive hypothesis to expose the divisor as a common factor
$\;f(k)=4^k+6k-1=9M \Rightarrow 4^k=9M-6k+1\;$
$\;f(k{+}1)=4(9M-6k+1)+6k+5=36M-18k+9=9(4M-2k+1)\;$
2qhypothesis substitution
Split a^{k+1} via index laws to expose the P(k) sub-expression
$\;4^{k+3} + 5^{2k+3}\;$
$\;4\cdot 4^{k+2} + 25\cdot 5^{2k+1} = 4\bigl(4^{k+2}+5^{2k+1}\bigr) + 21\cdot 5^{2k+1}\;$
2qindex law decomposition
Rearrange the inductive hypothesis to isolate one exponential term for direct substitution
$\;5^{k+1} - 1 = 4M,\; M \in \mathbb{Z} \Rightarrow 5^{k+1} = 4M + 1\;$
$\;5^{k+2} - 1 = 5 \cdot 5^{k+1} - 1 = 5(4M+1) - 1 = 20M + 4 = 4(5M+1)\;$
2qhypothesis rearrangement
Decompose the (k+1) case to expose the inductive hypothesis
$\;f(k) = 3^{k+1} - 2k - 3,\quad 4 \mid f(k)\;$
$\;f(k+1) - 3f(k) = (3^{k+2}-2k-5) - 3(3^{k+1}-2k-3) = 4k+4 = 4(k+1) \Rightarrow f(k+1)=3f(k)+4(k+1)\;$
2qinduction decomposition
Apply the sum-to-infinity formula to convert S∞ into algebra in a and r
$\;a = 2,\quad S_\infty = 8\;$
$\;8 = \dfrac{2}{1-r} \Rightarrow 1-r = \tfrac{1}{4} \Rightarrow r = \tfrac{3}{4}\;$
2qformula selection
Substitute the standard formula Σn = N(N+1)/2 to evaluate a linear sum in closed form
$\;\sum_{n=1}^{10} 3n\;$

2qstandard series substitution
Substitute known Maclaurin series instead of differentiating repeatedly
$\;e^{\sin x} \text{ up to } x^3\;$
$\;e^u = 1 + u + \tfrac{u^2}{2} + \tfrac{u^3}{6},\; u = x - \tfrac{x^3}{6} \Rightarrow 1 + x + \tfrac{x^2}{2} + \tfrac{x^3}{6}\;$
2qstandard series substitution
Substitute into a standard Maclaurin series to bypass repeated differentiation
$\;e^{x^2} \text{ up to } x^4\;$
$\;e^u = 1 + u + \tfrac{u^2}{2!} + \cdots \xrightarrow{u=x^2} 1 + x^2 + \tfrac{x^4}{2}\;$
2qstandard series substitution
Substitute one series equation into another to bridge and eliminate a shared variable
$\;S_\infty = \dfrac{a}{1-r} = 8,\quad S_2 = \dfrac{a(1-r^2)}{1-r} = 6\;$
$\;a = 8(1-r) \Rightarrow 6 = 8(1-r)(1-r^2)/(1-r) = 8(1-r^2) \Rightarrow r^2 = \tfrac{1}{4},\ r = \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
2qsubstitution bridge
Assemble Maclaurin polynomial from computed derivative values at zero
$\;y(0)=1,\ y'(0)=2,\ y''(0)=-6,\ y'''(0)=12\;$
$\;y \approx 1 + 2x + \dfrac{-6}{2!}x^2 + \dfrac{12}{3!}x^3 = 1 + 2x - 3x^2 + 2x^3\;$
2qmaclaurin assembly
Apply |r|<1 convergence condition to select the valid common ratio
$\;3r^2 - 4r - 4 = 0,\quad S_\infty \text{ exists}\;$
$\;(3r+2)(r-2)=0 \Rightarrow r=-\tfrac{2}{3}\ (|r|<1),\quad r=2\ \text{rejected}\;$
2qconstraint based root selection
Substitute a chosen x-value into the truncated series to obtain a numerical approximation
$\;e^x \approx 1 + x + \tfrac{x^2}{2},\quad x = 0.1\;$
$\;1 + 0.1 + \tfrac{0.01}{2} = 1.105\;$
2qseries approximation

$\;ar = 6,\quad r = 2\;$
$\;a \cdot 2 = 6 \Rightarrow a = 3\;$

2qequation strategy
Equate parametric lines with distinct parameters to test 3D intersection
$\;\mathbf{r}_1 = (1,0,0) + \lambda(1,1,0),\quad \mathbf{r}_2 = (0,1,0) + \mu(1,0,1)\;$
$\;\text{(i)}\ 1+\lambda = \mu,\quad \text{(ii)}\ \lambda = 1 \Rightarrow \mu = 2;\quad \text{(iii)}\ 0 \neq 2 \Rightarrow \text{skew}\;$
2qparametric intersection test
Test parallelism by extracting k from two components and seeking contradiction
$\;\mathbf{d}_1 = (1,\,2,\,3),\quad \mathbf{d}_2 = (2,\,4,\,5)\;$
$\;k = \tfrac{2}{1} = 2,\quad k = \tfrac{5}{3} \neq 2 \Rightarrow \text{not parallel}\;$
2qscalar multiple test
Substitute the known parameter into its own line equation to extract the intersection point

2qback substitution

$\;\theta = \arccos\!\left(\dfrac{|{-4}|}{2\cdot4}\right) = \arccos\tfrac{1}{2} = 60°\;$
2qacute angle adjustment
Parametrise point on line and square distance to solve for parameter

$\;|PE|^2 = t^2(1+4+4)=9t^2=36 \Rightarrow t=\pm2,\quad E=(3,4,4)\text{ or }(-1,-4,-4)\;$
2qparametric distance equation
Apply dot-product formula with absolute value to find acute angle between lines
$\;\mathbf{d}_1 = (1,2,2),\quad \mathbf{d}_2 = (2,-1,2)\;$
$\;\cos\theta = \frac{|\mathbf{d}_1 \cdot \mathbf{d}_2|}{|\mathbf{d}_1|\,|\mathbf{d}_2|} = \frac{|2-2+4|}{3\cdot3} = \frac{4}{9}\;$
2qdirection vector angle
Apply the point-to-plane perpendicular distance formula to compute shortest distance
$\;P=(1,\,2,\,3),\quad \Pi:\,2x + y - 2z = 3\;$
$\;D = \dfrac{|2(1)+1(2)-2(3)-3|}{\sqrt{4+1+4}} = \dfrac{|-3|}{3} = 1\;$
2qdistance formula
Apply scalar triple product to compute tetrahedron volume
$\;\mathbf{a} = \mathbf{i} + 2\mathbf{j} + 3\mathbf{k},\quad \mathbf{b} = 2\mathbf{i} + \mathbf{j},\quad \mathbf{c} = \mathbf{i} + \mathbf{k}\;$
$\;\mathbf{b} \times \mathbf{c} = \mathbf{i} - 2\mathbf{j} - \mathbf{k},\quad \mathbf{a} \cdot (\mathbf{b} \times \mathbf{c}) = 1 - 4 - 3 = -6 \Rightarrow V = \tfrac{1}{6}|{-6}| = 1\;$
2qscalar triple product volume
Combine root-fractions over αβ and reduce the numerator via symmetric identities

$\;\dfrac{\alpha^2+\beta^2}{\alpha\beta}=\dfrac{(\alpha+\beta)^2-2\alpha\beta}{\alpha\beta}=\dfrac{9-2}{1}=7\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Bridge integrand to u via shared-denominator decomposition

$\;u = 1 + \dfrac{2}{x-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{x+3}{x-1} = 1 + \dfrac{2}{x-1} + \dfrac{2}{x-1} = 2 + \dfrac{2}{x-1} = u + 1\;$

Split exponential of a sum and collapse e^{ln f} to f

1qlog law simplification

1qstrategic factorisation

1qstrategic factorisation
Factor out shared product before combining fraction with non-fraction

$\;(k+1)\!\left[\tfrac{k}{2}+1\right] = (k+1)\cdot\tfrac{k+2}{2} = \dfrac{(k+1)(k+2)}{2}\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Factor out common exponential before evaluating definite-integral limits
$\;\tfrac12 x\,e^{2x} - \tfrac14 e^{2x}\Big|_0^1\;$
$\;\tfrac14 e^{2x}(2x-1)\Big|_0^1 = \tfrac14 e^2(1) - \tfrac14(−1) = \tfrac14(e^2+1)\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Factor common exponential from repeated-IBP antiderivative before evaluating bounds
$\;-x^2 e^{-x} - 2x e^{-x} - 2e^{-x}\;$
$\;-e^{-x}(x^2 + 2x + 2)\Big|_0^1 = -5e^{-1} - (-2) = 2 - 5e^{-1}\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Factor common terms from derivative to expose linear factors
$\;f'(x) = 2(x-1)e^{2x} + 2(x-1)^2 e^{2x}\;$
$\;f'(x) = 2(x-1)e^{2x}\bigl[1+(x-1)\bigr] = 2(x-1)e^{2x}\,x\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Factor out shared bracket before combining algebraic terms
$\;x(x+1) + 3(x+1)\;$
$\;(x+1)[x+3] = (x+1)(x+3)\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Cross-multiply then collect and factor x to invert a rational function
$\;y = \dfrac{x+1}{x-2}\;$
$\;y(x-2) = x+1 \Rightarrow x(y-1) = 2y+1 \Rightarrow f^{-1}(x) = \dfrac{2x+1}{x-1}\;$
1qinverse function application
Set y = f(x), solve for x, then swap variables to invert
$\;y = \dfrac{2x+1}{x-1}\;$
$\;y(x-1)=2x+1 \Rightarrow x=\dfrac{y+1}{y-2},\quad f^{-1}(x)=\dfrac{x+1}{x-2}\;$
1qinverse function application
Cite range of f as domain of f⁻¹ via inverse duality
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{x+1}{x-2},\quad x \neq 2,\quad \text{range: } \mathbb{R}\setminus\{1\}\;$
$\;f^{-1}(x) = \dfrac{2x+1}{x-1},\quad \text{dom}(f^{-1}) = \mathbb{R}\setminus\{1\}\;$
1qinverse function application
Swap x and y to set up inverse rearrangement
$\;y = 2x + 1\;$
$\;x = 2y + 1 \Rightarrow y = \dfrac{x-1}{2}\;$
1qinverse function application
Decompose fractional powers as root-then-integer-power to evaluate cleanly
$\;8^{2/3}\;$
$\;8^{2/3} = \left(\sqrt[3]{8}\right)^{2} = 2^{2} = 4\;$
1qindex law decomposition
Regroup exponent as power-of-a-power to enable substitution
$\;4^{2x} - 3\cdot 4^x,\quad y = 4^x\;$
$\;4^{2x} = (4^x)^2 = y^2 \Rightarrow y^2 - 3y\;$

$\;e^{3\ln 2}\;$
$\;e^{3\ln 2} = 2^3 = 8\;$
1qindex law decomposition

1qcoefficient matching
Equate two expressions for a symmetric function to solve for an unknown parameter
$\;x^2 + px + 3 = 0 \text{ has roots } \alpha,\beta;\quad 3x^2 - 4x + 1 = 0 \text{ has roots } \tfrac{1}{\alpha},\tfrac{1}{\beta}\;$
$\;\frac{\alpha+\beta}{\alpha\beta} = \frac{-p}{3},\quad \frac{1}{\alpha}+\frac{1}{\beta} = \frac{4}{3} \Rightarrow \frac{-p}{3} = \frac{4}{3} \Rightarrow p = -4\;$
1qcoefficient matching
Match given polynomial to tan(nθ)=k identity to fix k by coefficient comparison
$\;x^4 + 2x^3 - 6x^2 - 2x + 1 = 0,\quad \tan 4\theta = \dfrac{4t - 4t^3}{1 - 6t^2 + t^4}\;$
$\;t^4 - \tfrac{4}{k}t^3 - 6t^2 + \tfrac{4}{k}t + 1 = 0 \Rightarrow -\tfrac{4}{k} = 2 \Rightarrow k = -2\;$
1qcoefficient matching
Translate verbal coefficient condition into equation in parameter

Substitute intersection x-values into the simpler of the two functions

$\;g(-1) = 3,\; g(2) = 9 \Rightarrow (-1,\,3),\;(2,\,9)\;$
1qstrategic substitution
Pick the equation with a variable already isolated for substitution
$\;y = 2x + 1,\quad 3x + y = 6\;$
$\;3x + (2x+1) = 6 \Rightarrow 5x = 5 \Rightarrow x = 1\;$
1qstrategic substitution
Reconstruct quadratic from sum and product, then clear denominators
$\;S = \tfrac{5}{3},\quad P = \tfrac{1}{3}\;$
$\;x^2 - \tfrac{5}{3}x + \tfrac{1}{3} = 0 \;\xrightarrow{\times 3}\; 3x^2 - 5x + 1 = 0\;$
1qreverse vieta's
Locate a root by scanning a table for a sign change
$\;f(x) = x^2 - 3,\quad f(1) = -2,\quad f(2) = 1\;$
$\;f(1)<0,\ f(2)>0,\ f \text{ continuous} \Rightarrow \exists\,\alpha \in (1,2):\ f(\alpha)=0\;$
1qsign change root location
Use Vieta's product-of-roots to pin down a repeated real root
$\;x^3 + Ax^2 + Bx - 50 = 0,\quad \text{roots: } 1+i,\ 1-i,\ r\;$
$\;(1+i)(1-i)\cdot r = 50 \Rightarrow 2r = 50 \Rightarrow r = 25\;$
1qvieta's formulas
Substitute the already-isolated variable into the other equation
$\;y = 3 - x,\quad 2x + y = 5\;$
$\;2x + (3 - x) = 5 \Rightarrow x = 2,\ y = 1\;$
1qsimultaneous substitution
Substitute the derived linear relation back into the original curve equation
$\;x^2 + y^2 = 8,\quad y = -x\;$
$\;x^2 + (-x)^2 = 8 \Rightarrow 2x^2 = 8 \Rightarrow x = \pm 2\;$
1qsimultaneous substitution
Substitute linear equation into quadratic to reduce to one-variable quadratic
$\;x^2 + y^2 = 5,\quad y = x + 1\;$
$\;x^2 + (x+1)^2 = 5 \Rightarrow 2x^2 + 2x - 4 = 0\;$
1qsimultaneous substitution
Polynomial long division to decompose an improper rational fraction
$\;\dfrac{x^2 + 3x + 5}{x + 1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{x^2 + 3x + 5}{x + 1} = x + 2 + \dfrac{3}{x + 1}\;$
1qpolynomial division
Split improper rational function into constant minus proper fraction
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{2x+1}{x+3}\;$
$\;\dfrac{2(x+3)-5}{x+3} = 2 - \dfrac{5}{x+3}\;$
1qpolynomial division
Rewrite numerator as multiple of denominator plus remainder
$\;\dfrac{x+3}{x+1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{(x+1)+2}{x+1} = 1 + \dfrac{2}{x+1}\;$
1qpolynomial division
Find domain boundary by enforcing logarithm argument positivity
$\;f(x) = \ln(x + 1)\;$
$\;x + 1 > 0 \Rightarrow x > -1\;$
1qdomain restriction
Require radicand non-negative to determine domain
$\;f(x) = \sqrt{x - 3}\;$
$\;x - 3 \ge 0 \Rightarrow x \ge 3\;$
1qdomain restriction
Restrict quadratic to a monotonic branch to enable inversion
$\;g(x) = 4 - x^2,\quad x \geq 0\;$
$\;y = 4 - x^2 \Rightarrow x = \sqrt{4 - y} \Rightarrow g^{-1}(x) = \sqrt{4 - x},\quad x \leq 4\;$
1qdomain restriction
Intersect algebraic solution with model's contextual domain
$\;t^2 - 6t + 5 < 0,\quad 0 \le t \le 3\;$
$\;1 < t < 5 \;\cap\; [0,3] \;=\; 1 < t \le 3\;$
1qdomain restriction
Convert decimal substitutions to exact fractions before rounding
$\;y = \dfrac{3}{1+2x},\quad x = 0.3\;$
$\;1+0.6 = \tfrac{8}{5},\quad y = \tfrac{3}{\,8/5\,} = \tfrac{15}{8} = 1.875\;$
1qprecision management
Carry exact value forward; round only at final answer
$\;\theta = \pi - 1.4,\quad A = \tfrac{1}{2}(2^2)\theta\;$
$\;A = 2(\pi - 1.4) = 3.483\ldots \approx 3.48 \text{ (3 s.f.)}\;$
1qprecision management
Assign linear numerator Bx+C over irreducible quadratic factor
$\;\dfrac{4x}{(x-1)(x^2+1)}\;$
$\;\dfrac{4x}{(x-1)(x^2+1)} = \dfrac{A}{x-1} + \dfrac{Bx+C}{x^2+1}\;$
1qpartial fractions setup
Select partial fraction template from denominator factor types
$\;\dfrac{3x+1}{(x-1)(x+2)^2(x^2+1)}\;$
$\;\equiv \dfrac{A}{x-1} + \dfrac{B}{x+2} + \dfrac{C}{(x+2)^2} + \dfrac{Dx+E}{x^2+1}\;$
1qpartial fractions setup
Read root multiplicities from factored form to classify axis behaviour

1qroot multiplicity analysis
Translate 4 distinct real roots into two distinct positive roots of the quadratic-in-u

1qroot multiplicity analysis

$\;x^4 = 16\;$

1qroot multiplicity analysis

$\;\log_{10} N = 2t + 3\;$
$\;N = 10^{2t+3} = 10^3 \cdot (10^2)^t = 1000 \cdot 100^t\;$
1qinverse power operation
Exponentiate twice to unwrap a nested logarithm
$\;\ln(1 + \ln y) = x\;$
$\;1 + \ln y = e^{x} \Rightarrow y = e^{\,e^{x}-1}\;$
1qinverse power operation
Verify continuity on the interval before applying IVT
$\;f(x) = x - 1 + \dfrac{1}{3x-1},\quad [1,2]\;$
$\;3x-1=0 \Rightarrow x=\tfrac{1}{3}\notin[1,2],\ f\text{ cts on }[1,2];\ f(1)=\tfrac{1}{2}>0,\ f(2)=\tfrac{6}{5}>0 \Rightarrow \text{IVT applies}\;$
1qdomain validity check
Validate case solutions against their domain constraints
$\;|x - 3| = 2x \Rightarrow x = 1 \;(x \le 3),\; x = 3 \;(x > 3)\;$
$\;x=1:\;1 \le 3\;\checkmark;\quad x=3:\;3 > 3\;\times \Rightarrow x = 1\;$
1qdomain validity check
Impose non-negativity of RHS when solving modulus equations
$\;|2x - 1| = x - 3\;$
$\;x - 3 \ge 0 \Rightarrow x \ge 3;\quad x = \tfrac{4}{3},\, x = -2 \Rightarrow \text{no solution}\;$
1qdomain validity check
Reject roots that violate the original function's domain

1qequation selection

1qequation selection
Express the target quantity symbolically in the parameter then equate to its given value

1qequation selection
Solve the parameter-free subsystem first, then back-substitute for the remaining unknown

Chain-substitute via linking equation to reduce to one variable
$\;a + b = 5,\quad ab = 6,\quad b = 2c\;$
$\;b = 2c \Rightarrow a = 5 - 2c \Rightarrow (5 - 2c)(2c) = 6 \Rightarrow 2c^2 - 5c + 3 = 0\;$
1qsystematic elimination
Reject extraneous roots using stated domain constraint
$\;k > 0,\quad k^2 - 4k - 5 = 0 \Rightarrow (k-5)(k+1) = 0\;$
$\;k = 5\ \checkmark,\quad k = -1\ (\!<0)\ \boldsymbol{\times} \Rightarrow k = 5\;$
1qsolution validation
Use discriminant to confirm a residual quadratic has no further real roots
$\;(r-1)(r^2 + r + 1) = 0\;$
$\;\Delta = 1^2 - 4(1)(1) = -3 < 0 \Rightarrow r = 1 \text{ is the only real root}\;$
1qdiscriminant completeness check
Back-substitute each root into the simplest linking equation to recover the partner parameter
$\;a = \dfrac{6}{r},\quad r = 2 \text{ or } r = 3\;$
$\;r=2 \Rightarrow a=3;\quad r=3 \Rightarrow a=2 \quad\Longrightarrow\quad (a,r)=(3,2)\text{ or }(2,3)\;$
1qparameter recovery
Equate curve and line, take positive root as integration limit
$\;y = x^2,\quad y = 4\;$
$\;x^2 = 4 \Rightarrow x = \pm 2 \Rightarrow x = 2 \quad (x \geq 0)\;$
1qintersection for limits
Isolate the unit-coefficient variable and substitute to eliminate it
$\;x + 2y = 7,\quad 3x + 5y = 20\;$
$\;x = 7 - 2y \Rightarrow 3(7-2y) + 5y = 20 \Rightarrow 21 - y = 20 \Rightarrow y = 1\;$
1qdirected elimination
Form ratio of two computed areas to extract k in k:1
$\;R_1 = \tfrac{8}{3},\quad R_2 = \tfrac{4}{3}\;$
$\;k = \dfrac{R_1}{R_2} = \dfrac{8/3}{4/3} = \dfrac{8}{3} \times \dfrac{3}{4} = 2 \Rightarrow R_1 : R_2 = 2 : 1\;$
1qratio comparison
Cross-multiply a single-fraction equation to clear denominators
$\;\dfrac{x}{x+2} = \dfrac{3}{x}\;$
$\;x \cdot x = 3(x+2) \Rightarrow x^2 - 3x - 6 = 0\;$
1qcross multiplication
Divide through by GCF to match show-that target form
$\;6x^2 + 18x - 24 = 0\;$
$\;\div\,6\colon\quad x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0\;$
1qgoal directed simplification
Recognise perfect square trinomial to solve repeated-root quadratic
$\;x^2 - 6x + 9 = 0\;$
$\;(x-3)^2 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 3\;$
1qpattern recognition
Decompose surd power using index laws to preserve exact form
$\;(\sqrt{3})^5\;$
$\;(\sqrt{3})^4 \cdot \sqrt{3} = 3^2 \cdot \sqrt{3} = 9\sqrt{3}\;$
1qsurd manipulation
Evaluate mixed exponential-polynomial model term-by-term at given t
$\;P = 1 + 2^{t-4} + 2^{4-t} - (t-4)^2,\quad t = 3\;$
$\;P = 1 + 2^{-1} + 2^{1} - (-1)^2 = 1 + \tfrac{1}{2} + 2 - 1 = \tfrac{5}{2}\;$
1qsubstitution evaluation
Decompose compound logarithm using product and power laws
$\;\log_{10}(100x^3)\;$
$\;\log_{10}100 + \log_{10}x^3 = 2 + 3\log_{10}x\;$
1qlogarithm decomposition
Take logarithm in the base dictated by the target form
$\;5^{x+1} = 2\;$
$\;\log_5(5^{x+1}) = \log_5 2 \Rightarrow x = \log_5 2 - 1\;$
1qlogarithm base selection
Reuse part (a) polynomial as negated integrand in part (b)
$\;\text{(a)}\ C_1 - C_2 = x^2 - 3x + 2,\quad \text{roots } x=1,\,2\;$
$\;\text{(b)}\ \int_1^2 (C_2 - C_1)\,dx = \int_1^2 -(x^2 - 3x + 2)\,dx = \int_1^2 (-x^2 + 3x - 2)\,dx\;$
1qstructural reuse
Sketch exponential y = a·b^x via intercept and horizontal asymptote
$\;y = 2 \cdot 3^x\;$
$\;x=0 \Rightarrow y=2,\quad \text{asymptote } y=0\;$
1qexponential curve analysis
Merge same-exponent factors into a single base via (ab)^x
$\;3^x \times 2^x = 12\;$
$\;3^x \times 2^x = 6^x = 12 \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{\log 12}{\log 6}\;$
1qbase merging
Substitute y = 2^x to reduce exponential equation to quadratic
$\;4^x - 3\cdot 2^x + 2 = 0\;$
$\;y = 2^x:\quad y^2 - 3y + 2 = 0 \Rightarrow (y-1)(y-2) = 0 \Rightarrow x = 0,\,1\;$
1qexponential to quadratic substitution
Recognise f(x−a) as horizontal translation to sketch transformed curve
$\;y = 2^{x-3}\;$
$\;y = 2^x \text{ translated } 3 \text{ right}: (0,1)\mapsto(3,1),\; y\text{-int } = 2^{-3}=\tfrac{1}{8}\;$
1qfunction transformation
Rewrite both sides to a common base, then equate exponents
$\;2^x = 4^{x-6}\;$
$\;2^x = 2^{2(x-6)} \Rightarrow x = 2x - 12 \Rightarrow x = 12\;$
1qcommon base reduction
Sketch exponential decay from base between 0 and 1
$\;N = \left(\tfrac{1}{2}\right)^t,\quad t \geq 0\;$
$\;(0,1),\; N \searrow,\; N \to 0^+ \text{ as } t \to \infty\;$
1qgraph recognition
Translate half-life condition into algebraic equation
$\;N = k\lambda^{t},\quad \text{half-life } T = 4\;$
$\;k/2 = k\lambda^{4} \Rightarrow \lambda^{4} = \tfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow \lambda = \left(\tfrac{1}{2}\right)^{1/4}\;$
1qmodelling interpretation
Validate candidate roots against original logarithm domain
$\;\log(x+2) + \log(x-1) = \log 4 \Rightarrow x = -3,\; x = 2\;$
$\;x+2>0,\; x-1>0 \Rightarrow x>1;\; x=-3 \text{ rejected},\; x=2 \text{ accepted}\;$
1qextraneous solution rejection
Equate arguments of same-base logs via injectivity
$\;\log_3(2x+1) = \log_3(x+3)\;$
$\;2x+1 = x+3 \Rightarrow x = 2\;$
1qlog equality to algebraic
Rewrite surds as fractional powers to unlock the log power rule
$\;\log_a\!\left(\sqrt{a}\right)\;$
$\;\log_a\!\left(a^{1/2}\right) = \tfrac{1}{2}\log_a a = \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qexponent rewrite
Reject substitution roots that violate exponential positivity
$\;y^2 - 2y - 3 = 0,\quad y = e^x\;$
$\;y = 3 \text{ or } y = -1;\quad y = -1 \text{ rejected } (e^x > 0) \Rightarrow x = \ln 3\;$
1qdomain constraint
Condense same-base log terms into a single logarithm
$\;\log_2(x) + \log_2(x+2) = 3\;$
$\;\log_2\!\bigl(x(x+2)\bigr) = 3 \Rightarrow x^2+2x = 8\;$
1qlog condensation
Fuse same-exponent factors via a^m·b^m = (ab)^m
$\;3^y \cdot 5^y\;$
$\;3^y \cdot 5^y = (3 \cdot 5)^y = 15^y\;$
1qbase fusion
Decompose log arguments into atoms log_a(a) and log_a(b)
$\;\log_a b = k,\quad \log_a(a^2 b^3)\;$
$\;\log_a(a^2 b^3) = 2\log_a a + 3\log_a b = 2 + 3k\;$
1qlogarithmic decomposition
Merge same-base logs by product law then equate arguments
$\;\log_2(x) + \log_2(3) = \log_2(12)\;$
$\;\log_2(3x) = \log_2(12) \Rightarrow 3x = 12 \Rightarrow x = 4\;$
1qlog merge and equate
Split linear exponents into variable and constant factors
$\;5^{x+2}\;$
$\;5^{x+2} = 5^2 \cdot 5^x = 25 \cdot 5^x\;$
1qexponent decomposition
Equate two independent expressions for a shared quantity to eliminate a variable
$\;3r = k + 2,\quad 3r = 5 - k\;$
$\;k + 2 = 5 - k \Rightarrow 2k = 3 \Rightarrow k = \tfrac{3}{2}\;$
1qbridge equation elimination
Equate arguments once equation is in log(A) = log(B) form
$\;\log_2(3x+1) = \log_2(x+5)\;$
$\;3x+1 = x+5 \Rightarrow x = 2\;$
1qlog injectivity
Multiply through by denominator to clear fractions into integer-coefficient form
$\;y - 1 = \tfrac{2}{3}(x - 3)\;$
$\;3(y - 1) = 2(x - 3) \Rightarrow 2x - 3y - 3 = 0\;$
1qformat conversion
Divide equation through by GCD of coefficients before factorising
$\;6x^2 + 9x + 3 = 0\;$
$\;\div 3:\quad 2x^2 + 3x + 1 = 0 \Rightarrow (2x+1)(x+1) = 0\;$
1qcoefficient reduction
Classify inside-vs-outside operations to decode graph transformations
$\;y = -2f(3x - 6) + 1,\quad f \text{ has max at } (2,\,4)\;$
$\;\text{Inside: } 3(x-2)\Rightarrow x:\,2\to\tfrac{2}{3}+2=\tfrac{8}{3};\quad \text{Outside: } {-2}(\cdot)+1\Rightarrow y:\,4\to -2(4)+1=-7;\quad \text{new max }\bigl(\tfrac{8}{3},\,-7\bigr)\;$
1qtransformation parsing
Locate modulus V-vertex by zeroing the inner expression
$\;f(x) = |2x - 6| + 1\;$
$\;2x - 6 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 3,\quad f(3) = 0 + 1 = 1 \Rightarrow \text{vertex } (3,\,1)\;$
1qmodulus vertex finding
Divide polynomial by known linear factor via coefficient comparison
$\;x^3 + 2x^2 - 5x - 6 = (x+1)(Ax^2 + Bx + C)\;$
$\;A=1,\ C=-6,\ B+1=2 \Rightarrow B=1 \Rightarrow (x+1)(x^2+x-6)\;$
1qinspection division
Set denominator to zero, then verify numerator non-zero, to locate vertical asymptotes
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{x+1}{x-3}\;$
$\;x-3=0 \Rightarrow x=3,\quad N(3)=4\neq 0 \Rightarrow \text{VA: } x=3\;$
1qasymptote detection
Find x-intercepts of f to locate reflection region for y=|f(x)|
$\;f(x) = x^2 - 4\;$
$\;f(x)=0 \Rightarrow x=\pm 2;\quad f(x)<0 \text{ on } (-2,2) \Rightarrow |f(x)| \text{ reflects this interval upward}\;$
1qtransformation preparation
Compare numerator and denominator degrees to classify non-vertical asymptote
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{x^2 + 1}{x - 1}\;$
$\;\deg(P) - \deg(Q) = 1 \Rightarrow \dfrac{x^2+1}{x-1} = x + 1 + \dfrac{2}{x-1} \Rightarrow y = x+1\;$
1qdegree analysis
Compose independent x and y transformations into one coordinate mapping rule
$\;y = 2f(3x),\quad f\text{ passes through }(3,\,1)\;$
$\;(x,y)\to\!\left(\tfrac{x}{3},\,2y\right):\;(3,\,1)\to(1,\,2)\;$
1qcomposite mapping rule
Split a modulus inequality into two signed linear cases
$\;|2x+1| < x+3\;$
$\;x \ge -\tfrac{1}{2}:\; 2x+1 < x+3 \Rightarrow x<2;\quad x < -\tfrac{1}{2}:\; -(2x+1) < x+3 \Rightarrow x > -\tfrac{4}{3};\quad \text{union: } -\tfrac{4}{3} < x < 2\;$
1qcase split
Match transformed vertex coordinates to find stretch and shift parameters
$\;y = f(x)\text{ has vertex }(3,\,2);\quad y = af(x+b)\text{ has vertex }(-1,\,-6)\;$
$\;3 - b = -1 \Rightarrow b = 4;\quad 2a = -6 \Rightarrow a = -3\;$
1qgraph transformations
Test boundary parameter values to fix strict versus non-strict inequalities
$\;|x - 1| = kx,\quad k \in \{1,\, \tfrac{1}{2}\} \text{ (boundary candidates for 2 solutions)}\;$
$\;k=1:\; x-1=x \Rightarrow \text{no soln (one root only)} \Rightarrow k<1;\quad k=\tfrac{1}{2}:\; x=2,\;x=\tfrac{2}{3} \Rightarrow k\ge\tfrac{1}{2};\quad \boxed{\tfrac{1}{2}\le k<1}\;$
1qboundary case verification
Reflect intercepts in y = x to sketch the inverse graph
$\;f(x) = 3 - x,\quad \text{intercepts } (0,3),\;(3,0)\;$
$\;f^{-1}\!:\; (0,3)\to(3,0),\;(3,0)\to(0,3) \quad\text{(reflect in } y=x\text{)}\;$
1qgraphical inverse
Cross-multiply rational equation, then use discriminant to prove no real solutions
$\;\dfrac{3x}{x-2} = \dfrac{4}{x}\;$
$\;3x^2 - 4x + 8 = 0,\quad \Delta = 16 - 96 = -80 < 0 \Rightarrow \text{no real solutions}\;$
1qdiscriminant as proof
Convert |E| < c to the double inequality −c < E < c
$\;|2x - 3| < 5\;$
$\;-5 < 2x - 3 < 5 \Rightarrow -1 < x < 4\;$
1qmodulus inequality conversion
Validate candidate solutions against each case's domain interval
$\;|x - 3| = 2x \Rightarrow \text{Case 1 } (x \ge 3):\ x=3;\ \text{Case 2 } (x<3):\ x=1\;$
$\;x=3:\ 3 \ge 3\ \checkmark;\ x=1:\ 1<3\ \checkmark \Rightarrow \{1,\,3\}\;$
1qback checking
Exclude parameter value that collapses two solutions into one
$\;|x - 3| = k \Rightarrow x_1 = 3+k,\; x_2 = 3-k\;$
$\;3+k = 3-k \Rightarrow k=0;\; \text{so } k>0 \text{ for two distinct solutions}\;$
1qdistinctness enforcement
Decompose modulus graph via chain of transformations from y = |x|
$\;y = -2|x - 1| + 3\;$
$\;y = |x| \xrightarrow{x \to x-1} |x-1| \xrightarrow{\times(-2)} -2|x-1| \xrightarrow{+3} -2|x-1|+3 \Rightarrow \text{vertex } (1,3),\; x\text{-intercepts } x = -\tfrac{1}{2},\; \tfrac{5}{2},\; y\text{-intercept } y = 1\;$
1qtransformation sequencing
Factorise quadratic denominator to expose shared linear factor with LCD
$\;\dfrac{3x}{x^2+3x+2}-\dfrac{1}{x+1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{3x}{(x+1)(x+2)}-\dfrac{(x+2)}{(x+1)(x+2)}=\dfrac{3x-x-2}{(x+1)(x+2)}=\dfrac{2(x-1)}{(x+1)(x+2)}\;$
1qfactorise for lcd
Isolate the modulus before case-splitting
$\;x^2 - 4 = 5 - |x - 3|}\;$
$\;|x - 3| = 9 - x^2,\quad 9 - x^2 \ge 0\;$
1qmodulus isolation
Clear a compound fraction by multiplying top and bottom by the inner LCD
$\;\dfrac{\dfrac{1}{a} + 5}{\dfrac{3}{a} - 2}\;$
$\;\dfrac{a\!\left(\dfrac{1}{a} + 5\right)}{a\!\left(\dfrac{3}{a} - 2\right)} = \dfrac{1 + 5a}{3 - 2a}\;$
1qcompound fraction clearance
Collapse |f(x)| = 0 to the single equation f(x) = 0
$\;|3x - 6| = 0\;$
$\;3x - 6 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2\;$
1qmodulus zero collapse
Compare numerator and denominator degrees before partial fractions
$\;\dfrac{x^3 + 1}{(x+1)(x+2)}\;$
$\;\deg(\text{num})=3 \ge \deg(\text{den})=2 \Rightarrow \text{divide first: } x-3+\dfrac{7x+7}{(x+1)(x+2)}\;$
1qdegree check
Cross-multiply, collect x-terms, and factor to invert a linear-over-linear function
$\;y = \dfrac{2x}{x+1}\;$
$\;y(x+1)=2x \Rightarrow xy+y=2x \Rightarrow y=x(2-y) \Rightarrow f^{-1}(x)=\dfrac{x}{2-x}\;$
1qcross multiply and isolate
Factorise quadratic denominator into distinct linear factors for partial fractions
$\;\dfrac{3}{x^2+3x+2}\;$
$\;x^2+3x+2=(x+1)(x+2) \Rightarrow \dfrac{3}{(x+1)(x+2)}=\dfrac{A}{x+1}+\dfrac{B}{x+2}\;$
1qfactorisation for decomposition
Set up partial fraction template with repeated linear factor terms
$\;\dfrac{3x+1}{(x-1)^2(x+2)}\;$
$\;\dfrac{3x+1}{(x-1)^2(x+2)} = \dfrac{A}{x-1} + \dfrac{B}{(x-1)^2} + \dfrac{C}{x+2}\;$
1qpartial fraction template
Reduce improper rational function via polynomial long division before partial fractions
$\;\dfrac{x^3}{x^2 - 1}\;$
$\;x^3 \div (x^2-1) = x + \dfrac{x}{x^2-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{x^3}{x^2-1} = x + \dfrac{x}{x^2-1}\;$
1qimproper fraction reduction
Trace reciprocal-squared monotonicity to pin range endpoints
$\;f(x) = 3 - \dfrac{1}{(x+1)^2},\quad x \ge 0\;$
$\;f(0) = 2,\; f(x) \to 3^- \text{ as } x \to \infty \Rightarrow \text{range} = [2,\, 3)\;$
1qrange by monotonicity
Flip-and-cancel: convert algebraic fraction division into reciprocal multiplication
$\;\dfrac{x^2}{x+2} \div \dfrac{x}{x-1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{x^2}{x+2} \times \dfrac{x-1}{x} = \dfrac{x(x-1)}{x+2}\;$
1qfraction simplification
Clear denominators to reduce a rational equation to polynomial form
$\;\dfrac{6}{x} = x - 1,\quad x \neq 0\;$
$\;6 = x(x-1) \Rightarrow x^2 - x - 6 = 0 \Rightarrow (x-3)(x+2) = 0\;$
1qdenominator elimination
Use strict inequality when domain endpoint is excluded
$\;f(x) = |x| + 1,\quad 0 < x \le 2\;$
$\;f(0^+) \to 1 \text{ (not attained)},\ f(2)=3 \Rightarrow 1 < f(x) \le 3\;$
1qendpoint exclusion analysis
Validate each case solution against its own domain restriction
$\;|x - 3| = 2x \quad \Rightarrow \quad \text{Case 1 } (x<3):\, x=1;\quad \text{Case 2 } (x\ge3):\, x=\tfrac{3}{5}\;$
$\;x=1:\,1<3\;\checkmark\;\text{accept};\quad x=\tfrac{3}{5}:\,\tfrac{3}{5}\ge3\;\times\;\text{reject} \quad\Rightarrow\quad x=1\;$
1qdomain checking
Resolve ± in inverse function using range-equals-original-domain constraint
$\;f(x)=x^2-1,\; x\ge0 \Rightarrow x=y^2-1 \Rightarrow y=\pm\sqrt{x+1}\;$
$\;\text{range}(f^{-1})=[0,\infty)\Rightarrow y\ge0 \Rightarrow f^{-1}(x)=+\sqrt{x+1}\;$
1qsign selection via domain
Switch to quadratic formula once integer factorisation is ruled out
$\;x^2 + 3x + 1 = 0\;$
$\;\Delta = 9 - 4 = 5 \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{-3 \pm \sqrt{5}}{2}\;$
1qquadratic solution selection
Rewrite rational function by long division to expose asymptote
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{2x+3}{x-1}\;$
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{2(x-1)+5}{x-1} = 2 + \dfrac{5}{x-1} \Rightarrow y = 2\;$
1qalgebraic restructure
Collapse rational inequality using positive squared denominator
$\;\dfrac{x-2}{(x+1)^2} > 0\;$
$\;(x+1)^2 > 0\ (x \neq -1) \Rightarrow x - 2 > 0 \Rightarrow x > 2\;$
1qsign reduction
Isolate the exponential, then take ln to linearise
$\;e^{-3t} = \dfrac{1}{5}\;$
$\;-3t = \ln\!\left(\tfrac{1}{5}\right) = -\ln 5 \Rightarrow t = \dfrac{\ln 5}{3}\;$
1qlog extraction
Factor out common x and cancel using positive-domain constraint
$\;x^2 - 3x = 0,\quad x > 0\;$
$\;x(x - 3) = 0,\quad x \neq 0 \Rightarrow x = 3\;$
1qdomain justified cancellation
Back-substitute exponential/log relation to express derivative in required variable
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{2}{10^y \ln 10},\quad 10^y = 2x+1\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{2}{(2x+1)\ln 10}\;$
1qvariable conversion
Convert between model time variable and calendar date
$\;t = \text{years after 1 Jan 2000},\quad t = 3.25\;$
$\;\text{year} = 2000+3 = 2003,\quad 0.25 \times 12 = 3 \text{ months} \Rightarrow \text{1 Apr 2003}\;$
1qcontextual interpretation
Divide by dominant exponential to expose horizontal asymptote
$\;N = \dfrac{600e^{0.3t}}{2 + e^{0.3t}}\;$
$\;N = \dfrac{600}{2e^{-0.3t} + 1} \;\xrightarrow{t\to\infty}\; \dfrac{600}{0+1} = 600\;$
1qasymptotic normalisation
Divide exponentials to collapse two-term equation into one
$\;e^{3x} = 5e^{x}\;$
$\;\dfrac{e^{3x}}{e^{x}} = 5 \Rightarrow e^{2x} = 5 \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{\ln 5}{2}\;$
1qexponential combination
Factor out the common variable before splitting into cases
$\;x^3 - 4x = 0\;$
$\;x(x^2 - 4) = 0 \Rightarrow x = 0,\ x = \pm 2\;$
1qfactor and split
Assign independent decay clocks to each superimposed dose
$\;x_1 = 10e^{-0.1t},\quad \text{doses at } t_{\text{abs}}=0 \text{ and } t_{\text{abs}}=4;\quad t_{\text{abs}}=4+T\;$
$\;x = 10e^{-0.1(4+T)} + 10e^{-0.1T} = 10e^{-0.1T}\!\left(e^{-0.4}+1\right)\;$
1qmodelling setup
Split compound exponent to expose and factor a common exponential
$\;3^{2x+1} + 3^{2x} = 12\;$
$\;3 \cdot 3^{2x} + 3^{2x} = 12 \Rightarrow 3^{2x}(3+1) = 12 \Rightarrow 3^{2x} = 3\;$
1qexponent law factoring
Minimize a positive reciprocal by maximizing its denominator
$\;y = \dfrac{6}{2 + \cos\theta}\;$
$\;\cos\theta \le 1 \Rightarrow y_{\min} = \dfrac{6}{2+1} = 2\;$
1qreciprocal extremum
Negate both sides to make leading coefficient positive before factorising
$\;-x^2 + 3x + 4 = 0\;$
$\;x^2 - 3x - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow (x-4)(x+1) = 0\;$
1qsign normalisation
Map known stationary points through graph transformations instead of re-differentiating
$\;y = f(x) \text{ has stationary point } (1,\,3);\quad g(x) = 2f(x-4)+5\;$
$\;(1+4,\; 2(3)+5) = (5,\,11)\;$
1qtransformation of points
Take logarithms of both sides to linearise mismatched-base exponents
$\;2^x = 5\;$
$\;x \ln 2 = \ln 5 \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{\ln 5}{\ln 2}\;$
1qlogarithmic linearisation
Factorise quadratic over integers by inspection when coefficients are small
$\;2x^2 - 7x + 3 = 0\;$
$\;(2x - 1)(x - 3) = 0 \Rightarrow x = \tfrac{1}{2},\; x = 3\;$
1qfactorisation choice
Substitute into derived exponential model with rounding discipline
$\;N = 5 \times (1.2)^t,\quad t = 10\;$
$\;N = 5 \times (1.2)^{10} \approx 5 \times 6.192 \approx 31 \text{ (2 s.f.)}\;$
1qmodel evaluation
Treat transcendental constants as parameters to solve linearly for x
$\;2^{x+1} = 3^{x}\;$
$\;(x+1)\ln 2 = x\ln 3 \Rightarrow x(\ln 2 - \ln 3) = -\ln 2 \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{\ln 2}{\ln 3 - \ln 2}\;$
1qparameter as constant
Predict from the log-linear equation rather than the rounded exponential form
$\;\log_{10} P = 0.5 + 0.1\,t,\quad t = 8\;$
$\;\log_{10} P = 0.5 + 0.1(8) = 1.3 \Rightarrow P = 10^{1.3} \approx 20.0\;$
1qerror avoidance
Exponentiate both sides with base 10 to recover the variable from its logarithm
$\;\log_{10} x = 3\;$
$\;x = 10^{3} = 1000\;$
1qanti logarithm
Decompose exponential term using index laws to reveal quadratic structure
$\;2^{2x+1} - 7 \cdot 2^x + 3 = 0\;$
$\;u = 2^x,\; 2u^2 - 7u + 3 = 0 \Rightarrow (2u-1)(u-3)=0\;$
1qstructure recognition
Propagate known range through chained operations including reciprocal
$\;-5 \le f(\theta) \le 5,\quad g = \dfrac{2}{10 + f(\theta)}\;$
$\;5 \le 10+f \le 15 \Rightarrow \dfrac{1}{15} \le \dfrac{1}{10+f} \le \dfrac{1}{5} \Rightarrow \dfrac{2}{15} \le g \le \dfrac{2}{5}\;$
1qrange tracking
Take log of exponential model to linearise against given axes
$\;A = p q^t\;$
$\;\log_{10} A = \log_{10} p + t\log_{10} q \quad \Rightarrow \quad Y = (\log_{10} q)\,t + \log_{10} p\;$
1qlog linearization
Retain exact exponential forms through differentiation before final substitution
$\;A = 10^{0.2 + 0.3t},\quad t = 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{dA}{dt} = 0.3\ln 10 \cdot 10^{0.2+0.3t}\Big|_{t=1} = 0.3\ln 10 \cdot 10^{0.5} = 0.3\sqrt{10}\,\ln 10\;$
1qexact form retention
Combine logs then equate arguments to strip to power form
$\;\log_{10} M = 2\log_{10} r + 0.5\;$
$\;\log_{10} M = \log_{10}(10^{0.5}\, r^{2}) \Rightarrow M = 10^{0.5}\, r^{2} \approx 3.16\, r^{2}\;$
1qlog stripping
Divide numerator and denominator by highest power of t to evaluate rational limit at infinity
$\;\lim_{t\to\infty} \dfrac{5t}{3t+1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{5}{3+\tfrac{1}{t}} \;\xrightarrow{t\to\infty}\; \dfrac{5}{3}\;$
1qasymptotic limit
Solve algebraically for the reappearing integral after cyclic IBP
$\;I = e^x \sin x - e^x \cos x - I\;$
$\;2I = e^x(\sin x - \cos x) \Rightarrow I = \tfrac{1}{2}e^x(\sin x - \cos x) + C\;$
1qalgebraic rearrangement
Factor common power from denominator to cancel with numerator
$\;\dfrac{8u}{u^3 + 2u^2}\;$
$\;\dfrac{8u}{u^2(u+2)} = \dfrac{8}{u(u+2)}\;$
1qstrategic cancellation
Invert a volume/area formula to make the linear dimension the subject
$\;V = \tfrac{4}{3}\pi r^{3},\quad V = 32\pi\;$
$\;r^{3} = \dfrac{3V}{4\pi} = \dfrac{3(32\pi)}{4\pi} = 24 \Rightarrow r = \sqrt[3]{24} = 2\sqrt[3]{3}\;$
1qformula inversion
