Condense log difference into single fraction to match k ln(a/b) form
$\;3\ln\tfrac{1}{2} - 3\ln\tfrac{1}{5}\;$
$\;3\!\left[\ln\tfrac{1}{2} - \ln\tfrac{1}{5}\right] = 3\ln\dfrac{\,1/2\,}{1/5} = 3\ln\dfrac{5}{2}\;$
1qlogarithm manipulation
Factor out a common constant to simplify the integrand
$\;\int 6 - 6x\,dx\;$
$\;6\int (1 - x)\,dx = 6\!\left(x - \tfrac{x^2}{2}\right) + C\;$
1qconstant extraction
Factor out lowest power of common base to combine product-rule terms
$\;2x(x+1)^{1/2} + x^2 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}(x+1)^{-1/2}\;$
$\;x(x+1)^{-1/2}\bigl[2(x+1) + \tfrac{x}{2}\bigr] = \dfrac{x(5x+4)}{2\sqrt{x+1}}\;$
1qlowest power factorisation
Isolate the square root then square to match required squared form
$\;2\sqrt{A} = t^2 + 4\;$
$\;\sqrt{A} = \tfrac{1}{2}t^2 + 2 \Rightarrow A = \left(\tfrac{1}{2}t^2 + 2\right)^2\;$
1qform matching rearrangement
Rearrange implicit equation as a quadratic in x with y as parameter
$\;x^2 + xy + y^2 - 4 = 0\;$
$\;1\cdot x^2 + (y)\,x + (y^2 - 4) = 0\;$
1qvariable role assignment
Multiply through by LCM of denominators to obtain integer-coefficient form
$\;y - 1 = \tfrac{1}{3}(x - 2)\;$
$\;3(y - 1) = x - 2 \Rightarrow x - 3y + 1 = 0\;$
1qformat compliance
Condense ln(a) − ln(b) into ln(a/b) for final-form simplification
$\;\ln(3x) - \ln 3\;$
$\;\ln(3x) - \ln 3 = \ln\!\left(\dfrac{3x}{3}\right) = \ln x\;$
1qlogarithm condensation
Combine root substitution with coefficient comparison for partial fraction constants
$\;\frac{x^2}{(x-1)(x^2+1)} = \frac{A}{x-1} + \frac{Bx+C}{x^2+1}\;$
$\;x=1\Rightarrow A=\tfrac{1}{2};\quad \text{coeff of } x^2\colon 1=A+B \Rightarrow B=\tfrac{1}{2};\quad \text{coeff of } x^0\colon 0=-A+C \Rightarrow C=\tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qhybrid constant finding
Multiply numerator and denominator by −1 to match target sign arrangement
$\;\dfrac{-(x+y)}{x-2y}\;$
$\;\dfrac{(-1)(-(x+y))}{(-1)(x-2y)} = \dfrac{x+y}{2y-x}\;$
1qsign manipulation
Set discriminant to zero to eliminate x and solve for y
$\;x^2 + 2x + y^2 - 4y + 1 = 0 \quad \text{(quadratic in } x\text{)}\;$
$\;\Delta = 4 - 4(y^2 - 4y + 1) = 0 \Rightarrow y^2 - 4y = 0 \Rightarrow y(y-4)=0\;$
1qdiscriminant elimination
Spot a dependent equation to reduce a 3×2 system to an independent pair
$\;\text{Eq }1\!: \lambda + \mu = 2,\quad \text{Eq }2\!: -2\lambda - 2\mu = -4,\quad \text{Eq }3\!: 2\lambda - \mu = 1\;$
$\;\text{Eq }2 = -2\cdot\text{Eq }1 \Rightarrow \text{drop Eq }2;\quad \text{Eq }1 + \text{Eq }3\!: 3\lambda = 3 \Rightarrow \lambda=1,\ \mu=1\;$
1qdependency detection
Select only term-pairs whose exponents sum to the target power
$\;\text{Coeff of } x^2 \text{ in } (1+3x)(1+x)^5,\quad (1+x)^5 = 1+5x+10x^2+\cdots\;$
$\;1\cdot10 + 3\cdot5 = 25\;$
1qproduct coefficient selection
Multiply tangent/normal equation by t² to clear all fractional powers of t at once
$\;y - \dfrac{5}{t} = -\dfrac{1}{t^2}(x - 5t)\;$
$\;\times\, t^2:\quad t^2 y - 5t = -(x - 5t) \Rightarrow t^2 y + x = 10t\;$
1qstrategic multiplication
Multiply through by parameter to clear fraction and match target form
$\;y - 2at = \dfrac{1}{t}(x - at^2)\;$
$\;\times t:\quad ty - 2at^2 = x - at^2 \Rightarrow ty = x + at^2\;$
1qtarget driven rearrangement
Choose factorisation over the quadratic formula to solve
$\;x^2 - 5x + 6 = 0\;$
$\;(x-2)(x-3)=0 \Rightarrow x=2 \text{ or } x=3\;$
1qfactorisation to solve
Solve the single-unknown equation first to decouple the system
$\;(1)\; x + y = 5,\quad (2)\; 2x = 6\;$
$\;(2)\Rightarrow x = 3,\quad (1)\Rightarrow y = 5 - 3 = 2\;$
1qstrategic equation ordering
Combine rational terms over a common denominator for an exact fraction
$\;2 + \dfrac{1}{3} - \dfrac{1}{9}\;$
$\;\dfrac{18}{9} + \dfrac{3}{9} - \dfrac{1}{9} = \dfrac{20}{9}\;$
1qarithmetic consolidation
Multiply through by parameter to clear fractional coefficient and match target form
$\;y - 4t = \dfrac{1}{t}(x - 2t^2)\;$
$\;t(y - 4t) = x - 2t^2 \Rightarrow ty = x + 2t^2\;$
1qstrategic rearrangement
Cancel a common parametric factor to isolate a coordinate
$\;-2t = -t(x - t^2),\quad t \neq 0\;$
$\;\div(-t):\quad 2 = x - t^2 \Rightarrow x = t^2 + 2\;$
1qparameter cancellation
Multiply through by the denominator to match the show-that target form
$\;y - 2a t = \dfrac{1}{t}(x - a t^2)\;$
$\;\times t:\quad ty - 2at^2 = x - at^2 \Rightarrow ty = x + at^2\;$
1qtarget form manipulation
Subtract paired parametric equations and factor symmetric difference
$\;x(p-q) = 2(p^3 - q^3) + 4(p-q)\;$
$\;(p-q)\bigl[2(p^2+pq+q^2)+4\bigr] \div (p-q) = 2(p^2+pq+q^2)+4\;$
1qsymmetric elimination
Classify monic versus non-monic to set factorisation strategy
$\;x^2 + 5x + 6 \quad\text{vs}\quad 2x^2 + 5x + 3\;$
$\;a=1\Rightarrow (x+2)(x+3);\quad a=2\neq1\Rightarrow (2x+3)(x+1)\;$
1qproblem classification
Clear denominators by multiplying through by the LCM
$\;\dfrac{x}{2} - \dfrac{x}{3} = 1\;$
$\;3x - 2x = 6 \Rightarrow x = 6\;$
1qscaling for integrality
Absorb leading coefficient into fractional factor to clear denominators before expanding
$\;2\left(x + \tfrac{1}{2}\right)(x - 3)\;$
$\;2\left(x + \tfrac{1}{2}\right) = 2x + 1 \Rightarrow (2x+1)(x-3)\;$
1qstrategic distribution
Define f(x) and apply change-of-sign rule on a closed interval
$\;f(x) = x^3 - x - 1,\quad [1,\,2]\;$
$\;f(1) = -1 < 0,\quad f(2) = 5 > 0 \Rightarrow \exists\;\alpha \in (1,\,2)\;$
1qroot existence proof
Combine reciprocal-paired new roots over common denominator αβ
$\;S = \alpha+\beta = 5,\; P = \alpha\beta = 2,\; S' = \dfrac{\alpha}{\beta}+\dfrac{\beta}{\alpha} = \dfrac{\alpha^2+\beta^2}{\alpha\beta}\;$
$\;S' = \dfrac{S^2-2P}{P} = \dfrac{25-4}{2} = \dfrac{21}{2},\; P' = 1 \Rightarrow x^2 - \tfrac{21}{2}x + 1 = 0\;$
1qalgebraic restructuring
Combine rational root expressions over common denominator to expose symmetric functions
$\;x^2 - 5x + 6 = 0,\quad S' = \dfrac{\alpha}{\beta} + \dfrac{\beta}{\alpha} = \dfrac{\alpha^2 + \beta^2}{\alpha\beta}\;$
$\;\dfrac{\sigma_1^2 - 2\sigma_2}{\sigma_2} = \dfrac{25 - 12}{6} = \dfrac{13}{6}\;$
1qalgebraic recombination
Extract pq before p+q when Vieta's gives reciprocal-root data
$\;3x^2 - 5x + 1 = 0 \text{ has roots } \tfrac{1}{p},\, \tfrac{1}{q}\;$
$\;\frac{1}{pq} = \frac{1}{3} \Rightarrow pq = 3,\quad p+q = \frac{4}{5} \cdot pq = \frac{5}{3} \cdot 3 = 5\;$
1qvieta's inversion
Extract sum and product of roots via Vieta's formulas
$\;x^2 - 5x + 6 = 0,\quad \text{roots } \alpha,\beta\;$
$\;\alpha + \beta = \tfrac{5}{1} = 5,\quad \alpha\beta = \tfrac{6}{1} = 6\;$
1qvieta's forward
Carry full precision through Newton-Raphson iterations until rounded values agree
$\;f(x)=\cos x - 2x,\quad x_1 = 0.346520\!\ldots\;$
$\;x_2 = x_1 - \frac{f(x_1)}{f'(x_1)} = 0.347432\!\ldots;\quad x_1 \approx 0.347,\; x_2 \approx 0.347 \Rightarrow \alpha = 0.347\ (3\text{ d.p.})\;$
1qconvergence criterion
Factor cubic as known quadratic times unknown linear and equate coefficients
$\;f(z) = z^3 + 2z^2 + 5z + 10,\quad z^2 + 5 \text{ is a factor}\;$
$\;z^3 + 2z^2 + 5z + 10 \equiv (z^2+5)(z+m)\Rightarrow z^3 + mz^2 + 5z + 5m \Rightarrow m=2\;$
1qequating coefficients
Expand symmetric denominator and reduce power sums via Newton's identity
$\;p+q=3,\; pq=2:\quad (1+p^2)(1+q^2)=1+(p^2+q^2)+(pq)^2\;$
$\;p^2+q^2=(3)^2-2(2)=5,\quad 1+5+4=10\;$
1qnewton identity reduction
Spot reciprocal-paired transformed roots whose product collapses to a constant
$\;\text{Roots of } x^2 - 3x + k = 0 \text{ are } \alpha,\beta;\quad \text{new roots } \tfrac{2\alpha}{\beta},\, \tfrac{2\beta}{\alpha}\;$
$\;\frac{2\alpha}{\beta}\cdot\frac{2\beta}{\alpha} = 4 \Rightarrow \frac{k}{1} = 4 \Rightarrow k = 4\;$
1qtelescoping simplification
Form new quadratic from sum and product of transformed roots
$\;x^2 - 3x + 1 = 0 \text{ has roots } \alpha,\beta;\quad \text{new roots } \tfrac{\alpha}{\beta},\, \tfrac{\beta}{\alpha}\;$
$\;S = \dfrac{\alpha^2+\beta^2}{\alpha\beta} = \dfrac{(3)^2-2(1)}{1} = 7,\quad P = 1 \Rightarrow x^2 - 7x + 1 = 0\;$
1qnew equation construction
Factor mixed-degree symmetric numerator by grouping into (p+q)(1+pq)
$\;p + q + p^2q + pq^2\;$
$\;(p+q) + pq(p+q) = (p+q)(1+pq)\;$
1qsymmetric polynomial reduction
Bridge two quadratics via Vieta's on both sides
$\;\alpha,\beta \text{ roots of } x^2 + 3x + 2 = 0;\quad 2\alpha,\,2\beta \text{ roots of } x^2 + bx + c = 0\;$
$\;b = -(2\alpha+2\beta) = -2(\!-3) = 6,\quad c = 4\alpha\beta = 4(2) = 8\;$
1qvieta's bridge
Confirm an ambiguous function expression by matching table values
$\;f(x)=x^2-3x+1,\quad \text{table: } f(2)=-1,\; f(3)=1\;$
$\;f(2)=4-6+1=-1\;\checkmark,\quad f(3)=9-9+1=1\;\checkmark\;$
1qfunction reconstruction
Combine transformed-root expressions over αβ to decompose into known power sums
$\;\alpha+\beta=3,\;\alpha\beta=2;\quad S=\frac{\alpha^3+\beta^3+\alpha+\beta}{\alpha\beta},\; P=\frac{(\alpha\beta)^2+\alpha^2+\beta^2+1}{\alpha\beta}\;$
$\;\alpha^2+\beta^2=5,\;\alpha^3+\beta^3=9 \Rightarrow S=\frac{9+3}{2}=6,\; P=\frac{4+5+1}{2}=5\;$
1qsymmetric decomposition
Sanity-check root parsing when transformed-roots answer looks unusually ugly
$\;\alpha+\beta=5,\;\alpha\beta=4;\;\text{new roots }\tfrac{\alpha}{\beta},\;\tfrac{\beta}{\alpha}\;\Rightarrow\;\text{sum}=\tfrac{\alpha^2+\beta^2}{\alpha\beta}=\tfrac{17}{4}\;$
$\;\text{If instead sum}=\tfrac{-17}{29},\;\text{re-parse as }\alpha-\beta,\;\beta-\alpha:\;\text{sum}=0,\;\text{product}=-(\alpha-\beta)^2=-(25-16)=-9\;\checkmark\;$
1qdiagnostic verification
Reverse substitution and clear compound fractions by scaling
$\;z = \dfrac{1}{y^2},\quad z = \dfrac{x}{2} + \dfrac{1}{4} + Ce^{x}\;$
$\;y^2 = \dfrac{1}{\frac{x}{2} + \frac{1}{4} + Ce^{x}} = \dfrac{4}{2x + 1 + Ae^{x}}\;$
1qsubstitution reversal
Recognise difference of squares to collapse a conjugate product
$\;(x+3)(x-3)\;$
$\;(x+3)(x-3) = x^2 - 9\;$
1qalgebraic recognition
Refactor exponential coefficients to match target base-power form
$\;12 \cdot 2^k - 18 \cdot 3^k\;$
$\;3 \cdot 2^2 \cdot 2^k - 2 \cdot 3^2 \cdot 3^k = 3 \cdot 2^{k+2} - 2 \cdot 3^{k+2}\;$
1qexponential regrouping
Solve self-referencing equation by treating the integral as an algebraic unknown
$\;I_n = (n-1)I_{n-2} - (n-1)I_n\;$
$\;I_n + (n-1)I_n = (n-1)I_{n-2} \Rightarrow I_n = \dfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2}\;$
1qalgebraic isolation
Divide by cosh to isolate tanh, then apply artanh logarithmic form
$\;3\cosh x = 5\sinh x\;$
$\;\tanh x = \dfrac{3}{5} \Rightarrow x = \dfrac{1}{2}\ln\!\left(\dfrac{1+\frac{3}{5}}{1-\frac{3}{5}}\right) = \dfrac{1}{2}\ln 4 = \ln 2\;$
1qratio to inverse hyperbolic
Factor expression to match a prescribed template form
$\;6x^3 + 4x^2 = 2x^2(px + q)\;$
$\;2x^2 \cdot 3x + 2x^2 \cdot 2 = 2x^2(3x+2) \Rightarrow p=3,\ q=2\;$
1qreverse engineer form
Expand compound hyperbolic argument using part (a) identity
$\;\cosh(x+\ln 2) = 5\sinh x\;$
$\;\tfrac{5}{4}\cosh x + \tfrac{3}{4}\sinh x = 5\sinh x \Rightarrow \tanh x = \tfrac{5}{17}\;$
1quse earlier result
Collect self-referencing integral on one side and divide to isolate
$\;I_n = (n-1)I_{n-2} - (n-1)I_n\;$
$\;I_n + (n-1)I_n = (n-1)I_{n-2} \Rightarrow I_n = \dfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2}\;$
1qcollect and isolate
Multiply and divide paired equations to decouple product-quotient unknowns
$\;xy = 12,\quad \dfrac{x}{y} = 3\;$
$\;x^2 = 12 \cdot 3 = 36 \Rightarrow x = 6,\quad y^2 = \dfrac{12}{3} = 4 \Rightarrow y = 2\;$
1qproduct quotient elimination
Factor constant out of modulus to simplify a fraction
$\;\dfrac{|6x - 3|}{4}\;$
$\;\dfrac{3|2x - 1|}{4}\;$
1qmodulus factoring
Replace hyperbolic functions with their exponential definitions
$\;\cosh x + \sinh x\;$
$\;\dfrac{e^x + e^{-x}}{2} + \dfrac{e^x - e^{-x}}{2} = e^x\;$
1qdefinition substitution
Square both sides to eliminate paired moduli and reduce to a quadratic
$\;|x+1| = 2|x-1|\;$
$\;(x+1)^2 = 4(x-1)^2 \Rightarrow 3x^2 - 10x + 3 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 3,\; x = \tfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qsquaring to remove moduli
Combine 1 + (dy/dx)² over a common denominator to collapse the arc-length radical
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{1}{2\sqrt{x}},\quad x > 0\;$
$\;1 + \left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2 = 1 + \dfrac{1}{4x} = \dfrac{4x+1}{4x} \Rightarrow \sqrt{\dfrac{4x+1}{4x}} = \dfrac{\sqrt{4x+1}}{2\sqrt{x}}\;$
1qintegrand simplification
Square both sides to clear modulus and surds in an angle/cosine equation
$\;\cos\theta = \dfrac{|2a+b|}{\sqrt{5}\,\sqrt{a^2+b^2}},\quad \sin\theta = \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{5}}\;$
$\;\dfrac{(2a+b)^2}{5(a^2+b^2)} = \dfrac{4}{5} \Rightarrow 4ab - 3b^2 = 0 \Rightarrow b(4a-3b)=0\;$
1qsquaring strategy
Multiply through by the denominator factor to clear a parametric gradient
$\;y - 2\sin\theta = \dfrac{\sin\theta}{\cos\theta}(x - 3\cos\theta)\;$
$\;y\cos\theta - 2\sin\theta\cos\theta = x\sin\theta - 3\sin\theta\cos\theta \Rightarrow x\sin\theta - y\cos\theta = \sin\theta\cos\theta\;$
1qstrategic clearing
Match expression to standard binomial series form (1+u)^n
$\;(1+3x)^{-2}\;$
$\;n=-2,\; u=3x:\quad 1 + (-2)(3x) + \dfrac{(-2)(-3)}{2!}(3x)^2 + \cdots = 1 - 6x + 27x^2 + \cdots,\;|x|<\tfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qtemplate matching
Apply generalised binomial expansion for fractional or negative powers
$\;(1+x)^{-1}\;$
$\;(1+x)^{-1} = 1 - x + x^2 - x^3 + \cdots,\quad |x|<1\;$
1qtemplate matching
Map expression to (1+y)^n template for binomial expansion
$\;(1 - 2x)^5,\quad n=5,\ y=-2x\;$
$\;1 + 5(-2x) + \tfrac{5 \cdot 4}{2}(-2x)^2 + \cdots = 1 - 10x + 40x^2 - \cdots\;$
1qtemplate matching
Apply binomial theorem directly in (a+b)^n form
$\;(1 + 2x)^4\;$
$\;\binom{4}{0}1^4 + \binom{4}{1}1^3(2x) + \binom{4}{2}1^2(2x)^2 + \binom{4}{3}1(2x)^3 + \binom{4}{4}(2x)^4 = 1 + 8x + 24x^2 + 32x^3 + 16x^4\;$
1qtemplate matching
Collect only required low-order terms from a polynomial-times-series product
$\;f(x) = (1+2x)(1+x)^{1/2},\quad \text{find coefficient of } x\;$
$\;(1+x)^{1/2} = 1 + \tfrac{1}{2}x + \cdots \Rightarrow [x]:\; 1\cdot\tfrac{1}{2} + 2\cdot 1 = \tfrac{5}{2}\;$
1qtargeted product collection
Treat composite second term as single unit in binomial expansion
$\;(1+3x)^4\;$
$\;T_{r+1}=\binom{4}{r}(3x)^r \Rightarrow 1+12x+54x^2+\cdots\;$
1qcomposite term identification
Target a single power via the binomial general term
$\;(1 + 2x)^5,\quad \text{coeff of } x^3\;$
$\;T_{4} = \binom{5}{3}(1)^{2}(2x)^{3} = 10 \cdot 8\,x^{3} = 80x^{3}\;$
1qgeneral term targeting
Evaluate binomial coefficients using the falling-factorial shortcut
$\;\dbinom{8}{3}\;$
$\;\dfrac{8 \times 7 \times 6}{3!} = \dfrac{336}{6} = 56\;$
1qcoefficient computation
Apply binomial theorem directly to a two-term base with positive integer exponent
$\;(1 + x)^4\;$
$\;\binom{4}{0} + \binom{4}{1}x + \binom{4}{2}x^2 + \binom{4}{3}x^3 + \binom{4}{4}x^4 = 1 + 4x + 6x^2 + 4x^3 + x^4\;$
1qdirect binomial expansion
Cancel shared powers of 2 between coefficient and denominator before multiplying
$\;\binom{6}{r} \cdot 2^{6-r} \cdot \left(\dfrac{x}{4}\right)^r = \binom{6}{r} \cdot \dfrac{2^{6-r}}{4^r} \cdot x^r\;$
$\;\dfrac{2^{6-r}}{4^r} = \dfrac{2^{6-r}}{2^{2r}} = 2^{6-3r}\;$
1qarithmetic simplification
Determine over/underestimate by checking sign of omitted binomial tail terms
$\;(1+x)^{6},\quad x=0.1,\quad \text{terms up to } r=2: \; 1+6(0.1)+15(0.01)=1.75\;$
$\;r=3,\dots,6:\; \tbinom{6}{r}(0.1)^r > 0 \;\Rightarrow\; \text{all omitted terms positive} \;\Rightarrow\; \text{underestimate}\;$
1qtruncation error analysis
Absorb the minus sign into b when matching (a+b)^n
$\;(1 - x)^5\;$
$\;T_{r+1} = \binom{5}{r}(1)^{5-r}(-x)^r = \binom{5}{r}(-1)^r x^r\;$
1qparameter identification
Extend binomial expansion one term beyond the stated requirement
$\;\dfrac{1}{x}(1+x)^5,\quad \text{expand to } x^2\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{x}\cdot\binom{5}{3}x^3 = \tfrac{1}{x}\cdot 10x^3 = 10x^2\;$
1qexpansion extension
Match x-powers across a linear-times-expansion product to isolate one term
$\;(2x+1)(1+x)^5,\quad (1+x)^5 = 1 + 5x + 10x^2 + \cdots\;$
$\;\text{coeff of } x^2\!: \ 2 \cdot [x^1] + 1 \cdot [x^2] = 2(5) + 1(10) = 20\;$
1qterm selection
Pair only the cross-terms that hit the target power
$\;(3+2x)(1+x)^3,\quad \text{coeff of } x^2\;$
$\;3\cdot\binom{3}{2}x^2 + 2x\cdot\binom{3}{1}x \Rightarrow 3(3)+2(3)=15\;$
1qselective multiplication
Bundle negative sign and fractional coefficient into a single substitution variable
$\;(1 - \tfrac{x}{3})^6,\quad y = -\tfrac{x}{3}\;$
$\;1 + \binom{6}{1}y + \binom{6}{2}y^2 = 1 + 6\!\left(-\tfrac{x}{3}\right) + 15\!\left(\tfrac{x^2}{9}\right) = 1 - 2x + \tfrac{5x^2}{3}\;$
1qsign management
Translate |X|<1 binomial convergence into an interval for x
$\;(1+3x)^{-1}\;$
$\;|3x|<1 \Rightarrow |x|<\dfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qconvergence domain
Extract a specific term using the general-term formula C(n,r)y^r
$\;\text{Find the coefficient of } x^2 \text{ in } (1+x)^5\;$
$\;T_{r+1} = \binom{5}{r}x^r,\; r=2 \Rightarrow \binom{5}{2}x^2 = 10x^2\;$
1qdirect term extraction
Distribute prefactor and match x-powers to isolate the constant term
$\;\left(\frac{1}{x}+\frac{2}{x^2}\right)\!\left(1+\frac{x}{3}\right)^{6}\;$
$\;\frac{1}{x}:\,r=1\;\Rightarrow\;\binom{6}{1}\frac{1}{3}=2;\quad \frac{2}{x^2}:\,r=2\;\Rightarrow\;2\binom{6}{2}\frac{1}{9}=\frac{10}{3};\quad \text{sum}=\frac{16}{3}\;$
1qpower matching
State validity of binomial expansion via |u| < 1
$\;(1 + 3x)^{-2}\;$
$\;|3x| < 1 \Rightarrow |x| < \tfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qvalidity condition
Separate sign, coefficient, and variable when expanding (a+bx)^n with composite X
$\;(1 - 2x)^{-2}\;$
$\;1 + (-2)(-2x) + \tfrac{(-2)(-3)}{2!}(4x^2) + \tfrac{(-2)(-3)(-4)}{3!}(-8x^3) = 1 + 4x + 12x^2 + 32x^3 + \cdots\;$
1qcomposite substitution bookkeeping
Reshape fraction-to-power into constant times (1+u)^n template
$\;\left(\dfrac{1}{2+x}\right)^3\;$
$\;\dfrac{1}{(2+x)^3} = \dfrac{1}{8}\left(1+\dfrac{x}{2}\right)^{-3}\;$
1qstandard form preparation
Defer scalar multiplication until after term-by-term binomial expansion
$\;3(1+x)^{-1}\;$
$\;(1+x)^{-1} = 1 - x + x^2 - \cdots \Rightarrow 3(1 - x + x^2 - \cdots) = 3 - 3x + 3x^2 - \cdots\;$
1qdeferred distribution
Binomial-expand (z+z^{-1})^n and pair symmetric powers to linearise cos^n θ
$\;16\cos^4\theta = (z+z^{-1})^4 = z^4 + 4z^2 + 6 + 4z^{-2} + z^{-4}\;$
$\;(z^4+z^{-4}) + 4(z^2+z^{-2}) + 6 = 2\cos4\theta + 8\cos2\theta + 6 \Rightarrow \cos^4\theta = \tfrac{1}{8}(\cos4\theta + 4\cos2\theta + 3)\;$
1qlinearisation via binomial
Choose x to link binomial series to target surd
$\;(1+x)^{1/2} \approx 1 + \tfrac{x}{2} - \tfrac{x^2}{8},\quad |x|<1\;$
$\;\sqrt{2} = (1+1)^{1/2}:\; x=1 \text{ fails } |x|<1;\quad \sqrt{\tfrac{3}{2}} = \left(1+\tfrac{1}{2}\right)^{1/2}:\; x=\tfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow 1+\tfrac{1}{4}-\tfrac{1}{32} = \tfrac{39}{32}\;$
1qreverse engineer substitution
Expand (1+u)^n as generalized binomial series for fractional/negative n
$\;(1+x)^{-1}\;$
$\;1 + (-1)x + \dfrac{(-1)(-2)}{2!}x^2 + \cdots = 1 - x + x^2 - \cdots\;$
1qseries generation
Factor out leading constant to reach (1+X)^n standard form
$\;(2+x)^{-1}\;$
$\;[2(1+\tfrac{x}{2})]^{-1} = \tfrac{1}{2}\left(1+\tfrac{x}{2}\right)^{-1}\;$
1qbinomial standardisation
Rewrite quotient as product to reuse a binomial expansion
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{1+3x}{(1+x)^2},\quad (1+x)^{-2} = 1 - 2x + 3x^2 - \dots\;$
$\;f(x) = (1+3x)(1-2x+3x^2-\dots) = 1 + x - 3x^2 + \dots\;$
1qalgebraic restructuring
Choose expanded polynomial form over factored form before differentiating
$\;f(x) = (x-1)(x-3) = x^2 - 4x + 3\;$
$\;f'(x) = 2x - 4\;$
1qimplicit differentiation
Differentiate implicitly, attaching dy/dx to every y-term via chain rule
$\;x^2 + xy + y^2 = 7\;$
$\;2x + y + x\dfrac{dy}{dx} + 2y\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{-(2x+y)}{x+2y}\;$
1qimplicit differentiation
Choose quotient rule over logarithmic differentiation when iterating derivatives
$\;y = \dfrac{\sqrt{1+\ln x}}{x}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{\frac{1}{2x\sqrt{1+\ln x}}\cdot x - \sqrt{1+\ln x}\cdot 1}{x^2} = \dfrac{1 - 2(1+\ln x)}{2x^2\sqrt{1+\ln x}}\;$
1qimplicit differentiation
Apply product rule to polynomial-times-exponential with internal chain rules
$\;f(x) = (x-2)^2\, e^{3x}\;$
$\;f'(x) = 2(x-2)e^{3x} + 3(x-2)^2 e^{3x} = (x-2)(3x-4)\,e^{3x}\;$
1qproduct rule selection
Differentiate parametrically instead of eliminating the parameter
$\;x = t^2,\quad y = t^3\;$
$\;\frac{dy}{dx} = \frac{dy/dt}{dx/dt} = \frac{3t^2}{2t} = \frac{3t}{2}\;$
1qparametric differentiation
Differentiate quadratic and solve dy/dx = 0 to locate vertex
$\;y = x^2 - 4x + 7\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2,\; y = 3 \Rightarrow \text{min } (2,\,3)\;$
1qstationary point condition
Find range via interior minimum when both endpoints diverge to +∞
$\;f(x) = x + \dfrac{4}{x},\quad x > 0\;$
$\;f'(x) = 1 - \dfrac{4}{x^2} = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2,\quad f(2) = 4 \Rightarrow \text{range } [4,\,\infty)\;$
1qstationary point condition
Differentiate composite trig via chain rule and set derivative to zero
$\;y = \sin(2x) + x\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2\cos(2x) + 1 = 0 \Rightarrow \cos(2x) = -\tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qstationary point condition
Bridge volume and depth rates via chain rule dh/dt = (dV/dt)/(dV/dh)
$\;V = 9\pi h,\quad \dfrac{dV}{dt} = 3\pi\;$
$\;\dfrac{dh}{dt} = \dfrac{dV/dt}{dV/dh} = \dfrac{3\pi}{9\pi} = \dfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qchain rule
Differentiate (dy/dx)² via chain rule as 2y'·y''
$\;\dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2\;$
$\;2\,\dfrac{dy}{dx}\cdot\dfrac{d^2y}{dx^2}\;$
1qchain rule
Evaluate derivative at given x to obtain gradient at a point
$\;y = x^3 - 2x,\quad x = 2\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 - 2 \;\Rightarrow\; \left.\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right|_{x=2} = 3(4) - 2 = 10\;$
1qgradient evaluation
Invert dy/dx to get dx/dy via reciprocal identity
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{3x^2}{2}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dx}{dy} = \dfrac{1}{\,3x^2/2\,} = \dfrac{2}{3x^2}\;$
1qreciprocal derivative
Differentiate inverse trig via x = sin(y) form and reciprocate
$\;y = \arcsin x \Rightarrow x = \sin y\;$
$\;\dfrac{dx}{dy} = \cos y \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{1}{\cos y} = \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{1 - x^2}}\;$
1qreciprocal derivative
Convert 'f is increasing' into the inequality f'(x) > 0
$\;f(x) = x^3 - 3x\;$
$\;f'(x) = 3x^2 - 3 > 0 \Rightarrow 3(x-1)(x+1) > 0 \Rightarrow x < -1 \text{ or } x > 1\;$
1qsign analysis
Sign-analyze derivative components to conclude monotonicity
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{6x}{x+1},\quad x > 0\;$
$\;f'(x) = \dfrac{6}{(x+1)^2},\quad 6>0,\ (x+1)^2>0 \Rightarrow f'(x)>0 \Rightarrow f \text{ increasing}\;$
1qsign analysis
Reduce fraction-equals-zero to numerator-equals-zero via positive denominator
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{1 - 2x}{(1+x^2)^2}\;$
$\;(1+x^2)^2 > 0\ \forall x \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx}=0 \iff 1-2x=0 \iff x=\tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qsign analysis
Classify a stationary point via first-derivative sign change
$\;f'(x) = (x-1)(x-3),\quad x_0 = 1\;$
$\;f'(0)=(-)(-) > 0,\; f'(2)=(+)(-)< 0 \Rightarrow +\to -\Rightarrow \text{local max at } x=1\;$
1qsign analysis
Deduce monotonicity of f∘f from sign of f' via chain rule
$\;f'(x)<0 \text{ on } (0,\infty),\; f:(0,\infty)\to(0,\infty)\;$
$\;(f\circ f)'(x)=f'(f(x))\cdot f'(x)=(-)(-)>0 \Rightarrow f\circ f \text{ strictly increasing on } (0,\infty)\;$
1qsign analysis
Discard strictly-positive factors when solving product = 0
$\;f'(x) = 3e^{2x}(x-1)(x+2)\;$
$\;e^{2x} > 0\ \forall x \Rightarrow f'(x)=0 \iff (x-1)(x+2)=0 \iff x=1,\,-2\;$
1qsign analysis
Set derivative equal to given gradient to locate tangent point
$\;y = x^2 - 3x,\quad \text{gradient } = 5\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x - 3 = 5 \Rightarrow x = 4,\; y = 4 \Rightarrow (4,\,4)\;$
1qgradient condition
Differentiate polynomial and evaluate to find tangent gradient at a point
$\;y = x^2 + 3x,\quad P(2,\,10)\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x + 3 \Rightarrow \left.\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right|_{x=2} = 7\;$
1qpower rule evaluation
Apply the power rule directly to fractional and negative exponents
$\;f(x) = 3x^{1/2} + x^{-1}\;$
$\;f'(x) = \tfrac{3}{2}x^{-1/2} - x^{-2}\;$
1qpower rule extension
Expand factored polynomial before differentiating term by term
$\;f(x) = (x-1)(x+2)(x+3)\;$
$\;(x-1)(x^2+5x+6) = x^3+4x^2+x-6 \Rightarrow f'(x)=3x^2+8x+1\;$
1qform conversion for power rule
Split polynomial-over-power-of-x fraction into separate x^n terms before differentiating
$\;y = \dfrac{x^3 + 2x}{x^2}\;$
$\;y = x + 2x^{-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 1 - 2x^{-2}\;$
1qalgebraic preparation
Exploit that additive constants vanish under differentiation to bypass unknowns
$\;y = x^2 - 4x + k\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2\;$
1qparameter elimination via differentiation
Read tangent form y = k as a zero-gradient condition
$\;f(x) = x^2 - 2x + 3,\quad x = 1\;$
$\;f'(1) = 2(1)-2 = 0 \Rightarrow \text{tangent: } y = f(1) = 2\;$
1qtangent form interpretation
Differentiate the first derivative to obtain the second derivative
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 - 4x + 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{d^2y}{dx^2} = 6x - 4\;$
1qsequential differentiation
Equate derivative to line's gradient to locate tangent point
$\;y = x^2,\quad y = 2x + c\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x = 2 \Rightarrow x = 1,\ y = 1,\ c = 1 - 2 = -1\;$
1qtangency gradient match
Substitute the given x-value into both derivatives, then equate to solve for the parameter
$\;f(x) = kx^3 + x^2 - kx. \text{ Given that } f'(2) = f''(2), \text{ find } k.\;$
$\;f'(2) = 12k + 4 - k = 11k + 4,\; f''(2) = 12k + 2 \Rightarrow 11k + 4 = 12k + 2 \Rightarrow k = 2\;$
1qparameter determination
Equate f'(x) and f''(x) generally to form a quadratic in x
$\;f(x)=x^3-3x^2+2x \Rightarrow f'(x)=3x^2-6x+2,\quad f''(x)=6x-6\;$
$\;3x^2-6x+2=6x-6 \Rightarrow 3x^2-12x+8=0\;$
1qderivative equation formation
Substitute given x-value into derivative to verify stationary point
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x^2 - 8,\quad x = 2\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx}\bigg|_{x=2} = 2(2)^2 - 8 = 8 - 8 = 0\;$
1qverify by substitution
Differentiate the simplified show-that form, not the original expression
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{5x}{x+3}\;$
$\;f'(x) = \dfrac{(x+3)(5) - (5x)(1)}{(x+3)^2} = \dfrac{15}{(x+3)^2}\;$
1qstrategic form selection
Differentiate or integrate term-by-term using linearity on a sum of power terms
$\;y = 3x^2 - x^{-1}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3\cdot 2\,x^{1} - (-1)x^{-2} = 6x + x^{-2}\;$
1qlinearity decomposition
Evaluate derivative at given x-values to disprove stationarity
$\;f'(x) = 2x + 3\;$
$\;f'(1) = 2(1)+3 = 5 \neq 0,\quad f'(-2) = 2(-2)+3 = -1 \neq 0 \Rightarrow \text{not stationary}\;$
1qcounter example by evaluation
Rewrite constant-over-linear as negative power before differentiating
$\;y = \dfrac{4}{(2x+1)^2}\;$
$\;y = 4(2x+1)^{-2} \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 4(-2)(2x+1)^{-3}\cdot 2 = -\dfrac{16}{(2x+1)^3}\;$
1qalgebraic preprocessing
Differentiate exponential model and evaluate derivative as instantaneous rate
$\;\theta = 50 - 30e^{-2t}\;$
$\;\dfrac{d\theta}{dt} = 60e^{-2t},\quad \left.\dfrac{d\theta}{dt}\right|_{t=1} = 60e^{-2}\;$
1qphysical interpretation of derivative
Extract common bracket from quotient-rule numerator to fully factorise
$\;f(x) = \dfrac{(x+1)^2}{x-2},\quad f'(x) = \dfrac{(x-2)\cdot 2(x+1) - (x+1)^2}{(x-2)^2}\;$
$\;\dfrac{(x+1)\bigl[2(x-2)-(x+1)\bigr]}{(x-2)^2} = \dfrac{(x+1)(x-5)}{(x-2)^2}\;$
1qstructured factorisation
Factor common power before solving derivative equal to zero
$\;y = x(x-1)^3 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = (x-1)^3 + 3x(x-1)^2\;$
$\;(x-1)^2[(x-1)+3x] = (x-1)^2(4x-1) = 0 \Rightarrow x=1,\; x=\tfrac{1}{4}\;$
1qfactor before solving
Select quotient rule when target form shows v² in denominator
$\;y = \dfrac{x}{1+x}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{(1+x)(1) - x(1)}{(1+x)^2} = \dfrac{1}{(1+x)^2}\;$
1qrule selection
Use second derivative test to filter minima from multiple stationary points
$\;y = x^3 - 3x \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 3x^2 - 3 = 0 \Rightarrow x = \pm 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{d^2y}{dx^2} = 6x:\quad x=-1 \Rightarrow -6<0\ (\text{max}),\quad x=1 \Rightarrow 6>0\ (\text{min})\;$
1qsecond derivative classification
Recycle the stationarity equation to simplify back-substitution
$\;f(x) = 4 - e^x - 4e^{-x},\quad f'(x)=0 \Rightarrow e^x = 4e^{-x}\;$
$\;e^{-x} = \tfrac{1}{4}e^{x} \Rightarrow f_{\max} = 4 - e^x - 4\cdot\tfrac{1}{4}e^x = 4 - 2e^x = 4 - 2\cdot 2 = 0\;$
1qcondition recycling
Factor derivative to expose zero-product structure
$\;g(x) = x^2 e^x \Rightarrow g'(x) = 2x\,e^x + x^2 e^x\;$
$\;g'(x) = x\,e^x(2 + x) = 0 \Rightarrow x = 0 \text{ or } x = -2\;$
1qfactor then analyse
Find range on closed interval via endpoints and interior critical points
$\;f(x) = x^3 - 3x \text{ on } [-2,\,2],\quad f'(x)=3x^2-3=0 \Rightarrow x=\pm1\;$
$\;f(-2)=-2,\ f(-1)=2,\ f(1)=-2,\ f(2)=2 \Rightarrow \text{range} = [-2,\,2]\;$
1qextreme value theorem
Eliminate always-nonzero factors to reduce a stationary-point equation
$\;f'(x) = e^x(2x - 1) = 0\;$
$\;e^x > 0 \Rightarrow 2x - 1 = 0 \Rightarrow x = \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qzero product elimination
Substitute stationary x-value into original equation for y-coordinate
$\;y = x^3 - 3x,\quad \dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow x = 1\;$
$\;y(1) = 1^3 - 3(1) = -2 \Rightarrow (1,\,-2)\;$
1qback substitution into original
Combine derivative sign change with end-behaviour to state range
$\;f(x) = x + \dfrac{1}{x},\quad x > 0,\quad f'(x) = 1 - \dfrac{1}{x^2} = 0 \Rightarrow x = 1\;$
$\;f'\!\left(\tfrac{1}{2}\right)<0,\ f'(2)>0 \Rightarrow \text{min at } f(1)=2;\ f\to+\infty \text{ as } x\to0^+,\,\infty \Rightarrow \text{range}=[2,\infty)\;$
1qrange from turning point
Differentiate a^t via the rule d/dt(a^t) = a^t ln a
$\;A = 5 \cdot 3^{2t}\;$
$\;\dfrac{dA}{dt} = 5 \cdot 3^{2t} \cdot 2\ln 3 = 10\ln 3 \cdot 3^{2t}\;$
1qexponential differentiation
Factor out the lowest fractional power to merge product-rule terms
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 2x(x+1)^{1/2} + x^2 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}(x+1)^{-1/2}\;$
$\;(x+1)^{-1/2}\!\left[2x(x+1) + \tfrac{x^2}{2}\right] = \dfrac{x(5x+4)}{2(x+1)^{1/2}}\;$
1qcommon factor extraction
Use exponential-beats-polynomial dominance to extract horizontal asymptote
$\;y = 5 + x^2 e^{-x},\quad x \to \infty\;$
$\;x^2 e^{-x} \to 0 \Rightarrow y \to 5\;$
1qdominance argument
Bridge dr/dt via chain rule using dV/dt and dV/dr
$\;V = \tfrac{4}{3}\pi r^3,\quad \dfrac{dV}{dt} = 8\pi,\quad r = 2\;$
$\;\dfrac{dr}{dt} = \dfrac{dV/dt}{dV/dr} = \dfrac{8\pi}{4\pi r^2}\bigg|_{r=2} = \dfrac{8\pi}{16\pi} = \dfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qconnected rates of change
Substitute given point coordinates into implicit dy/dx for numerical gradient
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{2x - y}{x + 2y},\quad P(1,\,1)\;$
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx}\bigg|_{(1,1)} = \dfrac{2(1) - 1}{1 + 2(1)} = \dfrac{1}{3}\;$
1qpoint evaluation
Invert constant rate by dividing total volume by flow rate
$\;V(h) = h^3,\quad h_{\max} = 5,\quad \dfrac{dV}{dt} = 25\;$
$\;t = \dfrac{V(5)}{25} = \dfrac{125}{25} = 5\;$
1qconstant rate inversion
Substitute point coordinates into implicit derivative to find tangent gradient
$\;\dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{-2x - y}{x + 6y},\quad P(1,2)\;$
$\;m = \dfrac{-2(1) - 2}{1 + 6(2)} = \dfrac{-4}{13}\;$
1qevaluate implicit derivative
Rearrange implicit product to explicit y = f(x) before differentiating
$\;xy = 4\;$
$\;y = 4x^{-1} \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = -4x^{-2}\;$
1qexplicit rearrangement
Take ln of both sides to differentiate variable-base variable-exponent forms
$\;y = x^x\;$
$\;\ln y = x\ln x \Rightarrow \frac{1}{y}\frac{dy}{dx} = \ln x + 1 \Rightarrow \frac{dy}{dx} = x^x(\ln x + 1)\;$
1qlogarithmic differentiation
Differentiate f to prepare the Newton-Raphson denominator
$\;f(x) = x^3 - 2x + 1,\quad x_0 = 2\;$
$\;f'(x) = 3x^2 - 2 \Rightarrow f'(2) = 10 \neq 0\;$
1qderivative as tool
Simplify derivative via Pythagorean identity before differentiating again
$\;f''(x) = \dfrac{-\sin x - \sin^2 x - \cos^2 x}{(1+\sin x)^2}\;$
$\;\dfrac{-\sin x - (\sin^2 x + \cos^2 x)}{(1+\sin x)^2} = \dfrac{-(1+\sin x)}{(1+\sin x)^2} = \dfrac{-1}{1+\sin x}\;$
1qintermediate simplification
Trace parameter domain through asymptotes to find Cartesian range
$\;x = \tan t,\; y = x^2,\; -\tfrac{3\pi}{4} \le t \le \tfrac{\pi}{4}\;$
$\;t\in[-\tfrac{3\pi}{4},-\tfrac{\pi}{2})\!:\,x\in[1,\infty);\; t\in(-\tfrac{\pi}{2},\tfrac{\pi}{4}]\!:\,x\in(-\infty,1] \Rightarrow x\in\mathbb{R} \Rightarrow y\in[0,\infty)\;$
1qdomain range analysis
Choose implicit differentiation over parametric for tangent gradient
$\;4x^2 - y^2 = 4,\quad P(\sec\theta,\, 2\tan\theta)\;$
$\;8x - 2y\,\dfrac{dy}{dx} = 0 \Rightarrow \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{4x}{y} = \dfrac{4\sec\theta}{2\tan\theta} = \dfrac{2}{\sin\theta}\;$
1qdifferentiation pathway choice
Build Maclaurin/Taylor series by repeated differentiation at the expansion point
$\;f(x) = e^x,\quad f(0)=1,\; f'(0)=1,\; f''(0)=1,\; f'''(0)=1\;$
$\;e^x = 1 + x + \dfrac{x^2}{2!} + \dfrac{x^3}{3!} + \cdots\;$
1qrepeated differentiation
Apply product rule with chain rule inside an outer quotient rule
$\;\dfrac{d^2y}{dx^2},\quad \dfrac{dy}{dx}=\dfrac{1+\ln x}{x(1+x)^{1/2}}\;$
$\;p=1+\ln x,\; q=x(1+x)^{1/2};\; q'=(1+x)^{1/2}+\dfrac{x}{2(1+x)^{1/2}}=\dfrac{2+3x}{2(1+x)^{1/2}} \Rightarrow \dfrac{d^2y}{dx^2}=\dfrac{\tfrac{1}{x}\cdot x(1+x)^{1/2}-(1+\ln x)\cdot\tfrac{2+3x}{2(1+x)^{1/2}}}{x^2(1+x)}\;$
1qnested differentiation
Convert x, surd, and dx to u via squaring and differentiating
$\;\int \dfrac{x}{\sqrt{x+1}}\,dx,\quad u=\sqrt{x+1}\;$
$\;x=u^2-1,\ dx=2u\,du \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{u^2-1}{u}\cdot 2u\,du = \int 2(u^2-1)\,du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Use 'hence' to reverse part (a)'s derivative as an antiderivative
$\;\text{(a)}\ \dfrac{d}{dx}\bigl[(1+x^2)^{1/2}\bigr] = \dfrac{x}{\sqrt{1+x^2}};\quad \text{(b)}\ \int \dfrac{3x}{\sqrt{1+x^2}}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \dfrac{3x}{\sqrt{1+x^2}}\,dx = 3\,(1+x^2)^{1/2} + C\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Substitute u = √x to rationalise surd integrand
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{1+\sqrt{x}}\,dx\;$
$\;u=\sqrt{x},\; dx=2u\,du \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{2u}{1+u}\,du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Differentiate the given substitution to express dx in terms of du
$\;\int 2x\,e^{x^2}\,dx,\quad u = x^2\;$
$\;\dfrac{du}{dx} = 2x \Rightarrow dx = \dfrac{du}{2x}\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Substitute u = inner function to absorb its derivative from the numerator
$\;\int \dfrac{\cos x}{(1+\sin x)^2}\,dx\;$
$\;u = 1+\sin x,\; du = \cos x\,dx \Rightarrow \int u^{-2}\,du = -\dfrac{1}{1+\sin x}+C\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Convert x-limits to u-limits immediately on substitution
$\;\int_0^1 2x\,(x^2+1)^3\,dx,\quad u=x^2+1\;$
$\;x=0\Rightarrow u=1,\; x=1\Rightarrow u=2:\quad \int_1^2 u^3\,du = \left[\tfrac{u^4}{4}\right]_1^2 = \tfrac{15}{4}\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Rearrange the substitution equation to rewrite leftover integrand pieces in u
$\;\int \dfrac{x}{(1+x)^2}\,dx,\quad u=1+x\;$
$\;x = u-1,\; dx = du \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{u-1}{u^2}\,du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Re-express x, dx, and all radical parts in the new variable u
$\;\int \frac{1}{1+\sqrt{x}}\,dx,\quad u = 1+\sqrt{x}\;$
$\;\sqrt{x}=u-1,\ x=(u-1)^2,\ dx=2(u-1)\,du \Rightarrow \int \frac{2(u-1)}{u}\,du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Split odd power to pair one factor with du in radical substitution
$\;\int x^3 \sqrt{4-x^2}\,dx\;$
$\;u=4-x^2,\; x^3\,dx = x^2\cdot x\,dx = (4-u)\!\left(-\tfrac{du}{2}\right) \Rightarrow -\tfrac{1}{2}\int (4-u)\sqrt{u}\,du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Invert the substitution to rewrite orphan x-factors in u
$\;\int x\sqrt{2x+1}\,dx,\quad u=2x+1\;$
$\;x=\tfrac{u-1}{2},\ dx=\tfrac{1}{2}du \Rightarrow \tfrac{1}{4}\int (u-1)\,u^{1/2}\,du = \tfrac{1}{4}\int \bigl(u^{3/2}-u^{1/2}\bigr)du\;$
1qsubstitution bridge
Apply integration by parts repeatedly until the log/polynomial factor is exhausted
$\;\int (\ln x)^2\,dx\;$
$\;x(\ln x)^2 - \int 2\ln x\,dx = x(\ln x)^2 - 2x\ln x + 2x + C\;$
1qintegration by parts
Multiply integrand by 1 to manufacture IBP product structure
$\;\int \ln x\,dx = \int \ln x \cdot 1\,dx\;$
$\;u=\ln x,\; v=x \Rightarrow x\ln x - \int x \cdot \dfrac{1}{x}\,dx = x\ln x - x + C\;$
1qintegration by parts
Assign u to the polynomial factor in polynomial×exponential integrals via LIATE/LIPET
$\;\int x\,e^{2x}\,dx\;$
$\;u = x,\; dv = e^{2x}\,dx \Rightarrow \tfrac{1}{2}x\,e^{2x} - \tfrac{1}{2}\!\int e^{2x}\,dx = \tfrac{1}{2}x\,e^{2x} - \tfrac{1}{4}e^{2x} + C\;$
1qintegration by parts
Assign u to the logarithmic factor by LIATE priority
$\;\int x \ln x\,dx\;$
$\;u = \ln x,\ v = \tfrac{x^2}{2} \Rightarrow \tfrac{x^2}{2}\ln x - \int \tfrac{x}{2}\,dx = \tfrac{x^2}{2}\ln x - \tfrac{x^2}{4} + C\;$
1qintegration by parts
Integrate polynomial times exponential using integration by parts
$\;\int x\, e^{2x}\, dx\;$
$\;u=x,\ dv=e^{2x}dx \Rightarrow \tfrac{x}{2}e^{2x} - \int \tfrac{1}{2}e^{2x}\,dx = \tfrac{x}{2}e^{2x} - \tfrac{1}{4}e^{2x} + C\;$
1qintegration by parts
Apply integration by parts twice to close a trig-polynomial reduction
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} x^n \cos x\,dx\;$
$\;I_n = \left(\tfrac{\pi}{2}\right)^n - n\!\int_0^{\pi/2} x^{n-1}\sin x\,dx = \left(\tfrac{\pi}{2}\right)^n - n(n-1)\,I_{n-2}\;$
1qreduction formula ibp
Iterate a reduction formula along the parity chain to the matching base case
$\;I_n = (n-1)\,I_{n-2},\quad I_0 = \tfrac{\pi}{2},\quad \text{find } I_4\;$
$\;I_4 = 3\,I_2 = 3\cdot 1\cdot I_0 = 3\cdot\tfrac{\pi}{2} = \dfrac{3\pi}{2}\;$
1qreduction formula ibp
Split x^n as x^{n-1}·x to enable IBP against a surd denominator
$\;I_n = \int \dfrac{x^n}{\sqrt{a^2 - x^2}}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \dfrac{x^{n-1} \cdot x}{\sqrt{a^2-x^2}}\,dx,\quad u = x^{n-1},\ dv = \dfrac{x}{\sqrt{a^2-x^2}}\,dx \Rightarrow v = -\sqrt{a^2-x^2}\;$
1qreduction formula ibp
Peel off one factor of sin x to set up IBP for reduction
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\,dx\;$
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-1}x \cdot \sin x\,dx,\quad u=\sin^{n-1}x,\ dv=\sin x\,dx\;$
1qreduction formula ibp
Classify ordinates as end-pair versus interior for trapezium rule
$\;n=3,\; h=1,\; y_0=1,\; y_1=3,\; y_2=5,\; y_3=2\;$
$\;\tfrac{h}{2}\bigl[(y_0+y_3)+2(y_1+y_2)\bigr]=\tfrac{1}{2}\bigl[(1+2)+2(3+5)\bigr]=\tfrac{19}{2}\;$
1qformula selection
Partition ordinates into endpoints versus interior values for the trapezium rule
$\;h=1,\quad y_0=1,\; y_1=3,\; y_2=2,\; y_3=5\;$
$\;\tfrac{h}{2}\bigl[(y_0+y_3)+2(y_1+y_2)\bigr]=\tfrac{1}{2}(6+10)=8\;$
1qformula selection
Integrate divided rational form using ln for k/(x−a) term
$\;\int_0^1 \left(3 + \dfrac{2}{x-3}\right)dx\;$
$\;\left[3x + 2\ln|x-3|\right]_0^1 = 3 + 2\ln 2 - 2\ln 3 = 3 + 2\ln\!\dfrac{2}{3}\;$
1qpartial fractions then integrate
Apply given multi-angle linearisation to integrate cos^n θ term-by-term
$\;\int_0^{\pi/6} 8\cos^3\theta\,d\theta,\quad 8\cos^3\theta = \cos 3\theta + 3\cos\theta\;$
$\;\int_0^{\pi/6}(\cos 3\theta + 3\cos\theta)\,d\theta = \left[\tfrac{\sin 3\theta}{3} + 3\sin\theta\right]_0^{\pi/6} = \tfrac{1}{3} + \tfrac{3}{2} = \tfrac{11}{6}\;$
1qpartial fractions then integrate
Integrate each partial fraction term using standard log and power rules
$\;\int \left(\dfrac{3}{x+1} + \dfrac{2}{x-1}\right) dx\;$
$\;3\ln|x+1| + 2\ln|x-1| + c\;$
1qpartial fractions then integrate
Set up trapezium rule strip width from ordinate count
$\;x = 0,\,1,\,2,\,3,\,4 \quad (k = 5 \text{ ordinates})\;$
$\;n = 5 - 1 = 4,\quad h = \dfrac{4-0}{4} = 1\;$
1qnumerical integration
Set up strip width and ordinate table for trapezium rule
$\;\int_0^{3} x^2\,dx,\quad n=3\;$
$\;h=1,\quad \text{Area}\approx\tfrac{1}{2}[0+9+2(1+4)]=\tfrac{19}{2}\;$
1qnumerical integration
Expand polynomial product directly instead of parts or substitution
$\;\int x(x+1)^2\,dx\;$
$\;\int (x^3+2x^2+x)\,dx = \tfrac{1}{4}x^4 + \tfrac{2}{3}x^3 + \tfrac{1}{2}x^2 + C\;$
1qalgebraic preparation
Rewrite reciprocal and root terms as negative or fractional powers before integrating
$\;\int\!\left(\dfrac{1}{x^2} + \sqrt{x}\right)dx\;$
$\;\int\!\left(x^{-2} + x^{1/2}\right)dx = -x^{-1} + \dfrac{2}{3}x^{3/2} + c\;$
1qalgebraic preprocessing
Evaluate the standard-form remainder exactly after splitting
$\;\int_1^2 \frac{1}{x}\,dx = [\ln x]_1^2\;$
$\;\ln 2 - \ln 1 = \ln 2\;$
1qexact evaluation
Integrate term-by-term using linearity and the power rule
$\;\int (3x^2 + 4x - 1)\,dx\;$
$\;= x^3 + 2x^2 - x + C\;$
1qterm by term power rule
Rewrite roots and reciprocals as fractional indices before integrating
$\;\displaystyle\int \dfrac{3}{\sqrt{x}}\, dx\;$
$\;\int 3x^{-1/2}\, dx = 3 \cdot \dfrac{x^{1/2}}{1/2} + c = 6\sqrt{x} + c\;$
1qindex law preprocessing
Subtract lower from upper to find area between curves, splitting where they cross
$\;y = x^2,\; y = x,\; x \in [0,2]\;$
$\;\text{Cross at } x=0,1;\quad A = \int_0^1 (x - x^2)\,dx + \int_1^2 (x^2 - x)\,dx = \tfrac{1}{6} + \tfrac{5}{6} = 1\;$
1qtop minus bottom
Rewrite follow-up integrand as linear combination of original integrand
$\;\int_0^2 (1 - \ln x)\,dx = 3,\quad \text{find } \int_0^2 (5 + \ln x)\,dx\;$
$\;5 + \ln x = 6 - (1 - \ln x) \Rightarrow \int_0^2 (5+\ln x)\,dx = 6(2) - 3 = 9\;$
1qintegrand bridge
Convert cross-sectional area to volume via V = A·v·t
$\;A = 2\,\text{m}^2,\quad v = 3\,\text{m/s},\quad t = 1\,\text{min} = 60\,\text{s}\;$
$\;V = A \cdot v \cdot t = 2 \times 3 \times 60 = 360\,\text{m}^3\;$
1qunits dimensional modelling
Partition region using geometric boundaries to assign per-piece integration limits
$\;y = x^2,\quad y = 2x,\quad y = 3 \quad (\text{intersections at } x=0,1,\sqrt{3})\;$
$\;A = \int_0^1 (2x - x^2)\,dx + \int_1^{\sqrt{3}} (3 - x^2)\,dx\;$
1qregion decomposition
Recognise 1/x as the logarithmic special case of integration
$\;\int \dfrac{5}{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\int 5x^{-1}\,dx = 5\ln|x| + c\;$
1qspecial case recognition
Integrate polynomial term-by-term and evaluate at bounds for definite area
$\;\int_1^2 (3x^2 - 2x)\,dx\;$
$\;\left[x^3 - x^2\right]_1^2 = (8-4)-(1-1) = 4\;$
1qpolynomial integration
Distribute fractional power across polynomial factor before applying power rule
$\;\int (u+1)\,u^{1/2}\,du\;$
$\;\int \bigl(u^{3/2}+u^{1/2}\bigr)\,du = \tfrac{2}{5}u^{5/2}+\tfrac{2}{3}u^{3/2}+C\;$
1qalgebraic reduction
Integrate LHS and match coefficients to determine unknown constant
$\;\int\!\left(3x + \dfrac{1}{x^2}\right)dx = \dfrac{3}{2}x^2 + \dfrac{k}{x}\;$
$\;\int x^{-2}\,dx = -\dfrac{1}{x} = \dfrac{k}{x} \Rightarrow k = -1\;$
1qcoefficient comparison
Assemble full antiderivative before applying definite limits
$\;\int_0^1 x\,e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\bigl[x\,e^{x} - e^{x}\bigr]_0^1 = (e - e) - (0 - 1) = 1\;$
1qdeferred evaluation
Take absolute value of negative definite integral to report geometric area
$\;\int_0^2 (x^2 - 4)\,dx = -\tfrac{16}{3}\;$
$\;\text{Area} = \left|-\tfrac{16}{3}\right| = \tfrac{16}{3}\;$
1qarea sign correction
Use total-area decomposition to replace awkward sub-region with complement
$\;R_1 + R_2 = \int_0^1 (x - x^2)\,dx = \tfrac{1}{6},\quad R_1 = \tfrac{(1-m)^3}{6},\quad R_1 = R_2\;$
$\;2 \cdot \tfrac{(1-m)^3}{6} = \tfrac{1}{6} \Rightarrow (1-m)^3 = \tfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow m = 1 - \tfrac{1}{\sqrt[3]{2}}\;$
1qarea complement
Sketch y = eˣ by labelling intercept, asymptote, and concavity
$\;y = e^x\;$
$\;y(0)=1,\quad y''=e^x>0,\quad y\to 0^+\ (x\to -\infty) \Rightarrow \text{intercept }(0,1),\ \text{asymptote }y=0,\ \text{concave up}\;$
1qcurve sketching checklist
Determine trapezium-rule strip width h from limits and ordinate count
$\;\int_0^1 f(x)\,dx,\quad x = 0,\, 0.25,\, 0.5,\, 0.75,\, 1\;$
$\;n = 5-1 = 4,\quad h = \dfrac{1-0}{4} = 0.25,\quad \dfrac{h}{2} = 0.125\;$
1qparameter identification
Determine trapezium-rule strip width h from a table of x-values
$\;x = 1,\, 1.5,\, 2,\, 2.5,\, 3\;$
$\;n = 5 - 1 = 4,\quad h = \dfrac{3 - 1}{4} = 0.5\;$
1qparameter extraction
Rewrite 1/uⁿ as u⁻ⁿ to apply the reverse power rule
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{x^3}\,dx\;$
$\;\int x^{-3}\,dx = \dfrac{x^{-2}}{-2} + C = -\dfrac{1}{2x^2} + C\;$
1qintegrand rewrite
Split integral into exact constant part and approximate function part
$\;\int_{1}^{4} (3 + 2f(x))\,dx,\quad \int_{1}^{4} f(x)\,dx \approx 5.2\;$
$\;\int_{1}^{4} 3\,dx + 2\int_{1}^{4} f(x)\,dx = 3(3) + 2(5.2) = 19.4\;$
1qlinearity of integration
Preserve full decimal precision through trapezium-rule arithmetic
$\;h=0.5,\quad y_0=1.00,\ y_1=1.25,\ y_2=2.00\;$
$\;\tfrac{0.5}{2}\bigl(1.00+2.00+2(1.25)\bigr)=0.25\times5.50=1.375\;$
1qprecision management
Evaluate boundary brackets immediately after each IBP round
$\;I = \int_0^1 x\,e^x\,dx,\quad u=x,\ dv=e^x\,dx\;$
$\;I = [xe^x]_0^1 - \int_0^1 e^x\,dx = e - [e^x]_0^1 = e - (e-1) = 1\;$
1qearly evaluation
Compute the trapezium-rule bracket fully before multiplying by h/2
$\;h=1,\quad y_0=1,\; y_1=3,\; y_2=5\;$
$\;B = (1+5)+2(3)=12,\quad A \approx \tfrac{1}{2}\times 12 = 6\;$
1qorder of operations
Label sub-integrals with letters to manage repeated IBP cleanly
$\;I = \int_0^1 x^2 e^x\,dx\;$
$\;I = e - 2J,\quad J = \int_0^1 x\,e^x\,dx = 1 \Rightarrow I = e - 2\;$
1qstructural labelling
Integrate cos(kx) by reverse chain rule with 1/k factor
$\;\int \cos 3x\,dx\;$
$\;\int \cos 3x\,dx = \dfrac{\sin 3x}{3} + C\;$
1qlinear argument adjustment
Substitute the show-that linearised identity before integrating
$\;\text{(a): } (1+\cos x)^2 = \tfrac{3}{2}+2\cos x+\tfrac{1}{2}\cos 2x\,;\quad \int_0^{\pi}(1+\cos x)^2\,dx\;$
$\;\int_0^{\pi}\!\left(\tfrac{3}{2}+2\cos x+\tfrac{1}{2}\cos 2x\right)dx = \left[\tfrac{3}{2}x+2\sin x+\tfrac{1}{4}\sin 2x\right]_0^{\pi} = \dfrac{3\pi}{2}\;$
1qshow that as tool
Label integral as I to close cyclic IBP algebraically
$\;I = \int e^{x}\sin x\,dx\;$
$\;\text{IBP twice} \Rightarrow I = \tfrac{1}{2}e^{x}(\sin x - \cos x) - I \Rightarrow I = \tfrac{1}{2}e^{x}(\sin x - \cos x) + C\;$
1qcyclic ibp
Use positivity of one factor to reduce a product-equals-zero to a single equation
$\;e^{2x}\sin x = 0\;$
$\;e^{2x} > 0\ \forall x \in \mathbb{R} \Rightarrow \sin x = 0 \Rightarrow x = n\pi,\ n \in \mathbb{Z}\;$
1qzero analysis for limits
Convert Cartesian volume of revolution to parametric integral via dx = (dx/dθ)dθ
$\;x = t^2,\; y = t,\quad t \in [0,1]\;$
$\;V = \int_0^1 \pi\, y^2\,\frac{dx}{dt}\,dt = \int_0^1 \pi\, t^2 \cdot 2t\, dt = \int_0^1 2\pi t^3\, dt\;$
1qparametric integration
Integrate to displacement equation then isolate linear-T term for iteration
$\;\int_0^T (5 - e^{-t})\,dt = 20\;$
$\;5T + e^{-T} - 1 = 20 \Rightarrow T = \tfrac{1}{5}(21 - e^{-T})\;$
1qrearrange to iteration
Cancel matching √x factors between integrand and dx after substitution
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x}\,(1+\sqrt{x})^2}\,dx,\quad u=1+\sqrt{x},\quad dx=2\sqrt{x}\,du\;$
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x}\,u^2}\cdot 2\sqrt{x}\,du = \int 2u^{-2}\,du = -\dfrac{2}{1+\sqrt{x}}+C\;$
1qsubstitution cancellation
Invert a rational substitution to write x and dx in terms of u
$\;u = \dfrac{x+1}{x-1}\;$
$\;x = \dfrac{u+1}{u-1},\quad dx = \dfrac{-2}{(u-1)^2}\,du\;$
1qsubstitution inversion
Split polynomial-over-single-power fraction into term-by-term powers
$\;\int \dfrac{x^2 + 1}{\sqrt{x}}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \left(x^{3/2} + x^{-1/2}\right)dx = \tfrac{2}{5}x^{5/2} + 2x^{1/2} + C\;$
1qalgebraic separation
Square e^{x/2} via index law to collapse to e^x
$\;\left(e^{x/2}\right)^2\;$
$\;e^{x/2 + x/2} = e^x\;$
1qexponential simplification
Integrate tan(ax) as −(1/a)ln|cos(ax)| via f'/f recognition
$\;\int \tan(3x)\,dx\;$
$\;\int \frac{\sin(3x)}{\cos(3x)}\,dx = -\tfrac{1}{3}\ln|\cos(3x)| + C\;$
1qtrig standard integral
Apply secondary linear shift to bypass partial fractions on repeated linear denominators
$\;\int \frac{x+3}{(x+1)^2}\,dx\;$
$\;w=x+1:\quad \int \frac{w+2}{w^2}\,dw = \int \left(\frac{1}{w}+\frac{2}{w^2}\right)dw = \ln|x+1|-\frac{2}{x+1}+C\;$
1qlinear shift simplification
Double a single-revolution volume to model a symmetric composite solid
$\;V_1 = \pi\int_0^{4} x\,dx = 8\pi\;$
$\;V_{\text{total}} = 2V_1 = 16\pi\;$
1qgeometric modelling
Split polynomial-over-monomial fraction into separate power terms
$\;\int \dfrac{x^2 + 1}{x^3}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \left(x^{-1} + x^{-3}\right)dx = \ln|x| - \tfrac{1}{2}x^{-2} + C\;$
1qterm by term division
Substitute u = √(linear) to convert surd integrand into polynomial
$\;\int \dfrac{x}{\sqrt{x+1}}\,dx,\quad u=\sqrt{x+1}\;$
$\;\int \dfrac{u^2-1}{u}\cdot 2u\,du = \int 2(u^2-1)\,du = \tfrac{2}{3}u^3 - 2u + C\;$
1qsurd substitution
Spot [f(t)]^n · f'(t) and integrate by reverse chain rule
$\;\int \sin^2 t\,\cos t\,dt\;$
$\;\int [\sin t]^2 \cdot (\sin t)'\ dt = \dfrac{\sin^3 t}{3} + C\;$
1qsubstitution by recognition
Factor out constant scalar to reuse part (a) antiderivative
$\;\text{(a)}\ \int x e^{x^2}\,dx = \tfrac{1}{2}e^{x^2}+C\qquad \text{(b)}\ \int_0^1 5x e^{x^2}\,dx\;$
$\;5\int_0^1 x e^{x^2}\,dx = 5\left[\tfrac{1}{2}e^{x^2}\right]_0^1 = \tfrac{5}{2}(e-1)\;$
1qresult chaining
Map Cartesian region boundaries to parameter t-limits
$\;x = \cos t,\; y = \sin t,\; 0 \le t \le \pi\;$
$\;y=0 \Rightarrow t=0,\; x=0 \Rightarrow t=\tfrac{\pi}{2} \Rightarrow \int_{0}^{\pi/2} y\,\dfrac{dx}{dt}\,dt\;$
1qparametric limit finding
Choose unfactored power form when bounds give perfect-square radicands
$\;\int_0^3 \dfrac{x}{\sqrt{x+1}}\,dx\;$
$\;\left[\tfrac{2}{3}(x+1)^{3/2} - 2(x+1)^{1/2}\right]_0^3 = \left(\tfrac{16}{3} - 4\right) - \left(\tfrac{2}{3} - 2\right) = \dfrac{8}{3}\;$
1qform selection
Apply FTC with Part 1 antiderivative on a 'Hence evaluate' definite integral
$\;F(x) = \tfrac{2}{3}x^{3/2},\quad \int_1^4 \sqrt{x}\,dx\;$
$\;\left[\tfrac{2}{3}x^{3/2}\right]_1^4 = \tfrac{2}{3}(8) - \tfrac{2}{3}(1) = \dfrac{14}{3}\;$
1qhence chain
Reuse part (a) antiderivative inside Fundamental Theorem for part (b)
$\;\text{(a)}\ \int x\,e^x\,dx = xe^x - e^x + C\;$
$\;\text{(b)}\ \int_0^1 x\,e^x\,dx = \bigl[xe^x - e^x\bigr]_0^1 = (e - e) - (0 - 1) = 1\;$
1qstructured exam linkage
Integrate e^{kx} via standard result with reciprocal coefficient 1/k
$\;\int e^{3x}\,dx\;$
$\;\dfrac{1}{3}\,e^{3x} + C\;$
1qstandard form integration
Assign u to the algebraic factor by LIATE priority
$\;\int x\,e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;u = x,\; dv = e^{x}\,dx \Rightarrow \int x\,e^{x}\,dx = x\,e^{x} - e^{x} + C\;$
1qliate assignment
Drop absolute value in ln when domain forces positivity
$\;\int \frac{1}{x}\,dx,\quad x>0\;$
$\;\ln|x|+C = \ln x + C \quad (\text{since } x>0)\;$
1qdomain simplification
Expand squared exponential binomial using index law before integrating
$\;\int (e^{0.5x} - 2)^2\,dx\;$
$\;(e^{0.5x})^2 - 2\cdot 2e^{0.5x} + 4 = e^x - 4e^{0.5x} + 4\;$
1qintegrand preparation
Defer limit substitution until full antiderivative is found
$\;\int_0^1 x\,e^{x}\,dx\;$
$\;F(x)=xe^x - e^x \Rightarrow F(1)-F(0)=(e-e)-(-1)=1\;$
1qdefinite integral deferral
Integrate fractional negative power via reverse power rule
$\;\int t^{-1/3}\,dt\;$
$\;\dfrac{t^{2/3}}{2/3} + C = \dfrac{3}{2}\,t^{2/3} + C\;$
1qfractional exponent integration
Find missing integration limit from curve-axis intersection
$\;y = x^2 - 4,\quad x = 3,\quad y = 0\;$
$\;x^2 - 4 = 0 \Rightarrow x = 2 \quad (x>0),\quad \int_{2}^{3}(x^2-4)\,dx\;$
1qregion identification
Split improper rational fraction by numerator surgery before integrating
$\;\int \frac{x}{x+1}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \left(1 - \frac{1}{x+1}\right)dx = x - \ln|x+1| + C\;$
1qalgebraic division then integrate
Split integrand by linearity to isolate the IBP-needing term
$\;\int x\sin^2 x\,dx = \tfrac{1}{2}\int (x - x\cos 2x)\,dx\;$
$\;= \tfrac{1}{2}\!\left[\int x\,dx \;-\; \underbrace{\int x\cos 2x\,dx}_{\text{IBP}}\right]\;$
1qintegral decomposition
Split linear-over-quadratic numerator into f'/f part plus constant part
$\;\int \dfrac{3x+4}{x^2+1}\,dx\;$
$\;\tfrac{3}{2}\!\int\!\dfrac{2x}{x^2+1}\,dx + 4\!\int\!\dfrac{1}{x^2+1}\,dx = \tfrac{3}{2}\ln(x^2+1) + 4\arctan x + C\;$
1qnumerator decomposition
Split integral by linearity to reuse earlier-part antiderivative
$\;\text{Given } \int x e^x\,dx = xe^x - e^x.\quad \text{Find } \int_0^1 (2x - xe^x)\,dx.\;$
$\;\int_0^1 2x\,dx - \int_0^1 xe^x\,dx = \bigl[x^2\bigr]_0^1 - \bigl[xe^x - e^x\bigr]_0^1 = 1 - (1 - (-1)) = -1\;$
1qexam scaffolding reuse
Exploit ln 1 = 0 and ln e = 1 at integration limits to collapse log terms
$\;\int_1^e x\ln x\,dx = \left[\tfrac{x^2}{2}\ln x - \tfrac{x^2}{4}\right]_1^e\;$
$\;\left(\tfrac{e^2}{2}(1) - \tfrac{e^2}{4}\right) - \left(\tfrac{1}{2}(0) - \tfrac{1}{4}\right) = \dfrac{e^2+1}{4}\;$
1qexact value substitution
Apply iterated IBP to reduce powers of ln x against polynomial
$\;\int x\,(\ln x)^2\,dx\;$
$\;\frac{x^2}{2}(\ln x)^2 - \int x\,\ln x\,dx = \frac{x^2}{2}(\ln x)^2 - \frac{x^2}{2}\ln x + \frac{x^2}{4} + C\;$
1qiterated ibp
Swap integration limits to absorb a leading negative sign
$\;\int_{5}^{2} -f(u)\,du\;$
$\;\int_{5}^{2} -f(u)\,du = \int_{2}^{5} f(u)\,du\;$
1qlimit manipulation
Apply the polar area formula ½∫r²dθ with correct limits
$\;r = 2\cos\theta,\quad A = ?\;$
$\;A = \tfrac{1}{2}\int_{-\pi/2}^{\pi/2}(2\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta = 2\int_{-\pi/2}^{\pi/2}\cos^2\theta\,d\theta = \pi\;$
1qpolar area formula
Divide by inner linear coefficient when integrating 1/(ax+b) forms
$\;\int \dfrac{3}{2x+1}\,dx\;$
$\;\dfrac{3}{2}\ln|2x+1| + C\;$
1qlinear chain rule
Combine logarithmic terms using log laws for compact exact answer
$\;\ln 3 - \ln 4 - \ln 2 + \ln 3\;$
$\;2\ln 3 - \ln 8 = \ln 9 - \ln 8 = \ln\!\dfrac{9}{8}\;$
1qlog simplification
Annihilate cosine and sine harmonics over a full period
$\;\int_0^{2\pi} \left(3 + 2\cos\theta - \sin 2\theta\right) d\theta\;$
$\;\cos\theta,\,\sin 2\theta \text{ vanish} \Rightarrow \int_0^{2\pi} 3\, d\theta = 6\pi\;$
1qorthogonality shortcut
Kill sin(kπ) terms when polar/integration limits are multiples of π
$\;\tfrac{1}{2}\int_0^{2\pi}(1+\cos\theta)^2\,d\theta = \tfrac{1}{2}\Big[\tfrac{3}{2}\theta + 2\sin\theta + \tfrac{1}{4}\sin 2\theta\Big]_0^{2\pi}\;$
$\;\sin 2\pi = \sin 4\pi = \sin 0 = 0 \Rightarrow \tfrac{1}{2}\Big[\tfrac{3}{2}(2\pi) - 0\Big] = \tfrac{3\pi}{2}\;$
1qlimit simplification
Equate evaluated definite integral to given value to solve for unknown limit
$\;\int_1^k \frac{1}{x^2}\,dx = \frac{1}{2}\;$
$\;\left[-\frac{1}{x}\right]_1^k = -\frac{1}{k}+1 = \frac{1}{2} \Rightarrow k = 2\;$
1qreverse problem setup
Linearise sin²θ via sin²θ = (1 − cos2θ)/2 to integrate
$\;\int \sin^2\theta\,d\theta\;$
$\;\int \dfrac{1-\cos 2\theta}{2}\,d\theta = \dfrac{\theta}{2} - \dfrac{\sin 2\theta}{4} + C\;$
1qdouble angle linearisation
Reduce improper rational integrand by polynomial long division first
$\;\int \dfrac{x^2}{x+1}\,dx\;$
$\;\int \left(x - 1 + \dfrac{1}{x+1}\right)dx = \tfrac{1}{2}x^2 - x + \ln|x+1| + C\;$
1qlong division reduction
Cancel cosθ against tanθ to reduce integrand to sinθ
$\;\int \cos\theta\,\tan\theta\,d\theta\;$
$\;\int \cos\theta \cdot \dfrac{\sin\theta}{\cos\theta}\,d\theta = \int \sin\theta\,d\theta = -\cos\theta + C\;$
1qintegrand simplification
Integrate both sides after recognising exact-derivative LHS
$\;\dfrac{d}{dx}\bigl[e^{x}\, y\bigr] = e^{x}\;$
$\;e^{x}\, y = \int e^{x}\, dx + C = e^{x} + C \Rightarrow y = 1 + C\,e^{-x}\;$
1qexact derivative integration
Carry forward part (a) simplified √(1+(dy/dx)²) into part (b) surface area integral
$\;y = \sqrt{9-x^2},\quad \sqrt{1+\left(\tfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^{\!2}} = \dfrac{3}{\sqrt{9-x^2}}\;$
$\;S = 2\pi\!\int_0^3 \!\sqrt{9-x^2}\;\cdot\;\dfrac{3}{\sqrt{9-x^2}}\,dx = 2\pi\!\int_0^3 3\,dx = 18\pi\;$
1qcross reference reuse
Split linear numerator as A·f'(x) + B over irreducible quadratic
$\;\int \dfrac{x+3}{x^2+2x+5}\,dx\;$
$\;x+3 = \tfrac{1}{2}(2x+2)+2 \Rightarrow \tfrac{1}{2}\ln|x^2+2x+5|+2\int\dfrac{dx}{(x+1)^2+4}\;$
1qnumerator manipulation
Substitute x = a cosh θ to eliminate (x² − a²)^{n/2} surds
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x^2 - 9}}\,dx\;$
$\;x = 3\cosh\theta,\; \sqrt{9\cosh^2\theta - 9} = 3\sinh\theta \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{3\sinh\theta}{3\sinh\theta}\,d\theta = \theta + C = \operatorname{arcosh}\!\left(\tfrac{x}{3}\right) + C\;$
1qhyperbolic substitution
Split sinⁿx as sinⁿ⁻¹x · sinx to seed reduction by parts
$\;I_n = \int \sin^n x\, dx\;$
$\;u = \sin^{n-1}x,\ dv = \sin x\, dx \Rightarrow I_n = -\sin^{n-1}x\cos x + (n-1)\int \sin^{n-2}x\cos^2 x\, dx\;$
1qparts decomposition
Complete the square to reach standard ∫1/(u²−a²) form
$\;\int \dfrac{1}{x^2 + 2x - 3}\,dx\;$
$\;x^2+2x-3=(x+1)^2-4 \Rightarrow \int \dfrac{du}{u^2-4} = \dfrac{1}{4}\ln\left|\dfrac{x-1}{x+3}\right|+C\;$
1qcompleting the square
Combine 1 + (dy/dx)² over common denominator to collapse the arc-length integrand
$\;y = \sqrt{4 - x^2},\quad \left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2 = \dfrac{x^2}{4 - x^2}\;$
$\;1 + \dfrac{x^2}{4-x^2} = \dfrac{4-x^2+x^2}{4-x^2} = \dfrac{4}{4-x^2} \Rightarrow \sqrt{1+(y')^2} = \dfrac{2}{\sqrt{4-x^2}}\;$
1qalgebraic collapse
Cancel matching surd factors in surface-area integrand before integrating
$\;S = 2\pi \int_0^3 \sqrt{9-x^2}\,\cdot\,\dfrac{3}{\sqrt{9-x^2}}\,dx\;$
$\;\sqrt{9-x^2}\,\cdot\,\dfrac{3}{\sqrt{9-x^2}} = 3 \Rightarrow S = 2\pi\int_0^3 3\,dx = 18\pi\;$
1qintegrand collapse
Split x^n with surd to pair derivative-factor into dv
$\;I_n = \int x^n \sqrt{x^3+1}\,dx = \int x^{n-2} \cdot x^2(x^3+1)^{1/2}\,dx\;$
$\;u = x^{n-2},\ dv = x^2(x^3+1)^{1/2}dx \Rightarrow I_n = \tfrac{2}{9}\,x^{n-2}(x^3+1)^{3/2} - \tfrac{2(n-2)}{9}\int x^{n-3}(x^3+1)^{3/2}\,dx\;$
1qibp split selection
Split (x³+1)^{3/2} as (x³+1)·(x³+1)^{1/2} to recover I_n and I_{n-3}
$\;\int x^{n-3}(x^3+1)^{3/2}\,dx\;$
$\;x^{n-3}(x^3+1)(x^3+1)^{1/2} = x^n(x^3+1)^{1/2} + x^{n-3}(x^3+1)^{1/2} \Rightarrow I_n + I_{n-3}\;$
1qreduction self reference
Split sin^n x as sin^(n-1)x · sin x to derive a reduction formula
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\,dx,\quad u = \sin^{n-1}x,\; dv = \sin x\,dx\;$
$\;I_n = \bigl[-\sin^{n-1}x\cos x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2} + (n-1)\!\int_0^{\pi/2}\!\sin^{n-2}x\,(1-\sin^2 x)\,dx \Rightarrow nI_n = (n-1)I_{n-2}\;$
1qibp partitioning
Recognise residual integral as lower-index I_k to close reduction recurrence
$\;I_n = \int_0^1 x^n e^{-x}\,dx \xrightarrow{\text{IBP}} -e^{-1} + n\!\int_0^1 x^{n-1}e^{-x}\,dx\;$
$\;\int_0^1 x^{n-1}e^{-x}\,dx = I_{n-1} \Rightarrow I_n = nI_{n-1} - e^{-1}\;$
1qpattern recognition recursion
Substitute cos²x = 1−sin²x to force self-referencing reduction
$\;I_n = (n-1)\!\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-2}x\,\cos^2 x\;dx\;$
$\;\cos^2 x = 1-\sin^2 x \Rightarrow I_n = (n-1)(I_{n-2}-I_n) \Rightarrow I_n = \dfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2}\;$
1qidentity driven recurrence
Use the parametric ds element instead of eliminating the parameter
$\;x = \cos t,\; y = \sin t,\; 0 \le t \le \tfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
$\;ds = \sqrt{(-\sin t)^2 + (\cos t)^2}\,dt = dt \Rightarrow L = \int_0^{\pi/2} dt = \dfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
1qparametric formulation
Apply arc-length/surface-area formula and collapse integrand to reduction family
$\;y = \ln(\cos x),\quad S = 2\pi\int_0^{\pi/4} y\,\sqrt{1+\left(\tfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2}\,dx\;$
$\;\tfrac{dy}{dx} = -\tan x,\; 1+\tan^2 x = \sec^2 x \Rightarrow S = 2\pi\int_0^{\pi/4} \ln(\cos x)\,\sec x\,dx\;$
1qformula application and simplification
Collapse square root of perfect square to linearise integrand
$\;1 + \left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^{\!2} = \dfrac{x^2}{4} + \dfrac{1}{2} + \dfrac{1}{4x^2}\;$
$\;\sqrt{\dfrac{x^2}{4} + \dfrac{1}{2} + \dfrac{1}{4x^2}} = \sqrt{\left(\dfrac{x}{2} + \dfrac{1}{2x}\right)^{\!2}} = \dfrac{x}{2} + \dfrac{1}{2x}\;$
1qradical elimination
Combine each limit's terms into one fraction before subtracting
$\;F(x)=\dfrac{x^3}{3}-\dfrac{x^2}{2},\quad F\Big|_1^2\;$
$\;F(2)=\dfrac{8}{3}-\dfrac{4}{2}=\dfrac{16-12}{6}=\dfrac{4}{6}=\dfrac{2}{3},\quad F(1)=\dfrac{1}{3}-\dfrac{1}{2}=\dfrac{2-3}{6}=-\dfrac{1}{6},\quad F(2)-F(1)=\dfrac{2}{3}+\dfrac{1}{6}=\dfrac{5}{6}\;$
1qarithmetic management
Apply IBP twice to recover the original integral and solve algebraically
$\;I = \int e^x \sin x\,dx\;$
$\;I = e^x \sin x - e^x \cos x - I \Rightarrow I = \tfrac{1}{2}e^x(\sin x - \cos x) + C\;$
1qself referencing ibp
Split sin^n x as sin^(n-1)x · sin x to set up IBP reduction
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\, dx = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-1} x \cdot \sin x\, dx\;$
$\;u = \sin^{n-1} x,\ dv = \sin x\, dx \Rightarrow I_n = \bigl[-\sin^{n-1} x\cos x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2} + (n{-}1)\!\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^{n-2} x\cos^2 x\, dx\;$
1qibp factorisation
Recognise part (b) integrand as I_n from part (a)'s reduction formula
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^n x\, dx,\quad I_n = \tfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2};\quad S = 2\pi\!\int_0^{\pi/2} \sin^4 x\, dx\;$
$\;S = 2\pi\, I_4 = 2\pi \cdot \tfrac{3}{4}\,I_2 = 2\pi \cdot \tfrac{3}{4}\cdot\tfrac{1}{2}\,I_0 = 2\pi \cdot \tfrac{3}{8}\cdot\tfrac{\pi}{2} = \dfrac{3\pi^2}{8}\;$
1qcross referencing parts
Link arc length or surface area integrand to a previously derived reduction formula
$\;L = \int_0^{\pi/2} x^2 \sin x\, dx,\quad I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} x^n \sin x\, dx,\; I_2 = \pi - 2\;$
$\;L = I_2 = \pi - 2\;$
1qpattern matching linkage
Rewrite a surd numerator as (radicand)/surd to close a reduction recurrence
$\;\int_0^1 x^{n-2}\sqrt{a - x^2}\,dx\;$
$\;\sqrt{a-x^2} = \dfrac{a-x^2}{\sqrt{a-x^2}} \Rightarrow \int_0^1 \dfrac{x^{n-2}(a-x^2)}{\sqrt{a-x^2}}\,dx = a\,I_{n-2} - I_n\;$
1qrationalisation
Iterate two-step reduction formula down to base case
$\;I_n = \tfrac{n-1}{n}\,I_{n-2},\quad I_0 = \tfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
$\;I_4 = \tfrac{3}{4}\,I_2 = \tfrac{3}{4}\cdot\tfrac{1}{2}\,I_0 = \tfrac{3}{4}\cdot\tfrac{1}{2}\cdot\tfrac{\pi}{2} = \tfrac{3\pi}{16}\;$
1qwallis type descent
Substitute x = ½cos θ to linearise √(1−4x²) via sin²θ identity
$\;\int \frac{1}{\sqrt{1-4x^2}}\,dx\;$
$\;x=\tfrac{1}{2}\cos\theta,\; dx=-\tfrac{1}{2}\sin\theta\,d\theta,\; \sqrt{1-4x^2}=\sin\theta \Rightarrow \int \frac{-\frac{1}{2}\sin\theta}{\sin\theta}\,d\theta = -\tfrac{1}{2}\theta + C\;$
1qtrig substitution
Peel off one x to pair with cos(x²) as exact derivative
$\;I_n = \int x^n \cos(x^2)\, dx\;$
$\;\int x^{n-1}\!\cdot\! x\cos(x^2)\, dx,\quad dv = x\cos(x^2)\,dx \Rightarrow v = \tfrac{1}{2}\sin(x^2)\;$
1qintegrand restructuring
Pick the polynomial factor as u in IBP to drive a reduction formula
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi} x^n \sin x\, dx\;$
$\;u = x^n,\ dv = \sin x\, dx \Rightarrow I_n = [-x^n \cos x]_0^{\pi} + n\!\int_0^{\pi} x^{n-1} \cos x\, dx\;$
1qibp factor selection
Exploit vanishing boundary terms at 0 and π/2 in IBP
$\;I_n = \int_0^{\pi/2} x^n \sin x\, dx\;$
$\;I_n = \bigl[-x^n \cos x\bigr]_0^{\pi/2} + n\!\int_0^{\pi/2} x^{n-1}\cos x\, dx = 0 + n\!\int_0^{\pi/2} x^{n-1}\cos x\, dx\;$
1qboundary term exploitation
Collapse the arc-length surd into a clean trig or hyperbolic integrand
$\;y = \ln(\sec x),\quad s = \int_0^{\pi/3}\!\sqrt{1+\left(\tfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^2}\,dx\;$
$\;1+\tan^2 x = \sec^2 x \Rightarrow s = \int_0^{\pi/3}\sec x\,dx = \ln(2+\sqrt{3})\;$
1qsurd collapse
Anchor reduction formula at base case then iterate upward
$\;I_n = nI_{n-2},\quad I_0 = 1,\quad \text{find } I_4\;$
$\;I_0=1,\; I_2=2I_0=2,\; I_4=4I_2=8\;$
1qrecursive evaluation
Set up arc-length or surface-area integral via dy/dx substitution
$\;y = \dfrac{x^2}{4} - \dfrac{\ln x}{2},\quad \dfrac{dy}{dx} = \dfrac{x}{2} - \dfrac{1}{2x}\;$
$\;1 + \left(\dfrac{dy}{dx}\right)^{\!2} = 1 + \dfrac{x^2}{4} - \dfrac{1}{2} + \dfrac{1}{4x^2} = \left(\dfrac{x}{2}+\dfrac{1}{2x}\right)^{\!2} \Rightarrow L = \int_1^2 \!\left(\dfrac{x}{2}+\dfrac{1}{2x}\right)dx\;$
1qgeometric integral setup
Convert roots between Cartesian and polar forms as the question demands
$\;z = 2\left(\cos\dfrac{2\pi}{3} + i\sin\dfrac{2\pi}{3}\right)\;$
$\;z = 2\left(-\dfrac{1}{2} + \dfrac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\,i\right) = -1 + \sqrt{3}\,i\;$
1qpolar conversion
Rationalise a complex constant ratio by conjugate multiplication
$\;\dfrac{1+i}{2-i}\;$
$\;\dfrac{1+i}{2-i}\cdot\dfrac{2+i}{2+i} = \dfrac{1+3i}{5}\;$
1qrationalisation
Realise complex denominator by multiplying by its conjugate
$\;\dfrac{1+i}{2+i}\;$
$\;\dfrac{(1+i)(2-i)}{(2+i)(2-i)} = \dfrac{3+i}{5}\;$
1qrationalisation
Plot nth roots as vertices of a regular polygon on a circle
$\;z^3 = 8\;$
$\;|z|=2,\quad z_k = 2\operatorname{cis}\!\left(\dfrac{2k\pi}{3}\right),\ k=0,1,2 \quad\text{(equilateral triangle on }|z|=2\text{)}\;$
1qgeometric interpretation
Recognise real-scalar multiple of a fixed complex number as a line through the origin
$\;w = t(1+2i),\quad t \in \mathbb{R}\;$
$\;u = t,\ v = 2t \Rightarrow v = 2u\;$
1qgeometric interpretation
Identify nth roots as vertices of a regular n-gon on circle of radius r^{1/n}
$\;z^3 = 8\;$
$\;z_k = 2e^{i \cdot 2\pi k/3},\ k=0,1,2 \Rightarrow \text{equilateral triangle on } |z|=2\;$
1qgeometric interpretation
Read |w - a| = |w - b| as the perpendicular bisector of segment ab
$\;|w - 1| = |w - 3|\;$
$\;\text{Perp.\ bisector of } [1,3] \Rightarrow \operatorname{Re}(w) = 2\;$
1qgeometric interpretation
Extract purely imaginary roots from x² = −k
$\;x^2 + 4 = 0\;$
$\;x^2 = -4 = (2i)^2 \Rightarrow x = \pm 2i\;$
1qde moivre root extraction
Apply zero-product property to a pre-factored polynomial
$\;(x^2+1)(x^2+4)=0\;$
$\;x^2+1=0 \Rightarrow x=\pm i;\quad x^2+4=0 \Rightarrow x=\pm 2i\;$
1qde moivre root extraction
Use |z|² = Re(z)² + Im(z)² to solve for an unknown real parameter
$\;z = \lambda + 2i,\quad |z| = \sqrt{5},\quad \lambda > 0\;$
$\;\lambda^2 + 2^2 = 5 \Rightarrow \lambda^2 = 1 \Rightarrow \lambda = 1\;$
1qmodulus equation
Reflect z in the real axis to locate its conjugate on an Argand diagram
$\;z = 3 + 2i \quad \Rightarrow \quad A(3,\,2)\;$
$\;z^* = 3 - 2i \quad \Rightarrow \quad B(3,\,-2)\;$
1qconjugate geometry
Build real quadratic factor from conjugate pair using sum and product
$\;\alpha = 1 + 2i,\quad \bar{\alpha} = 1 - 2i\;$
$\;S = 2,\; P = 1^2 + 2^2 = 5 \Rightarrow z^2 - 2z + 5\;$
1qfactor from roots
Compute argument from Cartesian form using sign-based quadrant check
$\;z = -1 + i\;$
$\;\text{Q2: } \arg z = \arctan\!\left(\tfrac{1}{-1}\right) + \pi = -\tfrac{\pi}{4} + \pi = \tfrac{3\pi}{4}\;$
1qquadrant aware arctan
Expand complex square by FOIL then substitute i² = −1
$\;(2+i)^2\;$
$\;4 + 2i + 2i + i^2 = 4 + 4i - 1 = 3 + 4i\;$
1qidentity substitution
Use conjugate-pair vertical symmetry to compute Argand triangle area
$\;z = 1,\; 3+2i,\; 3-2i \text{ plotted on Argand diagram}\;$
$\;\text{Area} = |b|\,|a - x_3| = 2 \times |3-1| = 4\;$
1qargand geometry
Invoke Conjugate Root Theorem to obtain second root for free
$\;z^3 - 4z^2 + 6z - 4 = 0,\quad z_1 = 1+i\;$
$\;\text{coeffs} \in \mathbb{R} \Rightarrow z_2 = \overline{1+i} = 1-i\;$
1qtheorem invocation
Check quadrant to select correct principal argument
$\;z = -1 + i\;$
$\;\alpha = \arctan\tfrac{1}{1} = \tfrac{\pi}{4},\quad \text{Q2} \Rightarrow \arg(z) = \pi - \tfrac{\pi}{4} = \tfrac{3\pi}{4}\;$
1qquadrant validation
Evaluate discriminant sign to classify root type at specific parameter value
$\;x = 3 \pm \sqrt{4 - d},\quad d = 7\;$
$\;4 - 7 = -3 < 0 \Rightarrow x = 3 \pm i\sqrt{3}\;$
1qdiscriminant classification
Recognise conjugate pair product to collapse to a real number
$\;(3-2i)(3+2i)\;$
$\;3^2 - (2i)^2 = 9 - (-4) = 13\;$
1qstructural recognition
Apply quadratic formula keeping parametric discriminant unsimplified
$\;x^2 - 6x + k^2 = 0\;$
$\;x = \dfrac{6 \pm \sqrt{36 - 4k^2}}{2} = 3 \pm \sqrt{9 - k^2}\;$
1qparametric discriminant analysis
Identify quadrant before applying arctan for principal argument
$\;z = -1 + i\;$
$\;x<0,\; y>0\ (\text{Q2}): \arg(z) = \arctan\!\left(\tfrac{1}{-1}\right) + \pi = -\tfrac{\pi}{4} + \pi = \tfrac{3\pi}{4}\;$
1qquadrant analysis
Square both sides of a modulus equation to clear the surd
$\;z = 2 + i,\quad |z| = \sqrt{5}\;$
$\;|z|^2 = 2^2 + 1^2 = 5 = (\sqrt{5})^2\;$
1qequation reduction
Write every root in explicit a + ib form, including zeros
$\;z^2 - 2z + 5 = 0 \Rightarrow z = 1 \pm 2i\;$
$\;z = 1 + 2i,\quad 1 - 2i\;$
1qcanonical form compliance
Expand Cartesian complex product and substitute i² = −1
$\;(1+2i)(3+i)\;$
$\;3 + i + 6i + 2i^2 = 3 + 7i - 2 = 1 + 7i\;$
1qcomplex arithmetic
Plot real root on real axis and conjugate pair symmetrically on Argand diagram
$\;z^3 - z^2 + z - 1 = 0 \Rightarrow z_1 = 1,\; z_2 = i,\; z_3 = -i\;$
$\;\text{Plot } (1,\,0),\; (0,\,1),\; (0,\,-1) \text{ on Re/Im axes — conjugate pair symmetric about Re-axis}\;$
1qargand representation
Compute modulus as Euclidean distance from origin
$\;z = 3 + 4i\;$
$\;|z| = \sqrt{3^2 + 4^2} = \sqrt{25} = 5\;$
1qmodulus computation
Plot complex roots on Argand diagram using Re-Im coordinates
$\;z^2 + 4 = 0 \Rightarrow z = 2i,\ -2i\;$
$\;(0,\,2) \text{ labelled } 2i,\quad (0,\,-2) \text{ labelled } {-2i}\;$
1qargand diagram plotting
Use Vieta's formulas to recover unknown coefficients from known roots
$\;z^3 + az^2 + bz + 10 = 0,\quad z_1 = 1-2i,\; z_2 = 1+2i\;$
$\;z_1 z_2 z_3 = 5z_3 = -10 \Rightarrow z_3 = -2,\quad a = -(2+(-2))=0,\quad b = 5+(-2)(1\!-\!2i)+(-2)(1\!+\!2i)=1\;$
1qroot coefficient relations
Collapse conjugate pair product to a²+b² via difference of squares
$\;(3-2i)(3+2i)\;$
$\;3^2 + 2^2 = 13\;$
1qconjugate product identity
Use product-of-roots first to isolate the unknown third root
$\;z^3 + az^2 + bz - 10 = 0,\quad z_1 = 1-2i,\; z_2 = 1+2i\;$
$\;z_1 z_2 = 5,\quad 5\,z_3 = 10 \Rightarrow z_3 = 2\;$
1qstrategic sequencing
Encode invariant point by setting w = z in the Möbius equation
$\;w = \dfrac{az + b}{z + d},\quad z_0 \text{ invariant}\;$
$\;z_0 = \dfrac{az_0 + b}{z_0 + d} \Rightarrow z_0^2 + dz_0 = az_0 + b \Rightarrow z_0^2 + (d-a)z_0 - b = 0\;$
1qdefinition encoding
Factor i from numerator and denominator to cancel
$\;\dfrac{2i + 3i}{4i + i}\;$
$\;\dfrac{i(2+3)}{i(4+1)} = \dfrac{5}{5} = 1\;$
1qcommon factor extraction
Rearrange equation to recycle part (a) polar form
$\;\text{(a)}\ 1+i = \sqrt{2}\,e^{i\pi/4}.\quad \text{(b)}\ z^2 + 1 + i = 0\;$
$\;z^2 = -(1+i) = \sqrt{2}\,e^{-i3\pi/4} \Rightarrow z = 2^{1/4}\,e^{i(-3\pi/4 + 2k\pi)/2},\ k=0,1\;$
1qcross part linkage
Equate real and imaginary parts to solve for a real parameter
$\;(2+i)p + 3i = 4 + 5i,\quad p \in \mathbb{R}\;$
$\;\text{Re: } 2p = 4,\quad \text{Im: } p+3 = 5 \Rightarrow p = 2\;$
1qreal imaginary separation
Apply de Moivre to compress (cosθ+isinθ)^n into cos(nθ)+isin(nθ)
$\;z = \cos\theta + i\sin\theta,\quad z^3 = (\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)^3\;$
$\;(\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)^3 = \cos 3\theta + i\sin 3\theta\;$
1qde moivre application
Expand (cosθ + i sinθ)^n by the binomial theorem to extract real and imaginary parts
$\;(\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)^3\;$
$\;\cos^3\theta + 3i\cos^2\theta\sin\theta - 3\cos\theta\sin^2\theta - i\sin^3\theta = (\cos^3\theta - 3\cos\theta\sin^2\theta) + i(3\cos^2\theta\sin\theta - \sin^3\theta)\;$
1qbinomial complex expansion
Shift k-index to keep nth-root arguments in principal range
$\;z^3 = \operatorname{cis}(-\tfrac{4\pi}{3}),\quad z_k = \operatorname{cis}\!\left(\tfrac{-\tfrac{4\pi}{3} + 2\pi k}{3}\right),\; k\in\{0,1,2\}\;$
$\;k=2:\; \tfrac{-\frac{4\pi}{3}+4\pi}{3} = \tfrac{8\pi}{9}>\pi,\;\text{replace } k=2\to k=-1:\; \tfrac{-\frac{4\pi}{3}-2\pi}{3} = -\tfrac{10\pi}{9}\Rightarrow k\in\{0,1,-1\},\; \text{args}\;\in(-\pi,\pi]\;$
1qprincipal value selection
Exploit conjugate-pair symmetry to halve root-finding work
$\;z^3 - 3z^2 + 4z - 12 = 0,\quad z = 2i \text{ is a root}\;$
$\;z = -2i \Rightarrow (z^2+4)(z-3)=0 \Rightarrow z = \pm 2i,\, 3\;$
1qsymmetry exploitation
Split modulus of a quotient to get an equation in the new variable
$\;z = \dfrac{w+1}{w-1},\quad |z| = 1\;$
$\;\dfrac{|w+1|}{|w-1|} = 1 \Rightarrow |w+1| = |w-1|\;$
1qmodulus transfer
Set z = e^{iθ} to convert cosθ into the symmetric sum z + z^{-1}
$\;z = e^{i\theta},\quad (2\cos\theta)^2 = (z+z^{-1})^2\;$
$\;z^2 + 2 + z^{-2} = 2\cos 2\theta + 2 \Rightarrow \cos^2\theta = \tfrac{1}{2}\cos 2\theta + \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qexponential parametrisation
Enumerate nth roots via (φ + 2kπ)/n argument shifts
$\;z^3 = 8i = 8\operatorname{cis}\!\left(\tfrac{\pi}{2}\right)\;$
$\;z_k = 2\operatorname{cis}\!\left(\dfrac{\frac{\pi}{2}+2k\pi}{3}\right),\; k=0,1,2 \Rightarrow z = 2\operatorname{cis}\tfrac{\pi}{6},\; 2\operatorname{cis}\tfrac{5\pi}{6},\; 2\operatorname{cis}\!\left(-\tfrac{\pi}{2}\right)\;$
1qroots of unity
Substitute w=u+iv and square moduli to extract Cartesian locus
$\;|w - 2| = |w + 2i|,\quad w = u + iv\;$
$\;(u-2)^2 + v^2 = u^2 + (v+2)^2 \Rightarrow -4u = 4v \Rightarrow v = -u\;$
1qcartesian decomposition
Test a convenient point to identify the correct inequality region
$\;|z - 2| \le |z + 2|}\;$
$\;z_0 = 0:\; |0-2| = 2,\; |0+2| = 2,\; 2 \le 2 \;\checkmark \Rightarrow \text{shade side containing } 0\;$
1qpoint testing
Equate real or imaginary parts of two complex representations
$\;(\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)^3 = \cos^3\theta + 3i\cos^2\theta\sin\theta - 3\cos\theta\sin^2\theta - i\sin^3\theta = \cos 3\theta + i\sin 3\theta\;$
$\;\text{Equate real parts: } \cos 3\theta = \cos^3\theta - 3\cos\theta\sin^2\theta\;$
1qequating parts
Convert complex number to exponential form before extracting nth roots

1qexponential form conversion
Insert +2kπ before taking the nth root to capture all roots
$\;z^3 = 8\;$

1qmulti valued argument
Choose k-values so all nth-root arguments fall in the required range
$\;z^3 = 8,\quad -\pi < \arg z \le \pi\;$
$\;\theta = \tfrac{0 + 2k\pi}{3}:\quad k=-1,0,1 \Rightarrow \theta = -\tfrac{2\pi}{3},\, 0,\, \tfrac{2\pi}{3}\;$
1qrange selection
Expand (cos θ + i sin θ)^n binomially to extract multiple-angle identities
$\;(\cos\theta + i\sin\theta)^3\;$

1qde moivre expansion
Reduce substituted modulus equation to Cartesian circle or line
$\;|2w - 1| = |w + 1|,\quad w = u + iv\;$
$\;(2u-1)^2 + 4v^2 = (u+1)^2 + v^2 \Rightarrow (u-1)^2 + v^2 = 1\;$
1qmodulus to cartesian
Use Vieta to conclude sum of nth roots equals zero
$\;z^4 - 16 = 0,\quad z_k = 2\,\mathrm{cis}\!\left(\tfrac{\pi k}{2}\right),\ k=0,1,2,3\;$
$\;\text{coeff of } z^3 = 0 \;\Rightarrow\; \sum_{k=0}^{3} z_k = -\frac{0}{1} = 0\;$
1qvieta polynomial root link
Use test points on locus and inside region to verify image and fix shading
$\;|z|=1,\quad w=\dfrac{1}{z+2}\;$
$\;z=1\Rightarrow w=\tfrac{1}{3};\quad z=0\ (\text{inside } |z|<1)\Rightarrow w_0=\tfrac{1}{2},\quad w_0\ \text{outside image} \Rightarrow \text{shade opposite side}\;$
1qtest point method
Convert polar roots to exact Cartesian form using standard-angle trig values
$\;z = 2\,\text{cis}\!\left(\dfrac{\pi}{3}\right)\;$

1qpolar to cartesian
Add 2kπ to argument before dividing by n to generate all nth roots
