$\;P = 2r + r\theta = 5(2 + 0.8) = 14\;$
1qgeometric decomposition
Map partial-period remainder back to a reference interval via periodicity
$\;\sin x = 0 \text{ on } (0,\, 5\pi],\quad T = 2\pi,\; \text{base solutions } x' \in \{\pi,\, 2\pi\}\;$
$\;5\pi = 2(2\pi) + \pi \Rightarrow 2 \text{ full periods} \times 2 + \bigl|\{\pi\} \subset (0,\pi]\bigr| = 4 + 1 = 5\;$
1qperiodic reduction
Sketch tan curve using asymptotes and zeros as structural anchors
$\;y = \tan\theta,\quad 0° \le \theta \le 360°\;$
$\;\text{Asymptotes: } \theta=90°,\,270° \quad\text{Zeros: } 0°,\,180°,\,360° \quad\text{Period }180°,\ \text{3 rising branches between anchors}\;$
1qstandard curve recall
Apply s = rθ for arc length using stored exact radian angle
$\;r = 5,\quad \theta = \dfrac{\pi}{3}\;$
$\;s = r\theta = 5 \times \dfrac{\pi}{3} = \dfrac{5\pi}{3}\;$
1qradian formula application
Drop perpendicular from circle point to form right triangle for central angle
$\;\text{Circle centre }O,\ r=2,\quad M\text{ foot of perp from }B\text{ to }OA,\quad OM=1\;$
$\;\cos(\angle AOB)=\dfrac{OM}{OB}=\dfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow \angle AOB=\dfrac{\pi}{3}\;$
1qright triangle construction
Scale per-cycle solution count by LCM-period repetitions over extended domain
$\;\sin\theta = \cos 2\theta \text{ has } 3 \text{ solutions in } [0°,\,360°]\;$
$\;\text{LCM}(360°,180°)=360°,\quad \dfrac{1080°}{360°}=3 \Rightarrow 3\times 3=9 \text{ solutions}\;$
1qperiodicity scaling
Take 2π minus the interior angle to get the major sector angle
$\;\theta = \dfrac{\pi}{3},\quad r = 4\;$
$\;\alpha = 2\pi - \dfrac{\pi}{3} = \dfrac{5\pi}{3},\quad A = \tfrac{1}{2}(4)^2\!\left(\dfrac{5\pi}{3}\right) = \dfrac{40\pi}{3}\;$
1qreflex angle complement
Invert transformed cosine argument to locate critical point
$\;y = \cos(2x^\circ),\quad 0 \le x \le 180\;$
$\;\cos\theta = -1 \Rightarrow 2x = 180 \Rightarrow x = 90,\quad \text{min } (90,\,-1)\;$
1qargument inversion
Bound the unknown reference angle to rank candidate solution magnitudes
$\;\cos\theta = k,\; \alpha \text{ smallest positive root, candidates } \alpha - 4\pi,\; -2\pi - \alpha\;$
$\;\alpha < 2\pi - \alpha \Rightarrow \alpha < \pi \Rightarrow |\alpha - 4\pi| - |{-2\pi - \alpha}| = 2\pi - 2\alpha > 0 \Rightarrow |-2\pi - \alpha| < |\alpha - 4\pi|\;$
1qconstraint reasoning
Chain modulus then vertical shift to update range incrementally
$\;f(x) \in [-3,\,3],\quad g(x) = |f(x)| + 2\;$
$\;|f(x)| \in [0,\,3] \Rightarrow g(x) \in [2,\,5]\;$
1qtransformation chaining
Take both ± square roots when extracting from a squared trig equation
$\;\sin^2 x = \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
$\;\sin x = \pm\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \Rightarrow x = 45°,\,135°,\,225°,\,315°\;$
1qsign bifurcation
Use kite symmetry axis to halve the vertex angle
$\;\text{Kite } OABC,\; OA=OC=1,\; AB=CB=2,\; \angle AOC=\theta\;$
$\;\angle AOB = \tfrac{\theta}{2},\; \cos\tfrac{\theta}{2} = \frac{1^2+OB^2-2^2}{2(1)(OB)} \Rightarrow \theta = 2\angle AOB\;$
1qsymmetry reduction
Cancel cos x as a common factor with explicit non-zero justification
$\;2\tan x \sin 2x = 3\;$
$\;2\cdot\dfrac{\sin x}{\cos x}\cdot 2\sin x\cos x = 3,\quad \cos x\neq 0 \Rightarrow 4\sin^2 x = 3\;$
1qguarded cancellation
Plot quarter-period key points to sketch transformed trig on restricted domain
$\;y = \sin(2x^\circ),\quad 0 \le x \le 270\;$
$\;T = 180,\; T/4 = 45:\quad (0,0),\,(45,1),\,(90,0),\,(135,-1),\,(180,0),\,(225,1),\,(270,0)\;$
1qcurve sketching
Apply the Sine Rule to extract a target angle once a complete side–angle pair exists
$\;\triangle ABC:\quad A=30^\circ,\; a=4,\; b=3,\; B=?\;$
$\;\dfrac{\sin B}{3}=\dfrac{\sin 30^\circ}{4} \Rightarrow \sin B=\dfrac{3}{8} \Rightarrow B=\arcsin\!\tfrac{3}{8}\;$
1qsine rule angle
Solve quadratic in cosθ and reject out-of-range root
$\;2\cos^2\theta - 3\cos\theta - 2 = 0\;$
$\;\cos\theta = \dfrac{3 \pm 5}{4} = 2\ (\text{reject: } |u|>1)\ \text{or}\ -\tfrac{1}{2}\ (\text{accept})\;$
1qvalidity filtering
Sweep a horizontal line across critical y-values to count intersections
$\;y = \sin x,\quad 0 \le x \le 2\pi,\quad y = k\;$
$\;k=1{:}\,1,\quad k\in(0,1){:}\,2,\quad k=0{:}\,3,\quad k\in(-1,0){:}\,2,\quad k=-1{:}\,1\;$
1qgraphical solution counting
Shift domain bounds to match compound-angle substitution
$\;\sin(\theta + 30°) = \tfrac{1}{2},\quad 0° \le \theta < 360°\;$
$\;X = \theta + 30° \Rightarrow 30° \le X < 390°\;$
1qrange transformation
Read max/min and its location directly from R cos(x+α) form
$\;3\cos x + 4\sin x = 5\cos(x - 53.13°)\;$
$\;\max = 5 \text{ at } x = 53.1°,\quad \min = -5 \text{ at } x = 233.1°\;$
1qamplitude phase extraction
Verify solutions against original denominators after cross-multiplying
$\;\tan\theta = \dfrac{1}{2\sin\theta - 1},\quad \theta = \tfrac{\pi}{6} \text{ candidate}\;$
$\;2\sin\tfrac{\pi}{6} - 1 = 2\!\cdot\!\tfrac{1}{2} - 1 = 0 \Rightarrow \text{reject } \theta = \tfrac{\pi}{6}\;$
1qvalidity checking
Bound a linear-in-sine expression using sine's range
$\;3 + 5\sin x\;$
$\;-1 \le \sin x \le 1 \Rightarrow 3 + 5(-1) \le 3 + 5\sin x \le 3 + 5(1) \Rightarrow -2 \le 3+5\sin x \le 8\;$
1qrange bounding
Factor out sin x to split zero and reduced-equation cases
$\;2\sin x \cos x - \sin x = 0\;$
$\;\sin x\,(2\cos x - 1) = 0 \Rightarrow \sin x = 0 \text{ or } \cos x = \tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qcase splitting
Reduce trig argument mod 2π then apply reference-angle and quadrant sign
$\;\sin\!\left(-\dfrac{17\pi}{6}\right)\;$
$\;-\dfrac{17\pi}{6} + \dfrac{24\pi}{6} = \dfrac{7\pi}{6}\;\Rightarrow\;\sin\!\left(\dfrac{7\pi}{6}\right) = -\sin\dfrac{\pi}{6} = -\dfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qangle reduction
Translate the θ-range to match a compound trig argument
$\;\tan(\theta + 30^\circ) = 1,\quad 0^\circ < \theta < 360^\circ\;$
$\;u = \theta+30^\circ,\; 30^\circ<u<390^\circ \Rightarrow u = 45^\circ,\,225^\circ \Rightarrow \theta = 15^\circ,\,195^\circ\;$
1qrange adjustment
Apply arctan to both sides to isolate the angle variable
$\;\tan\!\left(\dfrac{x}{2}\right) = 3,\quad x \in (0,\pi)\;$
$\;\dfrac{x}{2} = \arctan 3 \Rightarrow x = 2\arctan 3\;$
1qinverse function isolation
Resolve square-root sign ambiguity using the range of arcsin
$\;y = \arcsin x,\quad \cos^2 y = 1 - x^2\;$
$\;-\tfrac{\pi}{2} \le y \le \tfrac{\pi}{2} \Rightarrow \cos y \ge 0 \Rightarrow \cos y = +\sqrt{1-x^2}\;$
1qdomain restriction
Map x-bounds to inner-variable bounds before solving compound trig equation
$\;\tan(2x) = 1,\quad 0 < x < \pi\;$
$\;\theta = 2x,\; 0 < \theta < 2\pi \Rightarrow \theta = \tfrac{\pi}{4},\;\tfrac{5\pi}{4} \Rightarrow x = \tfrac{\pi}{8},\;\tfrac{5\pi}{8}\;$
1qdomain mapping
Reject trig roots violating range bounds (|cos|, |sin| ≤ 1; |sec|, |csc| ≥ 1)
$\;2\cos^2\theta - 3\cos\theta + 1 = 0\;$
$\;\cos\theta = 1 \text{ or } \cos\theta = \tfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow \text{both satisfy } |\cos\theta| \le 1, \text{ so both retained}\;$
1qdomain validation
Resolve square-root sign ambiguity using the stated domain
$\;\sin^2 y = \tfrac{1}{2}(1-x),\quad 0 \le y \le \pi\;$
$\;\sqrt{\sin^2 y} = |\sin y|,\ 0 \le y \le \pi \Rightarrow \sin y \ge 0 \Rightarrow \sin y = +\sqrt{\tfrac{1}{2}(1-x)}\;$
1qsign determination
Discard cos/sin roots outside [−1,1] before inverting
$\;2\cos^2 x + 3\cos x - 2 = 0\;$
$\;\cos x = \tfrac{-3 \pm 5}{4} \Rightarrow \cos x = \tfrac{1}{2}\ (\text{keep}),\quad \cos x = -2\ (\text{reject: } |{-2}|>1)\;$
1qrange filtering
Decompose R-form expression into ordered stretch and translation
$\;y = \cos\theta \;\to\; y = 2\cos\!\left(\theta + \tfrac{\pi}{3}\right)\;$
$\;\text{(i)}\; y=2\cos\theta \;[\text{stretch }\parallel y,\; \times2], \quad \text{(ii)}\; y=2\cos\!\left(\theta+\tfrac{\pi}{3}\right) \;\left[\text{translation } \begin{pmatrix}-\pi/3\\0\end{pmatrix}\right]\;$
1qtransformation decomposition
Convert a·cosθ + b·sinθ to R-form by expanding and matching coefficients
$\;3\cos\theta + 4\sin\theta = R\cos(\theta - \alpha)\;$
$\;R\cos\alpha = 3,\; R\sin\alpha = 4 \Rightarrow R = \sqrt{9+16} = 5,\; \alpha = \arctan\tfrac{4}{3}\;$
1qharmonic form conversion
Combine trig fractions over a common denominator to expose a compound-angle identity
$\;\dfrac{\cos x}{\sin x} - \dfrac{\sin x}{\cos x}\;$
$\;\dfrac{\cos^2 x - \sin^2 x}{\sin x \cos x} = \dfrac{\cos 2x}{\tfrac{1}{2}\sin 2x} = \dfrac{2\cos 2x}{\sin 2x}\;$
1qfraction combination
Square-and-add then divide to decouple R and α
$\;R\cos\alpha = 3,\quad R\sin\alpha = 4,\quad R>0\;$
$\;R^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 = 25 \Rightarrow R = 5,\quad \tan\alpha = \tfrac{4}{3} \Rightarrow \alpha = \arctan\tfrac{4}{3}\;$
1qpythagorean ratio decoupling
Read off max/min from p + q·cos(·) using bounded range
$\;f(x) = 4 + 3\cos(x - \alpha)\;$
$\;-1 \le \cos(x-\alpha) \le 1 \Rightarrow f_{\min} = 4 - 3 = 1,\quad f_{\max} = 4 + 3 = 7\;$
1qrange of trig function
Reduce perfect-square trig equation to its base equals zero
$\;(1 + 2\cos x)^2 = 0\;$
$\;1 + 2\cos x = 0 \Rightarrow \cos x = -\tfrac{1}{2}\;$
1qstructural reduction
Rewrite sec x as 1/cos x to reduce to a primary trig equation
$\;\sec x = 2\;$
$\;\frac{1}{\cos x} = 2 \Rightarrow \cos x = \frac{1}{2}\;$
1qreciprocal rewrite
Scale the interval for the multiple angle and enumerate every branch
$\;\sin 2\theta = \tfrac{1}{2},\quad \theta \in (0,2\pi)\;$
$\;\varphi = 2\theta \in (0,4\pi):\quad \varphi = \tfrac{\pi}{6},\ \tfrac{5\pi}{6},\ \tfrac{13\pi}{6},\ \tfrac{17\pi}{6} \Rightarrow \theta = \tfrac{\pi}{12},\ \tfrac{5\pi}{12},\ \tfrac{13\pi}{12},\ \tfrac{17\pi}{12}\;$
1qmultiple angle interval
Multiply through by cos θ to clear sec θ and form sin 2θ
$\;2\sin\theta = 3\sec\theta\;$
$\;2\sin\theta\cos\theta = 3 \Rightarrow \sin 2\theta = 3\;$
1qstrategic multiplication
Translate the domain bounds when substituting y = x − α
$\;\sin(x - 30°) = \tfrac{1}{2},\quad 0° \le x < 360°\;$
$\;y = x - 30° \Rightarrow -30° \le y < 330°,\quad y = 30°,\,150° \Rightarrow x = 60°,\,180°\;$
1qdomain translation
Split a sum to extract the denominator factor and cancel
$\;\dfrac{\sin 3\theta - \cos 3\theta}{\sin\theta - \cos\theta}\;$
$\;\frac{(\sin\theta - \cos\theta)(\sin 2\theta + \cos 2\theta) + 2\sin 2\theta\cos\theta}{\sin\theta - \cos\theta} = \sin 2\theta + \cos 2\theta + \frac{\sin 3\theta + \sin\theta}{\sin\theta - \cos\theta} \Rightarrow 2 + \sin 2\theta\;$
1qstrategic factorisation
Apply amplitude bound a²+b²≥c² to extract range of trig-rational expression
$\;y = \dfrac{3 + \sin x}{2 + \cos x}\;$
$\;\sin x - y\cos x = 2y - 3 \Rightarrow (2y-3)^2 \le 1 + y^2 \Rightarrow 3y^2 - 12y + 8 \le 0\;$
1qrange from bound
Multiply by x then divide by cos x to expose tan x in target form
$\;\cos x\,\ln x + \dfrac{\sin x}{x} = 0\;$
$\;\xrightarrow{\times\, x} x\cos x\,\ln x + \sin x = 0 \xrightarrow{\div\,\cos x} x\ln x + \tan x = 0\;$
1qtarget driven rearrangement
Generate the supplementary second solution for sin(φ) = k
$\;\sin\theta = 0.5,\quad 0°\le\theta<360°\;$
$\;\theta_1 = 30° \Rightarrow \theta_2 = 180° - 30° = 150°\;$
1qcast symmetry
Translate the domain when substituting a phase-shifted argument
$\;\sin(\theta - 30°) = \tfrac{1}{2},\quad 0° \le \theta < 360°\;$
$\;\varphi = \theta - 30°,\; -30° \le \varphi < 330°:\quad \varphi = 30°,\,150° \Rightarrow \theta = 60°,\,180°\;$
1qdomain shifting
Cross-multiply and reduce trig equation to quadratic in sinθ
$\;\dfrac{\sin\theta}{2} = 1 - 2\sin\theta - 4\sin^2\theta\;$
$\;\sin\theta = 2 - 4\sin\theta - 8\sin^2\theta \;\Rightarrow\; 8\sin^2\theta + 5\sin\theta - 2 = 0\;$
1qalgebraic reduction
Verify numerator divides denominator by expanding the conjectured factorisation
$\;\dfrac{\cos\theta + \sin\theta}{\cos 2\theta + \sin\theta}\;$
$\;(\cos\theta + \sin\theta)(1 - \sin\theta) = \cos\theta - \cos\theta\sin\theta + \sin\theta - \sin^2\theta = (1-2\sin^2\theta) + \sin\theta = \cos 2\theta + \sin\theta \;\checkmark\;$
1qcancellation factorisation
Bridge sin²φ to tan φ via Pythagorean quotient
$\;\sin^2\varphi = \tfrac{1}{4},\quad 0 < \varphi < \tfrac{\pi}{2}\;$
$\;\tan^2\varphi = \dfrac{1/4}{3/4} = \tfrac{1}{3} \Rightarrow \tan\varphi = \dfrac{\sqrt{3}}{3}\;$
1qratio bridge
Evaluate sin(arccos k) using Pythagorean identity
$\;\sin\!\left(\arccos \tfrac{3}{5}\right)\;$
$\;\sin\theta = \sqrt{1 - \cos^2\theta} = \sqrt{1 - \tfrac{9}{25}} = \tfrac{4}{5}\;$
1qinverse trig evaluation
Cascade double-angle identities from known sin²φ to evaluate sin 4φ exactly
$\;\sin^2\!\phi = \tfrac{1}{3},\quad \phi \text{ acute}\;$
$\;\sin 4\phi = 2\sin 2\phi\cos 2\phi = 2\!\cdot\!\tfrac{2\sqrt{2}}{3}\!\cdot\!\tfrac{1}{3} = \tfrac{4\sqrt{2}}{9}\;$
1qexact evaluation cascade
Pre-compute exact trig values once before substituting into Taylor coefficients
$\;f(x)=\tan x,\quad a=\tfrac{\pi}{3}\;$
$\;\sin\tfrac{\pi}{3}=\tfrac{\sqrt{3}}{2},\ \cos\tfrac{\pi}{3}=\tfrac{1}{2},\ \sec^2\!\tfrac{\pi}{3}=4 \Rightarrow f(a)=\sqrt{3},\; f'(a)=4,\; f(x)\approx \sqrt{3}+4\!\left(x-\tfrac{\pi}{3}\right)\;$
1qevaluate then substitute
Apply half-angle identities to collapse (1 ± cos θ) denominators
$\;\dfrac{\sin\theta}{1+\cos\theta}\;$
$\;\dfrac{2\sin(\theta/2)\cos(\theta/2)}{2\cos^2(\theta/2)} = \tan(\theta/2)\;$
1qhalf angle substitution
Reverse-read a power-linearisation identity to collapse a multi-angle equation into a polynomial in cosθ
$\;\cos 6\theta + 6\cos 4\theta + 15\cos 2\theta = 0,\quad 32\cos^6\theta = \cos 6\theta + 6\cos 4\theta + 15\cos 2\theta + 10\;$
$\;32\cos^6\theta - 10 = 0 \Rightarrow \cos^6\theta = \tfrac{5}{16} \Rightarrow \cos\theta = \pm\!\left(\tfrac{5}{16}\right)^{1/6}\;$
1qidentity reverse substitution
Use half the cross product magnitude for triangle area in 3D
$\;\overrightarrow{AB} = (1,0,2),\quad \overrightarrow{AC} = (0,1,1)\;$
$\;\overrightarrow{AB} \times \overrightarrow{AC} = (-2,-1,1),\quad \text{Area} = \tfrac{1}{2}\sqrt{4+1+1} = \tfrac{\sqrt{6}}{2}\;$
1qcross product normal
Parametrise symmetric line form to substitute into plane equation
$\;\frac{x-1}{2} = \frac{y-2}{1} = \frac{z}{-1} = t,\quad x+y+z=5\;$
$\;(1+2t)+(2+t)+(0-t)=5 \Rightarrow 2t+3=5 \Rightarrow t=1 \Rightarrow (3,\,3,\,-1)\;$
1qparametric substitution
Take absolute value of normals' dot product for acute dihedral angle
$\;\mathbf{n_1} = (1,0,1),\quad \mathbf{n_2} = (0,1,-1)\;$
$\;\cos\theta = \dfrac{|\mathbf{n_1}\cdot\mathbf{n_2}|}{|\mathbf{n_1}||\mathbf{n_2}|} = \dfrac{|-1|}{\sqrt{2}\cdot\sqrt{2}} = \dfrac{1}{2} \Rightarrow \theta = 60^\circ\;$
1qdot product angle
Build plane parametrically from anchor on contained line plus two spanning directions
$\;l_1: \mathbf{r} = \mathbf{i} + s(2\mathbf{i}+\mathbf{j}),\quad l_2: \mathbf{r} = 3\mathbf{i}+\mathbf{k} + t(\mathbf{i}-\mathbf{j}+\mathbf{k})\;$
$\;\mathbf{r} = (3\mathbf{i}+\mathbf{k}) + s(2\mathbf{i}+\mathbf{j}) + t(\mathbf{i}-\mathbf{j}+\mathbf{k})\;$
1qparametric plane construction
Use ½ab sin C when two sides and included angle are already known
$\;|PA| = 3,\quad |PE| = 2\sqrt{2},\quad \cos(\angle APE) = \tfrac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\;$
$\;\sin(\angle APE) = \tfrac{1}{\sqrt{2}},\quad \text{Area} = \tfrac{1}{2}(3)(2\sqrt{2})\!\left(\tfrac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right) = 3\;$
1qarea formula selection
Normalize a direction vector by dividing by its magnitude
$\;\mathbf{d} = (1,\,2,\,2)\;$
$\;|\mathbf{d}| = \sqrt{1+4+4} = 3,\quad \hat{\mathbf{d}} = \tfrac{1}{3}(1,\,2,\,2)\;$
1qunit vector extraction
Retain both ± roots when solving λ² = k for points on a line
$\;\mathbf{r} = (1,0,0) + \lambda(0,3,4),\quad |\mathbf{r} - (1,0,0)| = 10\;$
$\;25\lambda^2 = 100 \Rightarrow \lambda = \pm 2,\quad \mathbf{r} = (1,6,8) \text{ or } (1,-6,-8)\;$
1qgeometric sign interpretation
Isolate cosθ via division then apply arccos to extract the angle
$\;\cos\theta = \dfrac{\mathbf{a}\cdot\mathbf{b}}{|\mathbf{a}|\,|\mathbf{b}|} = \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{2}\cdot\sqrt{2}} = \dfrac{1}{2}\;$
$\;\theta = \arccos\!\left(\dfrac{1}{2}\right) = 60^{\circ}\;$
1qinverse trig extraction
Reverse one vector so both emanate from the angle's vertex
$\;\vec{AB} = \begin{pmatrix}1\\2\end{pmatrix},\quad \vec{BC} = \begin{pmatrix}3\\1\end{pmatrix},\quad \text{find } \angle ABC\;$
$\;\vec{BA} = -\vec{AB} = \begin{pmatrix}-1\\-2\end{pmatrix},\quad \cos\theta = \dfrac{\vec{BA}\cdot\vec{BC}}{|\vec{BA}|\,|\vec{BC}|} = \dfrac{-5}{\sqrt{5}\cdot\sqrt{10}}\;$
1qdirection alignment
Reuse part (a) angle in |a||b|sinθ for parallelogram area
$\;\lvert \vec{BA} \rvert = 3,\quad \lvert \vec{BC} \rvert = 5,\quad \cos(\angle ABC) = \tfrac{3}{5}\;$
$\;\text{Area} = 3 \cdot 5 \cdot \sin(\angle ABC) = 15\sqrt{1 - \tfrac{9}{25}} = 15 \cdot \tfrac{4}{5} = 12\;$
1qarea via sine product
Substitute given parameter value into line equation to recover a specific point
$\;l:\, \mathbf{r} = (1,2,3) + \lambda(2,1,-1),\quad \lambda = 2\;$
$\;\mathbf{r} = (1,2,3) + 2(2,1,-1) = (5,4,1)\;$
1qparametric evaluation
Exploit right angle at vertex to reduce triangle area to half-product of legs
$\;\triangle OAX,\quad \angle X = 90^\circ,\quad \overrightarrow{OX} = (1,\,2,\,2),\quad |\overrightarrow{XA}| = 3\;$
$\;\text{Area} = \tfrac{1}{2}\,|\overrightarrow{OX}|\,|\overrightarrow{XA}| = \tfrac{1}{2}\cdot 3 \cdot 3 = \tfrac{9}{2}\;$
1qgeometric shortcut via perpendicularity
Compute direction vector as displacement between two given points
$\;A(1,2,3),\quad B(4,6,7)\;$
$\;\mathbf{d} = \mathbf{b}-\mathbf{a} = \begin{pmatrix}3\\4\\4\end{pmatrix},\quad \mathbf{r} = \begin{pmatrix}1\\2\\3\end{pmatrix}+\lambda\begin{pmatrix}3\\4\\4\end{pmatrix}\;$
1qdirection from points
Chain displacement vectors via triangle law to find a position vector
$\;\vec{OA} = \begin{pmatrix} 3 \\ 1 \\ 2 \end{pmatrix},\quad \vec{AB} = \begin{pmatrix} 1 \\ -2 \\ 4 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\vec{OB} = \vec{OA} + \vec{AB} = \begin{pmatrix} 3+1 \\ 1-2 \\ 2+4 \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} 4 \\ -1 \\ 6 \end{pmatrix}\;$
1qvector path chaining
Subtract position vectors to obtain a displacement vector
$\;\vec{OA} = \begin{pmatrix} 1 \\ 3 \end{pmatrix},\quad \vec{OB} = \begin{pmatrix} 4 \\ 1 \end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\vec{AB} = \vec{OB} - \vec{OA} = \begin{pmatrix} 4-1 \\ 1-3 \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} 3 \\ -2 \end{pmatrix}\;$
1qdisplacement from positions
Convert perpendicularity condition into algebraic equation via dot product
$\;\mathbf{u}=(1,\,a,\,2),\quad \mathbf{v}=(3,\,1,\,-1),\quad \mathbf{u}\perp\mathbf{v}\;$
$\;\mathbf{u}\cdot\mathbf{v}= 3 + a - 2 = 0 \Rightarrow a = -1\;$
1qperpendicularity to equation
Find shortest distance as magnitude of foot-of-perpendicular displacement
$\;\overrightarrow{XA} = \bigl(3,\,4,\,0\bigr)\;$
$\;|\overrightarrow{XA}|^2 = 9 + 16 + 0 = 25 \Rightarrow |\overrightarrow{XA}| = 5\;$
1qmagnitude from components
Solve two equations then verify the third to confirm intersection
$\;\mathbf{r}_1 = \begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\2\end{pmatrix}+\lambda\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\\1\end{pmatrix},\quad \mathbf{r}_2 = \begin{pmatrix}0\\1\\1\end{pmatrix}+\mu\begin{pmatrix}2\\1\\3\end{pmatrix} \\[4pt] \text{Equating: }1+\lambda=2\mu,\quad \lambda=1+\mu,\quad 2+\lambda=1+3\mu \\[4pt] \text{From (i) and (ii): } \lambda=3,\; \mu=2\;$
$\;\text{Check (iii): } 2+3=1+3(2) \;\Rightarrow\; 5=7 \;(\text{false}),\; \therefore \text{lines are skew}\;$
1qoverdetermined system check
Invert midpoint relation to reflect a point via its foot of perpendicular
$\;A = (1,\,3),\quad X = (2,\,1)\;$
$\;B = 2X - A = (4,\,2) - (1,\,3) = (3,\,-1)\;$
1qmidpoint reflection
Split skew-lines proof into non-parallel and non-intersecting checks
$\;L_1: \mathbf{r}=(1,0,0)+\lambda(1,1,0),\quad L_2: \mathbf{r}=(0,1,1)+\mu(0,1,1)\;$
$\;(1,1,0)\neq k(0,1,1)\ \text{(not parallel)};\quad 1+\lambda=0,\ \lambda=1+\mu,\ 0=1+\mu \Rightarrow \mu=-1,\ \lambda=0,\ \text{but } 1+0\neq 0\ \text{(no intersection)}\Rightarrow \text{skew}\;$
1qproof by definition
Impose perpendicularity via dot product to locate foot of perpendicular
$\;l:\mathbf{r}=(1,0,0)+\lambda(1,1,0),\quad A=(3,1,2),\quad X=(1+\lambda,\,\lambda,\,0)\;$
$\;\overrightarrow{XA}\cdot\mathbf{d}=(2-\lambda)(1)+(1-\lambda)(1)+(2)(0)=0 \Rightarrow \lambda=\tfrac{3}{2}\;$
1qperpendicularity condition
Solve parameter-free equations first, use third as consistency check
$\;(A)\ \lambda - \mu = 1,\quad (B)\ 2\lambda - b\mu = 3,\quad (C)\ \lambda + \mu = 3\;$
$\;(A)+(C):\; 2\lambda = 4 \Rightarrow \lambda=2,\; \mu=1;\quad (B):\; 4 - b = 3 \Rightarrow b=1\;$
1qstrategic elimination
Parametrise a general point on a line using λ
$\;L:\, \mathbf{r} = (1,0,2) + \lambda(2,1,-1)\;$
$\;P = (1+2\lambda,\; \lambda,\; 2-\lambda)\;$
1qparametric representation
Form displacement vector from fixed point to parametrised point
$\;l:\mathbf{r}=(1,0,2)+\lambda(1,0,-1),\quad A=(3,0,4)\;$
$\;\overrightarrow{AP}=(1+\lambda-3,\,0-0,\,2-\lambda-4)=(\lambda-2,\,0,\,-\lambda-2)\;$
1qvector subtraction for distance
Solve two equations, substitute into the third to expose contradiction
$\;(i)\ \lambda + \mu = 1,\quad (ii)\ 2\lambda - \mu = 3,\quad (iii)\ \lambda + 2\mu = 5\;$
$\;(i),(ii)\Rightarrow \lambda=\tfrac{4}{3},\;\mu=-\tfrac{1}{3};\quad (iii):\ \tfrac{4}{3}+2(-\tfrac{1}{3})=\tfrac{2}{3}\neq 5 \quad\lightning\;$
1qoverdetermined inconsistency
Back-substitute parameter values into line equation to recover position vectors
$\;\mathbf{r} = \begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\2\end{pmatrix} + \lambda\begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\-1\end{pmatrix},\quad \lambda = 3\;$
$\;\mathbf{p} = \begin{pmatrix}1+3\\0\\2-3\end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix}4\\0\\-1\end{pmatrix}\;$
1qparameter to coordinates
Equate vector parametric forms component-wise to test intersection
$\;\mathbf{r}_1 = \begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\-1\end{pmatrix}+\lambda\begin{pmatrix}2\\1\\3\end{pmatrix},\quad \mathbf{r}_2 = \begin{pmatrix}4\\0\\2\end{pmatrix}+\mu\begin{pmatrix}1\\-1\\0\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;1+2\lambda=4+\mu\ \dots(1),\quad \lambda=-\mu\ \dots(2),\quad -1+3\lambda=2\ \dots(3) \Rightarrow \lambda=1,\ \mu=-1;\quad (1): 3=3\ \checkmark \Rightarrow \text{intersection }(3,1,2)\;$
1qparametric elimination
Verify parameters in the unused third equation to confirm intersection
$\;\lambda = 1,\; \mu = -1;\quad \text{check } i\!: \; 1 + 2\lambda \stackrel{?}{=} 4 + \mu\;$
$\;1 + 2(1) = 3,\; 4 + (-1) = 3 \;\Rightarrow\; \text{LHS} = \text{RHS} \;\Rightarrow\; \text{lines intersect}\;$
1qconsistency check
Square magnitude equation to obtain quadratic in parameter
$\;\overrightarrow{AP} = (\lambda - 1,\; \lambda + 2),\quad |\overrightarrow{AP}| = \sqrt{10}\;$
$\;(\lambda-1)^2 + (\lambda+2)^2 = 10 \Rightarrow 2\lambda^2 + 2\lambda + 5 = 10 \Rightarrow 2\lambda^2 + 2\lambda - 5 = 0\;$
1qsquaring to remove root
Divide normal vector by its GCD before plane and distance work
$\;\mathbf{n} = (12, -8, 4)\;$
$\;\gcd(12,8,4)=4,\quad \mathbf{n}' = \tfrac{1}{4}(12,-8,4) = (3,-2,1),\quad |\mathbf{n}'| = \sqrt{14}\;$
1qscalar simplification
Reuse direction vector to build parallel line through new point
$\;l_1:\mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\3\end{pmatrix}+\mu\begin{pmatrix}2\\1\\-1\end{pmatrix},\quad P(0,\,4,\,1)\;$
$\;l_2:\mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}0\\4\\1\end{pmatrix}+t\begin{pmatrix}2\\1\\-1\end{pmatrix}\;$
1qparallel line construction
Split skew-lines proof into non-parallel and non-intersecting checks
$\;L_1: \mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}1\\0\\0\end{pmatrix}+\lambda\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\\0\end{pmatrix},\quad L_2: \mathbf{r}=\begin{pmatrix}0\\0\\1\end{pmatrix}+\mu\begin{pmatrix}0\\1\\1\end{pmatrix}\;$
$\;\tfrac{1}{0}\neq\tfrac{1}{1}\Rightarrow \text{not parallel};\quad \lambda=0,\;\mu=0 \Rightarrow 0\neq1\;\text{(eq.3)}\Rightarrow \text{no intersection}\Rightarrow \text{skew}\;$
1qproof decomposition
Apply perpendicular distance formula from point to plane
$\;P(1,2,2),\quad 2x + y + 2z = 3\;$
$\;d = \dfrac{|2(1)+1(2)+2(2)-3|}{\sqrt{4+1+4}} = \dfrac{5}{3}\;$
1qprojection onto normal
Find triangle area by dropping a perpendicular onto a known line
$\;|\vec{AP}| = 5,\quad \cos\theta = \tfrac{3}{5},\quad PE = 4\;$
$\;h = \sqrt{|\vec{AP}|^2 - (|\vec{AP}|\cos\theta)^2} = \sqrt{25-9} = 4,\quad \text{Area} = \tfrac{1}{2}\cdot 4 \cdot 4 = 8\;$
1qprojection decomposition
Anchor displacement vectors at a common vertex for cross/triple products
$\;A=(0,0,0),\ B=(1,2,0),\ C=(0,1,3),\ D=(2,0,1)\;$
$\;\vec{AB}=(1,2,0),\ \vec{AC}=(0,1,3),\ \vec{AD}=(2,0,1)\;$
1qcommon origin vectors
Encode line-lies-in-plane by setting direction perpendicular to normal
$\;\Pi\colon x + 2y + z = 5,\quad \mathbf{n}=(1,2,1),\quad \mathbf{e}=(a,b,c)\;$
$\;\mathbf{e}\cdot\mathbf{n}=0 \Rightarrow a+2b+c=0 \Rightarrow c=-a-2b \Rightarrow \mathbf{e}=a(1,0,-1)+b(0,1,-2)\;$
1qgeometric constraint encoding
Set one coordinate to zero to find a point on a plane–plane intersection line
$\;\Pi_1: x + y + z = 2,\quad \Pi_2: 2x + y + z = 3\;$
$\;z=0:\; x+y=2,\; 2x+y=3 \Rightarrow x=1,\; y=1 \Rightarrow \mathbf{a}=\begin{pmatrix}1\\1\\0\end{pmatrix}\;$
1qfree parameter specialisation
Reduce homogeneous direction-vector equation to single ratio k = a/b
$\;21(18k+26)^2 = 1400(5k^2+16k+17),\quad k = \tfrac{a}{b}\;$
$\;6804k^2 + 19656k + 14196 = 7000k^2 + 22400k + 23800 \Rightarrow 196k^2 + 2744k + 9604 = 0 \Rightarrow k^2 + 14k + 49 = 0\;$
1qhomogeneous reduction
Rescale normal vector by its GCD to match target plane form
$\;\mathbf{n} = (6,\,2,\,-2),\quad \mathbf{a} = (1,\,2,\,1)\;$
$\;\gcd(6,2,2)=2,\quad \mathbf{n}' = (3,1,-1),\quad d = 3(1)+1(2)-1(1)=4 \Rightarrow 3x+y-z=4\;$
1qscalar equivalence
Substitute a known point into a plane equation to find the missing constant or coordinate
$\;\mathbf{n} = (2,\,1,\,-1),\quad A = (1,\,3,\,2) \text{ on } \Pi:\; 2x + y - z = d\;$
$\;d = 2(1) + 1(3) + (-1)(2) = 3 \Rightarrow \Pi:\; 2x + y - z = 3\;$
1qpoint on plane substitution
No moves match those filters.
